كتاب النكاح فصل في الكفاءة
۲۲۷
محرماً أو لا كما ذكره الولوالجي أنه المختار . وشمل كلامه ما إذا تزوجت غير كفء بغير رضا الولي بعد ما زوجها الولي أولاً منه برضاها وفارقته فللولي التفريق لأن الرضا بالأول لا يكون رضا بالثاني . وشمل ما إذا كانت مجهولة النسب فتزوجت رجلاً ثم ادعاها رجل من قريش وأثبت القاضي نسبها منه وجعلها بنتاً له وزوجها حجام فلهذا الأب أن يفرق بينها وبين زوجها ولو لم يكن ذلك لكن أقرت بالرق لرجل لم يكن لمولاها أن يبطل النكاح بينهما . كذا في الذخيرة وفيها أيضاً لو زوج أمة له صغيرة رجلاً ثم ادعى أنها بنته ثبت لنسب والنكاح على حاله إن كان الزوج كفؤاً وإن لم يكن كفؤاً فهو في القياس لازم، ولو باعها ثم ادعى المشتري أنها بنته فكذلك ا.هـ. وإذا فرق القاضي بينهما فإن كان بعد الدخول فلها المسمى وعليها العدة ولها النفقة فيها والخلوة الصحيحة كالدخول. وإن كان قبلهما فلا مهر لها لأن الفرقة ليست من قبله هكذا في الخانية وهو تفريع على انعقاده، وأما على المفتى به فينبغي أن يجب الأقل من المسمى ومن مهر المثل وأن لا نفقة لها في هذه العدة كما لا يخفى. وفي الخانية : وإن زوجها الولي غير كفء ودخل بها ثم بانت منه بالطلاق ثم زوجت نفسها هذا الزوج بغير ولي ثم فرق القاضي بينهما قبل الدخول كان على الزوج كل المهر الثاني وعليها عدة في المستقبل في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد: لا مهر على الزوج وعليها بقية العدة الأولى، وذكر لها نظائر تأتي في كتاب العدة، وينبغي أن يكون تفريعاً على ظاهر الرواية، أما على المفتي به فإنه لا يجب المهر الثاني بالاتفاق لأنه نكاح فاسد كما صرح به في الخانية فيما إذا كان النكاح الثاني فاسداً. وقيد بالنكاح لأن له المراجعة إذا طلقها رجعياً بعد ما زوجها الولي غير كفء برضاها. كذا في الذخيرة.
The Book of Marriage, Section on Compatibility. 227. Whether it is unlawful or not, as al-Walwaliji mentioned that it is the chosen view. His statement includes the case where a woman marries a non-compatible (non-kuf') person without the guardian's consent after the guardian had first married her (to someone else) with her consent and she separated from that first husband; then the guardian has the right to annul the second marriage because consent to the first does not constitute consent to the second. It also includes the case where a woman of unknown lineage marries a man, then a man from Quraysh claims her as his daughter and the judge establishes her lineage from him and declares her his daughter, while her husband is a cupper (low profession); then this father can separate her from her husband. And if that were not the case, but she confessed to being a slave of a man, then her master cannot invalidate the marriage between them. Thus in al-Dhakhirah. And in it also: If someone married off his slave girl who was a minor to a man, then claimed she is his daughter, then the lineage is established and the marriage remains valid if the husband is compatible; if he is not compatible, then analogically it is binding (but the fatwa position differs). And if he sold her then the buyer claimed she is his daughter, it is similar. [End quote]. And if the judge separates them, if it is after consummation, she gets the dower specified, she must observe the waiting period, she gets maintenance during it, and a valid seclusion is like consummation. If before that, then no dower is due because the separation is not from his side; thus in al-Khaniyyah, and it is a derivation upon the (marriage's) validity. But according to the fatwa position, the lesser of the specified dower and the proper dower should be due, and no maintenance for her during this waiting period, as is clear. And in al-Khaniyyah: If the guardian married her off to a non-compatible person and consummated the marriage, then she separated from him by divorce, then she married this same husband without a guardian, then the judge separated them before consummation, then according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, the husband owes the full second dower and she must observe a future waiting period; Muhammad said: no dower is due on the husband and she must complete the first waiting period. He mentioned parallels for this, which will come in the Book of Waiting Period. It should be a derivation based on the manifest narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). But according to the fatwa position, the second dower is not due by consensus because it is a void marriage, as clarified in al-Khaniyyah, in the case where the second marriage is void. He specified 'marriage' because he has the right to take her back if he divorced her revocably after the guardian had married her to a non-compatible person with her consent. Thus in al-Dhakhirah.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a ruling statement. It opens by establishing that a guardian's consent to one marriage with a non-kuf' (non-compatible) does not imply consent to a second marriage with a non-kuf'. This is because each marriage is a separate contract with its own rights, and the guardian may have valid reasons for consenting to one but not another. The text then presents several scenarios: a woman of unknown lineage who marries a man of low profession (cupper); if her lineage is later established to be from Quraysh (a high lineage), her father can annul the marriage because the husband is not compatible in lineage. Conversely, if she confesses to being a slave, the master cannot annul the marriage—this is because the master's right is over her as property, not as a guardian with marriage authority. Another scenario: a man marries off his minor slave girl, then claims she is his daughter; if the husband is compatible, the marriage remains; if not, analogically it is binding, but the fatwa position may differ. The passage then details the effects of judicial annulment: after consummation, she gets the full specified dower, must observe iddah, and gets maintenance; before consummation, no dower is due according to the analogy, but the fatwa says the lesser of the specified dower and proper dower is due. Then a clear intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: if the guardian married her to a non-kuf' (with consummation), she divorced, then she remarried the same husband without a guardian, and the judge annuls before consummation. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the husband owes the full second dower and she begins a new iddah. Muhammad says no dower and she completes the first iddah. The text notes that this is based on Zahir al-Riwayah, but the operative fatwa view (mufta bihi) is that the second marriage is void (fasid) and no dower is due by consensus. The last point clarifies that if the husband divorced her revocably, he can take her back, distinguishing between separation by judicial annulment and divorce.

Key Terms
كفء (kuf'): Compatibility in marriage between spouses in terms of lineage, freedom, Islam, profession, etc.
ولي (wali): Guardian of the woman for marriage; typically the father or closest male relative.
رضا (rida): Consent, especially of the guardian to the marriage.
مهر (mahr): Dower, the financial gift from husband to wife as part of marriage contract.
عدة (iddah): Waiting period a woman must observe after separation from husband before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the intra-Hanafi dispute presented, what is the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) position regarding the second marriage when a woman remarries the same non-kuf' husband without a guardian after a divorce?
A) The second marriage is valid and the husband pays the full second mahr.
B) The second marriage is void (fasid) and no second mahr is due.
C) The second marriage is valid but no mahr is due.
D) The second marriage is suspended on guardian approval.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that a second marriage to the same non-kuf' without guardian consent is void (fasid), so no second mahr is due and the first iddah is completed.

Consent of One Equal Guardian: The Principle and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether consent of some guardians suffices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on consent of multiple equal guardians, explain Abu Yusuf's objection, and evaluate the dalil for indivisible guardianship.

Core Idea
Guardianship is a single indivisible right, so consent of one equal guardian binds all.

In Hanafi nikah, the consent of the guardian (wali) is essential for a valid marriage. But what happens when there are multiple guardians of the same rank, such as two brothers or two uncles? The classical Hanafi position, held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, states that the consent of any one of them suffices, and the others cannot object later. Abu Yusuf disagreed, drawing an analogy to joint debt. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute and the reasoning behind the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
The rule is 'رضا البعض كالكل' (consent of some is like consent of all). It applies when guardians are equal in rank (mustawiyan fi al-daraja).
2
State Abu Yusuf's objection
He analogizes to joint creditors: one creditor's forgiveness does not bind others. So each guardian has an independent right to consent or object.
3
Examine the majority's counter-argument
The majority respond that guardianship is a single indivisible right (haqq wahid la yatajazza'), unlike divisible debt.
4
Explore the proof — talil with trust analogy
They compare it to 'wilayat al-amanah' (guardianship of trust), which vests completely in each trustee.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
Under the majority view, once one guardian consents, the marriage proceeds; Abu Yusuf would allow other guardians to object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ورضا البعض كالكل أي ورضا بعض الأولياء المستويين في الدرجة كرضا كلهم حتى يتعرض أحد منهم بعد ذلك. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكون كالكل كما إذا أسقط أحد الدائنين حقه من المشترك . ، ولهما إنه حق واحد لا يتجزأ لأنه ثبت بسبب لا يتجزأ فيثبت لكل على الكمال كولاية الأمان. قيدنا بالاستواء احترازاً عما إذا رضي الأبعد فإن للأقرب الاعتراض. كذا في فتح القدير وغيره وقيد بالرضا لأن التصديق بأنه كفء من البعض لا يسقط حق من أنكرها قال في المبسوط : لو ادعى أحد الأولياء أن الزوج كفء وأثبت الآخر أنه ليس بكفء يكون له أن يطالبه بالتفريق لأن المصدق ينكر سبب الوجوب الشيخ قاسم: وينبغي أن يقيد عدم ا الصحة المفتى به بما إذا كان لها أولياء أحياء لأن عدم الصحة إنما كان على ما وجه به هذه الرواية دفعاً لضررهم فإنهم يتضررون أما ما يرجع إلى حقها فقد سقط برضاها بغير الكفء اهـ . قلت : قد صرح بذلك المؤلف هناك ونقل الاتفاق عليه حيث قال : وهذا كله إذا كان لها ،أولياء أما إذا لم يكن لها ولي فهو صحيح مطلقاً اتفاقاً .
His statement: 'And the consent of some is like the consent of all' means that the consent of some of the guardians who are equal in rank is like the consent of all of them, such that none of them can object afterward. Abu Yusuf said: It is not like the consent of all, just as when one of the creditors forfeits his right from the common property. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is a single right that is indivisible because it is established due to an indivisible cause, so it is established for each in its entirety, like the guardianship of trust. We restricted it to equality to exclude the case where a more distant guardian consents, because the nearer guardian has the right to object. Thus in Fath al-Qadir and others. And we restricted it to consent because the affirmation that the husband is compatible by some does not forfeit the right of those who deny it. He said in al-Mabsut: If one of the guardians claims that the husband is compatible and the other proves that he is not compatible, the latter has the right to demand separation because the one who affirms denies the cause of obligation. Shaykh Qasim: And it should be restricted that the invalidity according to the fatwa is only when she has living guardians, because the invalidity is only on the basis of this narration to ward off their harm, for they are harmed; as for what pertains to her right, it has been forfeited by her consent to a non-compatible. I said: The author has stated that there and transmitted agreement on it, as he said: 'All this is when she has guardians; but if she has no guardian, it is absolutely valid by agreement.'
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a definition ruling. It explains the principle that if there are multiple guardians of equal rank (e.g., two brothers or two uncles), the consent of any one of them is sufficient for the marriage, and the others cannot object afterward. Abu Yusuf disagrees, analogizing it to a common debt where one creditor's forgiveness does not affect the others. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that the right of guardianship is a single indivisible right, like a trust (amana), so each guardian holds it in full. Therefore, once one consents, it is as if all have consented. The text adds restrictions: the guardians must be equal in rank (e.g., if a distant cousin consents, a nearer brother can still object); and consent means explicit approval, not mere silence. An example is given: if one guardian claims the husband is compatible and another proves he is not, the one who proves incompatibility can still demand separation. Finally, Shaykh Qasim notes that the fatwa position that the marriage is invalid (when a woman marries without kafa'ah) only applies when she has living guardians; if she has no guardian at all, the marriage is valid by consensus.

Key Terms
ولاية (wilayah): Guardianship authority over a woman for marriage.
استواء (istiwā'): Equality in rank among guardians (e.g., both are brothers, both are uncles).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for Abu Yusuf's objection to the general rule?
A) He thinks guardianship is indivisible.
B) He analogizes guardianship to joint debt.
C) He relies on a hadith from the Prophet.
D) He argues the woman must consent first.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, consent of one equal guardian is sufficient; Abu Yusuf's dissent does not affect the mufta bihi.

Restrictions on the Rule: Equality, Compatibility, and the Orphan Exception
Expansion of the ruling with restrictions and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two key restrictions (equality of rank and explicit consent vs. compatibility claim) and apply the exception for a woman with no guardian.

Core Idea
The rule 'consent of some equals all' only works among equal guardians; a distant guardian's consent can be overruled, and a woman without any guardian decides for herself.

The principle that consent of some guardians equals consent of all is not absolute. The text specifies two key restrictions: First, the guardians must be equal in rank — if a more distant guardian consents, a nearer one can still object. Second, consent means explicit approval; a mere claim by one guardian that the husband is compatible does not prevent another from denying compatibility. Additionally, if the woman has no living guardians at all, the marriage contract is valid by consensus, and no guardian’s consent is needed. This lesson examines these conditions and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the equality condition
The rule is restricted to 'المستويين في الدرجة' (those equal in rank). Example: two brothers vs. a brother and a paternal cousin.
2
Distinguish consent from compatibility affirmation
Consent (rida) is explicit agreement; affirming compatibility (tasdiq bil-kafa'ah) does not forfeit the right of another guardian to object on grounds of non-compatibility.
3
Apply the Mabsut example
If one guardian claims compatibility and another proves non-compatibility, the marriage can be annulled at the request of the objecting guardian.
4
Examine the orphan exception (Shaykh Qasim's note)
The fatwa that a marriage without kafa'ah is invalid applies only when she has living guardians; if she has no guardian, it is valid by consensus.
5
Synthesize the overall conceptual map
Combine the core rule, the two restrictions, and the exception into a single decision tree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ورضا البعض كالكل أي ورضا بعض الأولياء المستويين في الدرجة كرضا كلهم حتى يتعرض أحد منهم بعد ذلك. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكون كالكل كما إذا أسقط أحد الدائنين حقه من المشترك . ، ولهما إنه حق واحد لا يتجزأ لأنه ثبت بسبب لا يتجزأ فيثبت لكل على الكمال كولاية الأمان. قيدنا بالاستواء احترازاً عما إذا رضي الأبعد فإن للأقرب الاعتراض. كذا في فتح القدير وغيره وقيد بالرضا لأن التصديق بأنه كفء من البعض لا يسقط حق من أنكرها قال في المبسوط : لو ادعى أحد الأولياء أن الزوج كفء وأثبت الآخر أنه ليس بكفء يكون له أن يطالبه بالتفريق لأن المصدق ينكر سبب الوجوب الشيخ قاسم: وينبغي أن يقيد عدم ا الصحة المفتى به بما إذا كان لها أولياء أحياء لأن عدم الصحة إنما كان على ما وجه به هذه الرواية دفعاً لضررهم فإنهم يتضررون أما ما يرجع إلى حقها فقد سقط برضاها بغير الكفء اهـ . قلت : قد صرح بذلك المؤلف هناك ونقل الاتفاق عليه حيث قال : وهذا كله إذا كان لها ،أولياء أما إذا لم يكن لها ولي فهو صحيح مطلقاً اتفاقاً .

Abu Yusuf said: It is not like the consent of all, just as when one of the creditors forfeits his right from the common property. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is a single right that is indivisible because it is established due to an indivisible cause, so it is established for each in its entirety, like the guardianship of trust. I said: The author has stated that there and transmitted agreement on it, as he said: 'All this is when she has guardians; but if she has no guardian, it is absolutely valid by agreement.'

Silence of Guardian Is Not Consent
Clarifies guardian's silence is not consent with exception for childbirth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a guardian's silence does not imply consent to a non-kuf' marriage and identify the exception where childbirth eliminates the guardian's right to annul.

Core Idea
Silence is not consent—only childbirth or pregnancy removes the guardian's right to annul a non-kuf' marriage.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key principle in Hanafi marriage law. When a woman marries a man who is not her kuf' (compatible), the silence of her guardian does not count as consent. However, if she gives birth (or is visibly pregnant), the guardian loses the right to seek annulment, to avoid harm to the child. The passage also addresses the procedural aspect when the primary guardian is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The author states that a guardian's silence is not considered consent (رضا) because it is ambiguous (محتمل). This is the default ruling except in specific cases mentioned elsewhere.
The phrase 'لا السكوت' is from the base text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on childbirth
Some earlier sources (Mabsut, al-Mi'raj) allowed the guardian to annul even after childbirth, but the later commentators (sharihun) restricted this: if the woman gives birth, the guardian loses the right of annulment. This is the correct madhhab (mufta bihi), chosen in al-Khulasa.
The reasoning (talil) is the harm (darar) caused by annulment after the child is born.
3
Extend the ruling to pregnancy
Apparent pregnancy (حبل ظاهر) is analogized to birth, so the same rule applies: the guardian's right to annul is lost.
This is a logical extension based on similar harm.
4
Apply the procedural rule for absent guardians
If the first guardian (e.g., father) is absent with disconnected absence (ghayba munqati'a), the next guardian (e.g., brother) can dispute the marriage. The husband must prove that the first guardian married him; otherwise, the judge separates them.
The brother is considered a valid adversary because the first guardian is unreachable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (لا) (السكوت أي لا يكون سكوت الولي رضا لأنه محتمل فلا يجعل رضا إلا في مواضع مخصوصة ليس هذا منها. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا ولدت فله حق الفسخ بعد الولادة كما في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام، وكما في المعراج، لكن قيده الشارحون بعدم الولادة، فلو ولدت فليس له حق الفسخ، وظاهر كلامهم أنه المذهب الصحيح ولذا اختاره في الخلاصة وكأنه للضرر الحاصل بالفسخ وينبغي أن يكون الحبل الظاهر كالولادة. وشمل ما إذا طالت المدة كما في الخلاصة. وذكر في الذخيرة: امرأة تحت رجل هو ليس بكفء لها فخاصمه أخوها في ذلك وأبوها غائب غيبة منقطعة أو خاصمه ولي آخر غيره أولى منه وهو غائب عنه غيبة منقطعة فادعى الزوج أن الولي الأولى زوجه، يؤمر بإقامة البينة وإلا فرق بينهما، فإن أقام بينة على ذلك قبلت بينته وأجزتها على الأولى يعني الأول الذي هو أولى لأن هذا خصم ا هـ .
His statement: '(No) (silence)' means that the guardian's silence is not considered consent because it is ambiguous, so it is not made consent except in specific places, and this is not among them. It was left unrestricted, so it includes the case where she gives birth; he has the right of annulment after childbirth, as in the Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam and as in al-Mi'raj, but the commentators restricted it to the absence of childbirth, so if she gave birth, he does not have the right of annulment, and apparently their statement is the correct madhhab, and thus it was chosen in al-Khulasa, as if due to the harm caused by annulment, and apparent pregnancy should be like childbirth. And it includes if a long period has passed, as in al-Khulasa. And in al-Dhakhirah: A woman under a man who is not compatible with her; her brother disputes with him about that while her father is absent in a disconnected absence, or another guardian who is more entitled than him disputes while he too is absent in a disconnected absence, and the husband claims that the first guardian married him. He is ordered to provide evidence, otherwise the judge separates them. If he provides evidence of that, his evidence is accepted and I make it binding on the first guardian, i.e., the one who is more entitled, because this one is an adversary. [End quote].
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement clarifying that the silence of a guardian does not count as consent to a marriage with a non-kuf' (incompatible) spouse. The reason is that silence is ambiguous (muhtamal) — it could indicate acceptance, disapproval, or indecision — so it cannot be taken as consent except in specific cases where the law presumes consent from silence, and this situation of kafa'ah is not one of them. The text then discusses two scenarios: (1) If the woman gives birth after the marriage, the guardian's right to annul is lost, because annulment would cause harm to the child and family. Some early sources (Mabsut, al-Mi'raj) gave the guardian the option to annul even after birth, but the later scholars restricted it, and the correct madhhab is that birth eliminates the right of annulment. Apparent pregnancy (the belly showing) is treated like birth in this regard. (2) If a long period has passed without the guardian objecting, it does not amount to consent. Then an example from al-Dhakhirah: a woman is married to a non-kuf' man; her brother disputes the marriage. Her father is absent in a 'disconnected absence' (ghayba munqati'a, meaning no communication). The husband claims the father (the first guardian) married him. The husband is ordered to provide evidence; if he does, it is accepted and the judge will enforce the marriage against the father (who is the first guardian) because the brother (the adversary) is a valid opponent.

Key Terms
السكوت (al-sukūt): Silence of the guardian; not considered consent in matters of kafa'ah.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage by the guardian due to lack of compatibility.
غيبة منقطعة (ghaybah munqaṭi'ah): A long absence with no communication; in such cases, a lower guardian can act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi madhhab, does a guardian lose his right to annul a non-kuf' marriage if the woman gives birth?
A) Yes, the right is lost after childbirth.
B) No, the guardian can annul even after birth.
C) It depends on whether the birth was in wedlock.
D) The right is lost only if the father consented.

Key Takeaway
A guardian's silence is not consent to a non-kuf' marriage, but childbirth eliminates his right to seek annulment.

The Six Matters of Kafa'ah (Compatibility) in Marriage
Lists the six criteria for compatibility in marriage and the timing rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six matters considered for kafa'ah in Hanafi fiqh and explain when compatibility is assessed.

Core Idea
Kafa'ah is assessed at marriage contract inception; later change does not annul the marriage.

Kafa'ah (compatibility) in marriage is a key Hanafi concept that empowers a guardian to object if the groom is not a suitable match in certain specified attributes. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq lists those attributes and sets the crucial timing rule: compatibility matters at the time of the contract, not after.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six matters
Read the list: lineage, freedom, Islam, parents, piety, wealth and profession. Note that 'parents' are treated like 'fathers' in terms of social standing.
The text explicitly says 'six things'.
2
Understand the timing rule
Compatibility is considered at the beginning of the contract (at the time of marriage). If the husband later becomes a sinner, the marriage is not annulled.
This is based on the quote from al-Zuhriyyah.
3
Distinguish validity vs. guardian's right
Kafa'ah is not a condition for the contract's validity; it is a condition for the guardian's option to annul if the marriage was contracted without his consent.
The marriage remains sahih even if compatibility is absent, but the guardian can seek annulment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الكفاءة تعتبر نسباً فقريش أكفاء والعرب أكفاء وحرية وإسلاماً وأبوان فيهما كالآباء وديانة ومالاً وحرفة لأن هذه الأشياء يقع بها التفاخر فيما بينهم فلا بد من اعتبارها . وتعتبر الكفاءة عند ابتداء العقد وزوالها بعد ذلك لا يضر ولذا قال في الظهرية : ولو تزوجها وهو كفء لها ثم صار فاجراً داعراً لا يفسخ النكاح ا.هـ. وقد ذكر المصنف اعتبارها في ستة أشياء : الأولى النسب وهو معروف، وأما العرب فهم خلاف العجم وأحدهما عربي، قوله (وأجزتها على الأولى ضمير المتكلم في قوله وأجزتها للإمام محمد فإن المسألة في
His statement: '(Compatibility is considered in lineage: Quraysh are compatible with Quraysh, Arabs are compatible with Arabs, and in freedom, and in Islam, and parents in these are like fathers, and in piety, and in wealth, and in profession) because these are things by which boasting occurs among them, so they must be considered. Compatibility is considered at the inception of the contract; its disappearance afterward does not harm, hence it was said in al-Zuhriyyah: If he married her while he was compatible with her, then later became a wicked sinner, the marriage is not annulled. Ends. The author has mentioned its consideration in six things: first, lineage, which is known; as for Arabs, they are the opposite of non-Arabs, and one of them is an Arab.' The text then starts another topic but is cut off in the OCR.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling enumerating the six criteria for kafa'ah (compatibility) in marriage according to the Hanafi school. The six matters are: (1) Lineage (nasab): Quraysh are compatible with other Quraysh, and Arabs (non-Quraysh Arabs) are compatible with other Arabs. (2) Freedom (hurriyyah): a free person is compatible with a free person. (3) Islam: a Muslim is compatible with a Muslim. (4) Parents (abawān): the condition of the parents in compatibility, like the condition of fathers—meaning the social standing of parents matters. (5) Piety (diyānah): religiousness and moral character. (6) Wealth (māl) and Profession (ḥirfah): both are considered because people boast about these. The text emphasizes that these criteria are considered at the time of the marriage contract; if compatibility disappears later (e.g., the husband becomes a sinner), the marriage is not annulled. This is an important principle: once valid, it remains valid. The 'six things' list may seem like more than six, but the author combines 'parents' with 'fathers' and 'wealth' with 'profession' as two items? Probably the six are: 1) lineage, 2) freedom, 3) Islam, 4) parents, 5) piety, 6) wealth and profession (as one category). The OCR cuts off before completion, but the intended list is clear.

Key Terms
كفاءة (kafā'ah): Compatibility between spouses in specific attributes.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; Quraysh compatible with Quraysh, Arabs with Arabs.
حرية (ḥurriyyah): Freedom; a free person is compatible with a free person.
إسلام (Islām): Religion; a Muslim is compatible with a Muslim.
ديانة (diyānah): Piety and moral character.
حرفة (ḥirfah): Profession or occupation; certain low professions (e.g., cupper, butcher) affect compatibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many matters are considered for kafa'ah (compatibility) according to this passage?
A) Four things: lineage, freedom, Islam, and piety.
B) Five things: lineage, freedom, Islam, parents, and piety.
C) Six things: lineage, freedom, Islam, parents, piety, wealth and profession.
D) Three things: lineage, freedom, and Islam.

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah is considered in six matters at contract inception; later change does not annul the marriage.

Kafa'ah Among Quraysh: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Operative Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kafa'ah among Quraysh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that all Quraysh are equal in kafa'ah, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the majority, and apply the dominant view to a marriage scenario.

Core Idea
All Quraysh are equal in kafa'ah; a Hashimite woman may marry a non-Hashimi Qurayshi.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage compatibility (kafa'ah). The chapter on Nikah defines who is considered Quraysh and whether subtribes differentiate. The passage explains the lineage of the four caliphs to show they are all Quraysh, then presents the evidence for equality. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify the operative fatwa when scholars differ.

Guided Path
1
Define Quraysh lineage
Identify the common ancestor (al-Nadr ibn Kinanah) and note that all descendants are Quraysh. The caliphs trace back to this ancestor.
This definition is crucial to determine who falls under the ruling.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: all Quraysh are equal; a Hashimite woman's marriage to a non-Hashimi Qurayshi is valid and cannot be annulled for lack of kafa'ah.
This is the mufta bihi.
3
Identify Imam Muhammad's opposing view
Imam Muhammad argued that the family of the caliphate (Ahl al-Bayt al-Khilafa) is higher, so a woman from that family is not equal to other Quraysh.
He held that such a marriage would be subject to annulment.
4
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The majority proof: the Prophet married his daughter to Uthman (Umayyad) and Ali married his daughter to Umar (Adawi) – both non-Hashimi. This shows no differentiation.
This refutes Muhammad's position.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: under the majority, a Hashimite woman can marry any Qurayshi man without risk of annulment; under Muhammad's view, she could not marry a non-Hashimi Qurayshi if he is from a caliphal family.
This shows how ikhtilaf affects real marriage contracts.

Source Text

Book of Nikah, Section on Kafa'ah. ... And thereby the scholars deduced that difference is not considered among Quraysh, and that is the meaning of 'they are equal' so that if a Hashimite woman marries a Qurayshi non-Hashimi, her contract is not invalidated, but if she marries a non-Qurayshi Arab, they have the right to annul it, like marrying an Arab woman to a non-Arab. The evidence is that the Prophet married his daughter to Uthman who was Umayyad not Hashimi, and Ali married his daughter Umm Kulthum to Umar who was Adawi not Hashimi. Thus the statement of Muhammad is refuted who considers increase by caliphate so that the people of the caliphate household are not equal to other Quraysh.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about kafa'ah among Quraysh. The author defines Quraysh as descendants of al-Nadr ibn Kinanah, and lists the lineages of the four caliphs to show they are all Quraysh. The main ruling: all Quraysh are equal in marriage compatibility; a Hashimite woman can marry a non-Hashimi Qurayshi without annulment. The proof is the Prophet's marriage of his daughter to Uthman (Umayyad) and Ali's marriage of his daughter to Umar (Adawi). This refutes Imam Muhammad's view that the caliph's family has higher status. The commentary by Ramli notes a variant from al-Fayd al-Karaki that a Qurayshi is not equal to a Hashimi, but the author suggests the word 'not' may be a scribal addition.

Key Terms
قريش (Quraysh): Descendants of al-Nadr ibn Kinanah; all Arabs from that lineage are Quraysh.
الكفاءة (al-kafa'ah): Equivalence in marriage compatibility based on lineage, religion, profession, etc. Here focusing on lineage.
هاشمي (Hashimi): Descendant of Hashim, great-grandfather of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

All Quraysh are equal in kafa'ah; a Hashimite woman's marriage to a non-Hashimi Qurayshi is valid and cannot be annulled.

Non-Arab Kufu' for Arab Woman: The Knowledge Exception
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kafa'ah and the exception for the scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether a knowledgeable non-Arab is kufu' for an Arab woman and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Zahir al-riwaya says no, but later scholars exempt the scholar based on knowledge's superior honor.

In Hanafi marriage law, kafa'ah (compatibility) is a condition that gives the guardian the right to annul an unequal marriage. One key criterion is lineage: can a non-Arab man ever be equal to an Arab woman? The apparent transmitted position (zahir al-riwaya) says no, absolutely. But a strong line of later Hanafi masters argues that a knowledgeable non-Arab is equal, because the honor of knowledge outweighs lineage. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores that intra-madhhab debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core question: is a non-Arab (ajami) man kufu' for an Arab woman? Note that the debate focuses on the knowledgeable non-Arab.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Position A (zahir al-riwaya): absolute non-equality. Position B (many later mashayikh): equality for the knowledgeable non-Arab.
3
Analyze the proofs for each side
For position A: hadith on Arab superiority, and the principle that lineage is a fixed criterion. For position B: qiyas that knowledge elevates status (e.g., 'the learned are heirs of prophets'), and the redefinition of 'hasib' as knowledgeable.
4
Follow the tarjih
The author notes that although zahir al-riwaya is the 'madhhab', many later authorities (Ibn al-Humam, al-Bazzazi, etc.) adopt the exception for the scholar. The practical fatwa often follows the exception.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a non-Arab scholar marries an Arab woman, some judges would annul upon guardian's objection, others would not. The mufta bihi leans toward validity, especially if the scholar is knowledgeable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والحسب مكارم الأخلاق في المحيط عن صدر الإسلام الحسيب الذي له جاه وحشمة ومنصب. وفي الينابيع : الأصح أنه ليس كفئاً للعلوية. وأصل ما ذكره المشايخ من ذلك ما روي عن أبي يوسف أن الذي أسلم بنفسه أو أعتق إذا أحرز من الفضائل ما يقابل نسب الآخر كان كفئاً له كذا في فتح القدير. وكله تفقهات المشايخ، وظاهر الرواية أن العجمي لا يكون كفئاً للعربية مطلقاً. قال في المبسوط : أفضل الناس نسباً بنو هاشم ثم قريش ثم أقول : وقد أخذه من البحر فتحرر أن فيه اختلافاً ولكن حيث صح أن ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يكافئها فهو المذهب وخصوصاً وقد نص في الينابيع أنه لا تأمل . اهـ كلام الرملي أقول الثابت في ظاهر الرواية أن العجمي لا وقد أفتى في آخر الفتاوى الخيرية في قرشي جاهل تقدم على عالم في مجلس بأنه يحرم إذ كتب العلماء طافحة بتقدم العالم على القرشي ولم يفرق سبحانه وتعالى بين القرشي وغيره في قوله هل يستوي الذين يعلمون والذي لا ذكره تلوه لا يدل يصح
And the author conveyed that non-Arab is not equal to Arab even if he is hasib or knowledgeable. But Qadikhan mentioned in his Jami' that they said: the hasib is equal to the nasib, so the knowledgeable non-Arab is equal to the ignorant Arab and the Alawi woman because the honor of knowledge is above lineage and hasab. In al-Muhit from Sadr al-Islam: hasib is one with dignity and position. In al-Yanabi': the correct view is that he is not equal to the Alawiya. ... The apparent of the riwaya is that a non-Arab is not equal to an Arab woman absolutely. It is said in al-Mabsut: the best in lineage are Banu Hashim then Quraysh then Arabs... And after discussion, Ramli says: the established in the apparent riwaya is that the non-Arab is not equal to the Arab, but the scholars restricted it to the ignorant non-Arab... And the fatwa in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya on an ignorant Qurayshi taking precedence over a scholar is prohibited...
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the issue of a non-Arab man (ajami) being kufu' for an Arab woman. The main established position (zahir al-riwaya) is that a non-Arab is absolutely not equal. However, some later scholars (mashaikh) made an exception for a knowledgeable non-Arab, arguing that knowledge outweighs lineage. This is supported by Qadikhan and others. The discussion includes defining 'hasib' as one with position vs. knowledge. The text from al-Mabsut about best lineages is used by some to argue that knowledge can equalize, but it is not a direct proof. Ultimately, the relied-upon view in many later works is that a non-Arab, even if knowledgeable, is not equal, but the exception for the scholar has been adopted by many authorities including Ibn al-Humam. The passage ends with a note that the difference is based on the interpretation of 'hasib'.

Key Terms
العجمي (al-'ajami): Non-Arab, regardless of ethnicity.
الحسيب (al-hasib): One with honor, position, or knowledge; sometimes defined as one with worldly status, sometimes as knowledgeable.
النسيب (al-nasib): One of noble lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the view that a knowledgeable non-Arab is kufu' for an Arab woman?
A) It is the majority view and mufta bihi without dispute.
B) It is a weak view rejected by all later authorities.
C) It is affirmed by many later authorities but contrasts with the apparent riwaya.
D) It applies only to Qurayshi women.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on a non-Arab marrying an Arab woman: the apparent riwaya says absolute non-equality, but the later relied-upon view accepts a knowledgeable non-Arab as kufu'.

The Non-Arab's Match for an Arab Woman: Zahir al-Riwaya vs. Later Fatwa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kafa'a by lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi zahir al-riwaya ruling on a non-Arab's kafa'a for an Arab woman and identify the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
A non-Arab is absolutely not a match for an Arab woman in zahir al-riwaya, but later scholars allowed it for the learned.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym examines the disputed issue of whether a non-Arab man can be a suitable match (kuf') for an Arab woman, particularly a descendant of Fatima. The author navigates between the clear transmission from the early imams and the later fatwa of the mashayikh, showing how a madhhab can maintain a core position while accommodating practical concessions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling
The matn (source text) states: 'a non-Arab is not a match for an Arab, even if he is a nobleman or a scholar'. This is the starting point.
The ruling appears absolute.
2
Note the opposing view from the mashayikh
Scholars like Qadikhan and others report that a hasib (nobleman/scholar) can be a match for a nasib (one of lineage), and especially a non-Arab scholar matches an ignorant Arab or Alawiyya.
This view relies on Abu Yusuf's narration and the superiority of knowledge.
3
Trace the proofs for each position
The zahir al-riwaya proof is a hadith about Arab lineage hierarchy. The opposing proof uses the analogy that knowledge outweighs lineage, citing Aisha's superiority over Fatima due to knowledge.
The author calls the opposing view 'tafaqquhat' (juristic deductions).
4
Understand the author's tarjih
Ibn Nujaym follows the zahir al-riwaya as the madhhab, supported by al-Yanabi' and Tanwir al-Absar, but acknowledges the later fatwa is permissible to act upon.
The fatwa is a concession, not the primary ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفاد المصنف أن غير العربي لا يكافئ العربي وإن كان حسيباً أو عالماً لكن ذكر قاضيخان في جامعه قالوا الحسيب يكون كفئاً للنسيب فالعالم العجمي يكون كفئاً للجاهل العربي والعلوية لأن شرف العلم فوق شرف النسب والحسب مكارم الأخلاق في المحيط عن صدر الإسلام الحسيب الذي له جاه وحشمة ومنصب. وفي الينابيع : الأصح أنه ليس كفئاً للعلوية. وأصل ما ذكره المشايخ من ذلك ما روي عن أبي يوسف أن الذي أسلم بنفسه أو أعتق إذا أحرز من الفضائل ما يقابل نسب الآخر كان كفئاً له كذا في فتح القدير. وكله تفقهات المشايخ، وظاهر الرواية أن العجمي لا يكون كفئاً للعربية مطلقاً. قال في المبسوط : أفضل الناس نسباً بنو هاشم ثم قريش ثم العرب لما روي عن محمد بن علي عليه السلام أن الله اختار من الناس العرب ومن العرب قريشاً واختار منهم بني هاشم واختارني من بني أنها رواية عنه قوله (قالوا الحسيب الخ) قال الرملي : لا يخفى على أخي الفقه ما في قوله قالوا من التبري تأمل قوله (وكله) تفقهات المشايخ الخ قال الرملي قال في مجمع الفتاوى : العالم يكون كفؤاً للعلوية لأن شرف الحسب أقوى من شرف النسب، وعن هذا قيل : إن عائشة أفضل من فاطمة رضي الله تعالى عنهما لأن لعائشة شرف العلم كذا في المحيط. أقول: وقد جزم به صاحب المحيط وارتضاه كما ارتضاه في فتح القدير . ثم قال في النهر : وقد ارتضاه في فتح القدير وجزم به البزازي وجزم به في الفيض وجامع الفتاوى وذكره في الخلاصة بصيغة قال بعض المشايخ: وقد جعله صاحب الغرر متناً . وفي تنوير الأبصار العجمي : لا يكون كفؤاً للعربية ولو عالماً وهو الأصح اهـ. قال في شرحه : كذا في الفتح نقلاً عن الينابيع. أقول : وقد أخذه من البحر فتحرر أن فيه اختلافاً ولكن حيث صح أن ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يكافيها فهو المذهب وخصوصاً وقد نص في الينابيع أنه لا تأمل . اهـ كلام الرملي أقول الثابت في ظاهر الرواية أن العجمي لا يكون كفؤاً للعربية، وهذا وإن كان ظاهره الإطلاق لكن قيده المشايخ بغير العالم وكم له من نظير حيث يكون اللفظ مطلقاً فيحملونه على بعض مدلولاته أخذاً من قواعد مذهبية أو مسائل فرعية أو أدلة شرعية أو عقلية. وقد أفتى في آخر الفتاوى الخيرية في قرشي جاهل تقدم على عالم في مجلس بأنه يحرم إذ كتب العلماء طافحة بتقدم العالم على القرشي ولم يفرق سبحانه وتعالى بين القرشي وغيره في قوله هل يستوي الذين يعلمون والذي لا يعلمون ﴾ [الزمر: ٩] الخ وحيث جزم بهذا في مجمع الفتاوى والمحيط والبزازية والفيض وارتضاه المحقق ابن الهمام يجوز العمل به ولا يقال إنه مخالف لظاهر الرواية. وأما ما صححه في الينابيع فهو مبني على تفسير الحسيب بذي المنصب والجاه لا على تفسيره بالعالم والله أعلم
The author indicates that a non-Arab is not a match for an Arab, even if he is a nobleman or a scholar. But Qadikhan mentioned in his Jami' that they said: The nobleman (hasib) is a match for the one of lineage (nasib); so a non-Arab scholar is a match for an ignorant Arab and for an Alawiyya woman because the honor of knowledge is superior to the honor of lineage. 'Hasab' is good morals. In al-Muhit from Sadr al-Islam: the hasib is one who has status, dignity, and position. And in al-Yanabi': the correct view is that he is not a match for the Alawiyya. The origin of what the mashayikh mentioned from that is what was narrated from Abu Yusuf that one who becomes Muslim by himself or is freed, if he acquires virtues that match the lineage of the other, he is a match for him, as in Fath al-Qadir. All of this are juristic deductions (tafaqquhat) of the mashayikh, and the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) is that a non-Arab is absolutely not a match for an Arab woman. He said in al-Mabsut: The best people in lineage are Banu Hashim, then Quraysh, then the Arabs, due to what was narrated from Muhammad ibn Ali (peace be upon him) that Allah chose the Arabs from people, Quraysh from the Arabs, Banu Hashim from them, and from Banu Hashim He chose me. This is a narration from him. His statement: 'They said the hasib etc.' Al-Ramli said: It is not hidden from a brother of fiqh what is in his statement 'they said' of disassociation. Reflect on his statement: 'All of this are tafaqquhat of the mashayikh etc.' Al-Ramli said: In Majma' al-Fatawa: The scholar is a match for the Alawiyya because the honor of hasab is stronger than the honor of lineage. And from this it is said that Aisha is better than Fatima, may Allah be pleased with them, because Aisha has the honor of knowledge. Thus in al-Muhit. I say: The author of al-Muhit affirmed it and approved it, just as it was approved in Fath al-Qadir. Then he said in al-Nahr: It was approved in Fath al-Qadir, and affirmed by al-Bazzazi, affirmed in al-Fayd and Jami' al-Fatawa, and mentioned in al-Khulasa in the form 'some mashayikh said', and the author of al-Ghurar made it a matn. In Tanwir al-Absar: A non-Arab is not a match for an Arab woman even if he is a scholar, and this is the correct view. He said in its commentary: Thus in al-Fath from al-Yanabi'. I say: He took it from al-Bahr, so it is established that there is disagreement, but since it is confirmed that the apparent transmission is that he does not match her, that is the madhhab, especially since al-Yanabi' explicitly states that there is no reflection. End of al-Ramli's speech. I say: The established view in the apparent transmission is that a non-Arab is not a match for an Arab woman. This, although its apparent meaning is absolute, the mashayikh qualified it to exclude the scholar, and how many examples are there where the wording is absolute but they restrict it to some of its meanings, based on madhhab rules or subsidiary issues or legal or rational proofs. And a fatwa was issued at the end of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya regarding an ignorant Qurayshi who proceeded ahead of a scholar in a gathering: that it is forbidden, since the writings of scholars are overflowing with preferring the scholar over the Qurayshi, and Allah Most High did not differentiate between the Qurayshi and others in His saying: 'Are those who know and those who do not know equal?' [39:9] etc. And since this was affirmed in Majma' al-Fatawa, al-Muhit, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Fayd, and approved by Ibn al-Humam, it is permissible to act upon it, and it should not be said that it contradicts the apparent transmission. As for what al-Yanabi' corrected, it is based on the interpretation of hasib as one with position and status, not on the interpretation as scholar. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the suitability (kafa'a) of a non-Arab man for an Arab woman in marriage. The author first states the general ruling from the matn: a non-Arab is not a match for an Arab, even if he is a nobleman (hasib) or a scholar. However, he then presents the view of Qadikhan that according to some scholars, a hasib (one with good character and status) can be a match for a nasib (one of lineage), and particularly a non-Arab scholar is a match for an ignorant Arab and even for an Alawiyya woman (a descendant of Fatima). This is because the honor of knowledge supersedes the honor of lineage. The definition of hasab is given as good morals or status. In al-Yanabi', the correct view is that such a man is not a match for an Alawiyya. The author traces the origin of the lenient view to a narration from Abu Yusuf that one who embraces Islam or is freed, if he acquires virtues equivalent to the other's lineage, becomes a match. He then notes that all these lenient views are juristic deductions (tafaqquhat) of later scholars (mashayikh), whereas the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) from the founding imams is that a non-Arab is absolutely not a match for an Arab woman. The passage then cites al-Mabsut to establish the hierarchy of Arab lineages as evidence for the superiority of Arabs. Al-Ramli's commentary follows, emphasizing that the zahir al-riwaya is the madhhab, and the qualification by mashayikh (restricting the absolute to non-scholars) is a departure from the clear transmission. He concludes that the correct view for fatwa is the zahir al-riwaya, and the opinion that a learned non-Arab is a match is based on a different interpretation of 'hasib' (as one with status, not knowledge).

Key Terms
الكفاءة (al-kafa'a): Suitability or equality between spouses in specified criteria (lineage, religion, freedom, etc.) for marriage validity and to prevent annulment.
الحسيب (al-hasib): In this passage, interpreted as one with good character and status (makarim al-akhlaq, jah, hashmah, mansib).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The clear and established transmission from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the six core books (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what is the ruling of zahir al-riwaya regarding a non-Arab scholar marrying an Arab woman?
A) The non-Arab scholar is a suitable match (kuf') for an Arab woman if he is learned.
B) The non-Arab scholar is not a match for an Arab woman at all.
C) The non-Arab scholar is only a match for an Alawiyya woman.
D) The non-Arab scholar is a match only if he is also from Quraysh.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, the core transmission holds that a non-Arab is not a match for an Arab woman, but later fatwa allows it for scholars without overriding the madhhab.

Lineage in Kafa'a: The Ruling on Banu Bahila
Commentary on the hierarchy of Arab lineages and the ruling on Banu Bahila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of Arab lineages for kafa'a and apply the rule that Banu Bahila are suitable matches for other non-Qurayshi Arabs.

Core Idea
Banu Bahila are suitable for other Arabs; the bad acts of some do not taint the whole tribe.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the hierarchy of Arab lineages in marriage suitability (kafa'a). The author clarifies that lineage is only considered for Arabs, not for non-Arabs (mawali). Within Arabs, the best are Banu Hashim, then Quraysh, then the rest. A key point of dispute is whether the tribe of Banu Bahila is suitable for other Arabs. We will examine the evidence and the resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy
What is the order of Arab lineages according to al-Mabsut? Banu Hashim, then Quraysh, then the rest of Arabs.
2
Understand mawla
Why are non-Arabs not considered by lineage? Because they lost their lineages and pride is in religion or because they were conquered.
3
State the ruling on Banu Bahila
What does the author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) say? They are suitable for other Arabs except Quraysh.
4
Analyze the objection
Why does al-Hidaya exclude Banu Bahila? Due to reports of baseness (marrow extraction, eating leftover food).
5
Evaluate the refutation
How does Fath al-Qadir answer? The text does not differentiate; not every Bahili is base; actions of a subgroup do not apply to all.
The mufta bihi is the absolute view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله قال في المبسوط أفضل الناس نسباً بنو هاشم ثم قريش ثم العرب لما روي عن محمد بن علي عليه السلام أن الله اختار من الناس العرب ومن العرب قريشاً واختار منهم بني هاشم واختارني من بني هاشم ا هـ . ولم يذكر المصنف الموالي لأن المراد بالمولى هنا ما ليس بعربي وإن لم يمسه رق لأن العجم لما ضلوا أنسابهم كان التفاخر بينهم في الدين كما في الفتح، أو لأن بلادهم فتحت عنوة بأيدي العرب فكان للعرب استرقاقهم فإذا تركوهم أحراراً فكأنهم أعتقوهم. والمولي هم المعتقون كما في التبيين أو لأنهم نصروا العرب على قتل الكفار من أهل الحرب. والناصر يسمى مولى قال تعالى (وإن الكافرين لا مولى لهم [محمد : ۱۱] كما في غاية البيان . والحاصل أن النسب المعتبر هنا خاص بالعرب. وأما العجم فلا يعتبر في حقهم ولذا كان بعضهم كفئاً لبعض. وأما معتق العربي فهو ليس بكفء لمعتق العجمي كما سيأتي في الحرية. وأطلق المصنف في العرب فأفاد أن بني باهلة كفء لبقية العرب غير قريش. وفي الهداية : وبنو باهلة ليسوا بأكفاء لعامة العرب لأنهم معروفون بالخساسة ا هـ . قالوا : لأنهم كانوا يستخرجون النفي من عظام الموتى ويطبخون العظام ويأخذون الدسومات منها ويأكلون بقية الطعام مرة ثانية ورده في فتح القدير بأنه لا يخلو من نظر فإن النص لم يفصل مع أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان أعلم بقبائل العرب وأخلاقهم. وقد أطلق في قوله العرب بعضهم وليس كل باهلي كذلك بل فيهم الأجواد. وكون فصيلة منهم أو بطن صعاليك فعلوا ذلك لا يسري في حق الكل ا هـ . . فالحق الإطلاق. وباهلة في الأصل اسم امرأة من همدان والتأنيث للقبيلة، سواء كان في الأصل اسم رجل أو اسم امرأة. كذا الصحاح. وقال في الديوان الباهلة قبيلة من قبيلة القيس. وفي القاموس : باهلة قوم.
His statement: He said in al-Mabsut: The best people in lineage are Banu Hashim, then Quraysh, then the Arabs, due to what was narrated from Muhammad ibn Ali (peace be upon him) that Allah chose the Arabs from people, Quraysh from the Arabs, Banu Hashim from them, and from Banu Hashim He chose me. End. And the author did not mention the mawali because what is meant by mawla here is what is not Arab, even if not touched by slavery, because when the non-Arabs lost their lineages, their pride was in religion as in al-Fath, or because their lands were conquered forcefully by the hands of the Arabs, so the Arabs had the right to enslave them. When they left them free, it is as if they freed them. And the mawali are the freed slaves as in al-Tabyin, or because they aided the Arabs in killing the disbelievers of the people of war. And the aider is called mawla. Allah said: 'And indeed the disbelievers have no mawla' [47:11] as in Ghayat al-Bayan. The conclusion is that the lineage considered here is specific to Arabs. As for non-Arabs, it is not considered for them, therefore some of them are matches for others. As for the Arab freed slave, he is not a match for a non-Arab freed slave, as will come in freedom. And the author made absolute in 'Arabs' so it indicates that Banu Bahila are matches for the rest of the Arabs other than Quraysh. In al-Hidaya: Banu Bahila are not matches for the generality of Arabs because they are known for baseness. They said: Because they used to extract marrow from the bones of the dead, cook bones, take fats from them, and eat the leftover food a second time. But it was refuted in Fath al-Qadir: This is not free from consideration, because the text did not differentiate, while the Prophet (peace be upon him) was most knowledgeable of Arab tribes and their morals. And he made absolute in his statement 'Arabs' — not every Bahili is like that; rather among them are the generous. The fact that a subgroup or belly of vagabonds did that does not apply to all. So the truth is absolute. And Bahila originally is a woman's name from Hamdan, the feminine is for the tribe, whether the original is a man's name or a woman's name. Thus in al-Sihah. And it said in al-Diwan: Bahila is a tribe of al-Qays. In al-Qamus: Bahila is a people.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the hierarchy of Arab lineages and the ruling on Banu Bahila. The commentator first explains the statement from al-Mabsut that the best in lineage are Banu Hashim, then Quraysh, then the rest of Arabs, citing a hadith from Muhammad ibn Ali. The author (of the matn) did not mention the mawali (freed slaves/clients) because the term mawla here refers to non-Arabs, even if they were never slaves, since non-Arabs lost their own lineages and their pride is in religion. Alternatively, because their lands were conquered, the Arabs had the right to enslave them, so freeing them is like manumission. The conclusion is that lineage is only considered for Arabs; non-Arabs are not evaluated by lineage, so they are suitable for each other. An Arab freed slave is not a match for a non-Arab freed slave. The author then mentions that Banu Bahila are suitable for other Arabs (except Quraysh). However, al-Hidaya states that Banu Bahila are not suitable for general Arabs because they are known for baseness—specifically, they used to extract marrow from bones of the dead, cook bones, and eat leftover food. This is refuted by Fath al-Qadir, arguing that the text does not differentiate (it says 'Arabs' generally), and the Prophet was most knowledgeable; not every Bahili is like that; there are generous ones among them. The actions of a subgroup do not apply to all. Thus the correct view is that Banu Bahila are suitable (kuf') for other Arabs. The passage ends with a linguistic note on the word 'Bahila'.

Key Terms
المولى (al-mawla): Here it refers to non-Arabs (ajam) who are clients/freed slaves, but also includes those who were never slaves but are considered like mawali due to loss of lineage.
باهلة (Bahila): An Arab tribe; originally a woman's name; the tribe is considered part of the Arabs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir, why is the view that Banu Bahila are not suitable for other Arabs rejected?
A) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) expressly said they are suitable.
B) Because the bad acts of some individuals do not apply to the entire tribe.
C) Because Banu Bahila are actually from Quraysh.
D) Because the text in al-Hidaya is non-credible.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position is that Banu Bahila are suitable (kuf') for other non-Qurayshi Arabs; exceptions based on alleged baseness are not accepted.

Kafa'a Based on Freedom and Islam for Non-Arabs
Explanation of how freedom and Islam serve as criteria for kafa'a among non-Arabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criteria for kafa'a among non-Arabs and apply the gradations of freedom and Islam to determine suitability.

Core Idea
For non-Arabs, kafa'a hinges on freedom and Islam, not lineage; each degree matters.

In the Hanafi school, kafa'a is determined by different criteria for Arabs and non-Arabs. While Arabs are evaluated by lineage, non-Arabs take pride in freedom and Islam. This lesson unpacks the detailed gradations of these two criteria and shows how they affect marriage suitability. Understanding these rules helps guardians and judges decide on objections based on kafa'a.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Arab vs. non-Arab criteria
Identify that for non-Arabs, pride is in freedom and Islam, not lineage. This is stated at the beginning: 'وأما الثاني والثالث - أعني الحرية والإسلام - فهما معتبران في حق العجم لأنهم يفتخرون بهما دون النسب.'
2
Identify the two criteria and their gradations
Freedom and Islam each have degrees: the text lists for Islam: convert without Muslim parent → one Muslim parent → both Muslim parents → many ancestors in Islam. Similarly for freedom: slave → freed slave → father freed → both parents free, etc.
3
Apply the rule of non-matching
For each gradation, a man is not kuf' for a woman of higher degree. Examples: slave not for free-born; freed slave not for free-born; one parent in Islam not for both parents, etc.
4
Note the exception for Quraysh
Among Quraysh, fine gradations are not considered; even a Hashimi woman can marry a Qurayshi man. This is mentioned to avoid confusion.
5
Examine the subtlety about the freed slave
The text questions whether a slave is kuf' for a mu'taqa (freed woman). It says 'ظاهره أن العبد كفء للمعتقة وفيه تأمل'. Also, a noble freed slave is not matched by a lowly freed slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني والثالث - أعني الحرية والإسلام - فهما معتبران في حق العجم لأنهم يفتخرون بهما دون النسب، وهذا لأن الكفر عيب وكذا الرق لأنه أثره، والحرية والإسلام زوال العيب فيفتخر بهما دون النسب فلا يكون من أسلم بنفسه كفئاً لمن لها أب في الإسلام، ولا يكون من له أب واحد كفئاً لمن لها أبوان في الإسلام، ومن له أبوان في الإسلام كفء لمن لها آباء كثيرة فيه وهو المراد بقوله وأبوان فيهما كالآباء» أي في الإسلام والحرية وهي نظير الإسلام فيما ذكرنا فلا يكون العبد كفئاً لحرة الأصل. وكذا المعتق، لا يكون كفئاً لحرة أصلية والمعتق أبوه لا يكون كفئاً لمن له أبوان في الحرية. كذا في المعراج . وظاهره أن العبد كفء للمعتقة وفيه تأمل. وفي المجتبى معتقة الشريف لا يكافئها معتق الوضيع. وفي التجنيس : لو كان أبوها معتقاً وأمها حرة الأصل لا يكافئها المعتق لأن فيه أثر على أنه أورده لذلك بل لفائدة معرفة التفاضل في الأنساب وإلا يشكل بتأخير قريش عن بني هاشم، وقد علمت فيما سبق أنه لا يعتبر التفاضل فيما بين قريش حتى لو تزوجت هاشمية قرشياً لم يرد عقدها تأمل . قوله (لا يكافئها معتق الوضيع أما الموالي فإنه يكافيها قال في الذخيرة: وفي شرح الطحاوي
As for the second and third - namely freedom and Islam - they are considered for non-Arabs because they take pride in them rather than lineage. This is because disbelief is a defect, and likewise slavery because it is its effect. Freedom and Islam are removal of defect, so they take pride in them rather than lineage. So one who became Muslim by himself is not a match for one whose father is in Islam; and one who has one father in Islam is not a match for one whose both parents are in Islam; and one with both parents in Islam is a match for one with many ancestors in Islam. This is what is meant by his statement: 'And both parents in them are like ancestors' i.e., in Islam and freedom. And it is analogous to Islam in what we mentioned. So a slave is not a match for a free-born woman. Similarly, a freed slave is not a match for a free-born woman; and one whose father is a freed slave is not a match for one whose both parents are free. Thus in al-Mi'raj. Its apparent meaning is that a slave is a match for a freed slave woman (mu'taqa), but there is reflection. In al-Mujtaba: A noble freed woman (mu'taqat al-sharif) is not matched by a lowly freed slave (mu'taq al-wadi'). In al-Tajnisi: If her father is a freed slave and her mother is free-born, the freed slave does not match her because there is a trace of slavery. But he mentioned it only for the benefit of knowing the gradation in lineages, otherwise it would be problematic to rank Quraysh after Banu Hashim, and you have already learned that gradation is not considered among Quraysh; even if a Hashimi woman marries a Qurayshi man, her contract is not rejected. Reflect. His statement: 'The lowly freed slave does not match her. As for the mawali, he does match her.' Said in al-Dhakhira: And in Sharh al-Tahawi...
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the criteria of freedom and Islam for kafa'a among non-Arabs. Since non-Arabs do not have a lineage-based pride, their suitability is determined by the degree of freedom and adherence to Islam. Disbelief and slavery are defects, while freedom and Islam remove those defects. The text then elaborates on gradations: a self-convert is not a match for a woman with a Muslim father; a woman with both Muslim parents is not matched by one with only one Muslim parent; and multiple generations in Islam increase suitability. Similarly for freedom: a slave is not a match for a free-born woman; a freed slave is not a match for a free-born; and one generation of freedom is less than two. The apparent implication that a slave is a match for a freed woman (mu'taqa) is questionable. Further distinctions are made for noble versus lowly freed slaves. The author notes that these fine gradations are for understanding lineage, but among Quraysh, such fine gradation is not applied—a Hashimi woman marrying a Qurayshi man is valid without rejection. The passage ends with a note that a lowly freed slave does not match a noble freed woman, but a mawla (freed slave of the same status) does match her, referencing al-Dhakhira and Sharh al-Tahawi (though the quote is cut off).

Key Terms
الحرية (al-hurriyya): Freedom from slavery; considered a criterion for kafa'a among non-Arabs; detailed gradations from free-born to freed slave to descendant of freed slave.
المعتق (al-mu'taq): A freed slave; he is not a match for a free-born woman, nor for a woman of higher freed status (e.g., freed from a noble master).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, who is a suitable match (kuf') for a woman whose both parents are free (hurrat al-asl)?
A) A freed slave (mu'taq).
B) A man whose both parents are free.
C) A man whose father is a freed slave.
D) A slave.

Key Takeaway
For non-Arabs, kafa'a in nikah depends on equality in freedom and Islam, with detailed gradations; lineage is not considered.

The Condition of Piety (Diyaana) in Kafa'a: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on piety as a condition for marriage suitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the consideration of piety in kafa'a, and identify the mufta bihi position with its rationale.

Core Idea
Piety is required for kafa'a according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad only requires it when immorality brings public shame.

This passage tackles a nuanced point within Hanafi nikah: should a woman's piety determine who is a suitable husband? The senior Hanafi imams divided on the answer, and their difference carries practical consequences for marriage contracts. By mastering this dispute, you will be able to apply the correct ruling in fatwa and understand how later Hanafi authorities resolved the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Element
Determine exactly what is being disputed: the fourth condition of kafa'a, namely piety (diyaana). Note that the passage distinguishes diyaana from mere 'deen' (Islam) to avoid repetition.
Piety here means taqwa, zuhd, and righteousness, not just being Muslim.
2
State the View of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They consider piety a necessary condition for marital suitability. Their dalil: piety is among the highest boasts, and a woman is more shamed by her husband's immorality than by low lineage.
This view is labeled 'as-sahih' (correct) in the text, indicating its strength in transmission.
3
State the View of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad holds that piety is not a condition unless the man's misconduct is publicly degrading—he slaps, is mocked, or goes drunk in the streets. His dalil: matters of the afterlife should not govern worldly contracts unless public honor is affected.
Muhammad's exception is specific: only when the man becomes an object of public scorn.
4
Analyze the Tarjih and Mufta Bihi
The passage cites Fath al-Qadir and al-Muhit that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. Some sources use 'qil' (it is said), but the relied-upon position is Muhammad's. This means in practice, a sinful man is considered kuf' unless his behavior causes public disgrace.
The authority weight is fatawa muta'akhkhirin, as the preference is from later Hanafi masters.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, a pious woman cannot be forced to marry an openly sinful man, and the marriage would be invalid for lack of kafa'a. Under Muhammad, the marriage is valid unless the sin is notorious—thus protecting marital stability while preserving honor.
Modern application: a man who drinks privately is still kuf'; one who is publicly drunk and scorned is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الرابع وهو الديانة ففسرها في غاية البيان بالتقوى والزهد والصلاح، وإنما لم يقل والدين لأنه بمعنى الإسلام فيلزم التكرار. وإن أريد بالأول إسلام الآباء وهنا إسلام الزوج لم يصح لأن إسلام الزوج ليس من الكفاءة وإنما هو شرط جواز النكاح. واعتبار التقوى فيها قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وهو الصحيح لأنه من أعلى المفاخر، والمرأة تعير بفسق الزوج فوق ما تعير بضعة نسبه. وقال محمد: لا أمور الآخرة فلا تبتنى أحكام الدنيا عليه إلا إذا كان يصفع ويسخر منه أو يخرج إلى الأسواق سكران ويلعب به الصبيان لأنه مستخف به كذا في الهداية. وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى المحيط إن الفتوى على قول محمد ولعله المحيط لبرهاني فإنه لم أجده في المحيط الرضوي وهو موافق لما صححه في المبسوط من أنها لا تعتبر عند أبي حنيفة وتصحيح الهداية معارض له، فالإفتاء بما في المتون أولى فلا يكون الفاسق كفئاً للصالحة بنت الصالحين، سواء كان معلناً معتقة أشرف القوم تكون كفؤاً للموالي لأن لها شرف الولاء وللموالي شرف إسلام الآباء قوله (وفي فتح القدير واعلم أنه لا يبعد الخ مقتضاه أنه بحث له ورأيت في الذخيرة ما صورته : ذكر ابن في الرجل يسلم والمرأة معتقة أنه كفء لها اهـ. والظاهر أن مثله ما لو كانت المرأة قد أسلمت والرجل معتق لكن بشرط أن لا يكون إسلامه طارئاً بل يكون مسلم الأصل بأن يكون أبوه إسلامه تبعاً لإسلام أبويه ثم يعتق هو وحده، أما لو كان إسلامه طارئاً فيكون فيه أثر الكفر وأثر الرقية معاً فلا يكون كفؤاً للحرة التي أسلمت تأمل قوله فعلى هذا فالنسب معتبر الخ حاصله أن النسب معتبر في العرب فقط، وإسلام الأب والجد في العجم فقط، والجزية في العرب والعجم، وكذا إسلام نفس الزوج قوله (وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى المحيط أن الفتوى على قول محمد الذي في التتارخانية عن المحيط وقيل وعليه الفتوى ومثله في الرمز معزياً إلى المحيط البرهاني وكذا في الذخيرة عبر بـ«قيل» قوله فإنهم قالوا لا يكون الفاسق كفؤا للصالحة بنت الصالحين لفظ الصالحة زائد من الكاتب فإن الذي في شروح الهداية كالفتح والمعراج وغاية البيان: لو نكحت امرأة من بنات سماعة
As for the fourth, which is diyaana (piety), it is explained in Ghayat al-Bayan as taqwa, zuhd, and righteousness. He did not say 'deen' because it means Islam, leading to repetition... Considering taqwa is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and it is correct because it is among the highest boasts... Muhammad said: These are matters of the Hereafter, so worldly rulings are not built upon them except if he slaps, is mocked, or goes to markets drunk...
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth condition of kafa'a: piety (diyaana). The author explains that piety means taqwa (God-consciousness), zuhd (asceticism), and righteousness. It is not simply 'deen' because that would be synonymous with Islam, causing repetition. The position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that piety is considered in marital suitability because it is a source of pride, and a woman is more disparaged by her husband's immorality than by low lineage. Muhammad, however, argues that piety pertains to the afterlife and should not affect worldly rulings unless the husband's misconduct is notorious, leading to public scorn—such as being slapped, mocked, or seen drunk in the streets. The fatwa according to Fath al-Qadir and al-Muhit is on Muhammad's view, though some sources state 'qil' (it is said). The passage also includes a note on the equality of a freed woman of noble descent to mawali due to the honor of wala', and the condition that the man's Islam must be original, not recent. It ends with a citation about a woman from the daughters of Sama'a, indicating the ruling applies mutatis mutandis.

Key Terms
الديانة (al-diyaana): Piety, religious observance, and moral uprightness.
التقوى (al-taqwa): God-consciousness and piety, the essence of diyaana.
الكفاءة (al-kafa'a): Marital suitability; equivalence between spouses in certain qualities determined by custom and law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition does Muhammad agree that piety should be considered?
A) If the man is a habitual sinner in private.
B) If the man's sin is publicly known and causes him to be despised and mocked.
C) If the woman's family is more pious than the man's.
D) If the man has committed any major sin.

Key Takeaway
Piety as a condition for kafa'a is disputed within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi (Muhammad's view) requires it only when the man's immorality is publicly disgraceful.
