Suitability in Piety: Fasiq vs Saliha
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kafa'ah in piety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a fasiq is kuf' for a saliha, identify the competing positions (father's piety vs woman's piety), and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The woman's own piety, not her father's, is the decisive criterion for kafa'ah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a nuanced debate within the Hanafi school: is a sinful man (fasiq) considered suitable (kuf') for a pious woman (saliha) in marriage? The issue turns on whose piety matters—the woman's, her father's, or both. The author navigates conflicting statements from earlier Hanafi authorities and provides a reconciled ruling. By examining this debate, you will learn how later Hanafi jurists (mutakhkhirin) settled an apparent contradiction and why the woman's own piety ultimately takes precedence.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the legal question: is a fasiq kuf' for a saliha? This is not about validity of marriage but about the guardian's right to object based on kafa'ah.
Kafa'ah is a condition for enforcement, not for contract validity.
2
Identify the competing positions
Extract the two main views: (1) only the father's piety matters (apparent from early explainers), (2) the woman's piety also matters (from al-Majma' and al-Khaniyah). Some scholars even consider both sides.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; no explicit dalil—based on custom and reasoning.
3
Analyze the reconciling views
Examine how later commentators like al-Qahistani and al-Ramz reconcile: they argue that a woman's piety is usually known through her father's piety, so mentioning only the father's piety implicitly includes her. Thus, both conditions are effectively required.
This reconciliation preserves both the letter of earlier texts and the underlying principle.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a fasiq is never kuf' for a saliha, regardless of her father's piety, because taqwa is the universal standard for all lineages.
Wealth or social status does not override lack of taqwa.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test the ruling: if a fasiq man (e.g., a wealthy but openly sinful merchant) proposes to a pious woman who comes from a pious family, the guardian has the right to object. If the woman herself is also sinful, then he may be considered kuf'.
The key is the woman's actual piety, not her father's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالفسق أو لا كما في الذخيرة ووقع لي تردد فيما إذا كانت صالحة دون أبيها أو كان أبوها صالحاً دونها هل يكون الفاسق كفئاً لها أو لا؟ فظاهر كلام الشارحين أن العبرة لصلاح أبيها وجدها فإنهم قالوا لا يكون الفاسق كفئاً للصالحة بنت الصالحين واعتبر في المجمع صلاحها فقال : فلا يكون الفاسق كفئاً للصالحة. وفي الخانية : لا يكون الفاسق كفئاً للصالحة بنت الصالحين فاعتبر صلاح الكل والظاهر أن الصلاح منها أو من آبائها كافٍ لعدم كون الفاسق كفئاً لها ولم أره صريحاً وظاهر كلامهم أن التقوى معتبرة في حق العرب والعجم فلا يكون العربي الفاسق كفئاً للصالحة عربية كانت أو عجمية. ثم ذكر: الصالحين فاسقاً كان للأولياء حق الردا . قوله ( والظاهر أن الصلاح منها أو من آبائها كاف) قال في النهر : ما في الخانية يقتضي اعتبار الصلاح من حيث الآباء فقط حيث قال : إذا كان الفاسق محترماً معظماً عند الناس كأعوان السلطان يكون كفئاً لبنات الصالحين ثم قال : وقال بعض مشايخ بلخ: لا يكون كفئاً لبنت الصلاح معلنا كان أو لا، وهو اختيار ابن الفضل وهذا هو الظاهر، ويؤيده ما مر عن المحيط، وحينئذ فلا اعتبار بفسقها والله تعالى الموفق .اهـ. ولا يخفي أن ما ذكره المؤلف عن الخانية أيضاً يقتضي اعتباره من جهتها أيضاً فالواجب التوفيق بما قاله المؤلف أو باشتراط الصلاح من الجهتين ويؤيده قول القهستاني في شرح قوله فليس فاسق كفئاً لبنت صالح» ما نصه : صالحة وإنما لم يذكر لأن الغالب أن تكون البنت صالحة بصلاحه .اهـ. فجعل صلاحها شرطاً وهي كصلاح آبائها وعليه يحمل كلام الشارحين ثم رأيته في الرمز صرح بذلك حيث قال: قلت: اقتصارهم بناء على أن صلاحها يعرف بصلاحهم لخفاء حال المرأة غالباً لا سيما الأبكار والصغائر اهـ. وفي الحواشي اليعقوبية : قوله فليس فاسق كفء بنت صالح فيه كلام وهو أن بنت الصالح يحتمل أن تكون فاسقة فيكون كفئاً كما صرحوا به، والأولى ما في المجمع وهو أن الفاسق ليس كفئاً للصالحة إلا أن يقال : الغالب أن بنت الصالح صالحة وكلام المصنف بناء على الغالب قوله (وظاهر كلامهم أن التقوى معتبرة الخ قال في النهر : صرح بهذا في إيضاح الإصلاح على أنه المذهب قوله
Regarding sinfulness or not as in al-Dhakhirah, and I had hesitation: if she is pious without her father, or her father is pious without her, is the sinner suitable for her or not? The apparent words of the explainers are that consideration is for the piety of her father and grandfather, for they said: The sinner is not suitable for a pious woman who is the daughter of pious people. And in al-Majma' they considered her piety and said: The sinner is not suitable for a pious woman. And in al-Khaniyah: The sinner is not suitable for a pious woman who is the daughter of pious people, so they considered piety of all. The apparent is that piety from her or from her fathers is sufficient for the sinner not being suitable for her, and I have not seen it explicitly. And their apparent words are that taqwa is considered regarding Arabs and non-Arabs, so the Arab sinner is not suitable for a pious woman whether she is Arab or non-Arab. Then he mentioned: For the parents, if he is a sinner, the guardians have the right of refusal. His statement: (And the apparent is that piety from her or from her fathers is sufficient). He said in al-Nahr: What is in al-Khaniyah necessitates considering piety only from the fathers' side, for he said: If the sinner is respected and honored among the people like the sultan's aides, he is suitable for the daughters of the pious. Then he said: And some scholars of Balkh said: He is not suitable for the daughter of a pious person whether openly or not, and this is the choice of Ibn al-Fadl, and this is the apparent, and it is supported by what passed from al-Muhit. Then there is no consideration for her sinfulness. And Almighty Allah is the giver of success. This is not hidden, that what the author mentioned from al-Khaniyah also necessitates considering it from her side, so it is necessary to reconcile with what the author said, or by stipulating piety from both sides. And it is supported by the saying of al-Qahistani in his commentary on his statement: 'So a sinner is not suitable for a pious man's daughter' with his text: She is pious, and he only did not mention it because the daughter is usually pious due to his piety. So he made her piety a condition and it is like the piety of her fathers. Upon this is borne the words of the explainers. Then I saw it in al-Ramz: he stated that explicitly where he said: I said: Their brevity is based on the fact that her piety is known by their piety due to the condition of women usually being hidden, especially virgins and minors. And in al-Hawashi al-Ya'qubiyyah: His statement: So a sinner is not kuf' for a pious man's daughter. There is discussion in it, for the daughter of a pious man may be sinful, so he would be suitable as they explicitly stated. And the better is what is in al-Majma': The sinner is not suitable for a pious woman, unless it is said: Usually the daughter of a pious man is pious, and the author's words are based on the usual. His statement: (And their apparent words are that taqwa is considered) etc. He said in al-Nahr: This is stated explicitly in Idah al-Islah that it is the school. His statement.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a sinful man (fasiq) is kuf' (suitable) for a pious woman (saliha). The discussion hinges on whether the woman's own piety matters or that of her father/forefathers. The author first presents differing views from sources like al-Dhakhirah, al-Majma', and al-Khaniyah. Some say only her father's piety matters; others say her piety alone or both. The commentary from al-Nahr suggests that the apparent view is that her piety is not considered if her father is pious, but a later reconciling view from al-Ramz argues that her piety is known through her father's piety due to the difficulty of knowing women's conditions. The preferable view, as in al-Majma', is that a fasiq is not kuf' for a saliha, but if she is actually sinful, he could be suitable. The passage ends by stating that taqwa is considered for both Arabs and non-Arabs.

Key Terms
كفء (kuf'): A man who is equal or suitable to a woman in marriage with respect to lineage, piety, wealth, profession, etc.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking taqwa.
صالحة (saliha): A woman who is righteous and pious, obedient to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) No, never
C) Yes, if he is wealthy
D) Yes, if she is also sinful

Key Takeaway
The decisive criterion for kafa'ah in piety is the woman's own piety; a fasiq is not suitable for a pious woman, even if her father is sinful or the fasiq is wealthy.

Wealth Suitability in Marriage: Ability to Pay Mahr and Nafaqa
Detailed discussion of wealth criteria in kafa'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for wealth suitability (kafa'ah) in marriage, including the ability to pay mahr and provide nafaqa, and identify the exceptions involving minor spouses and the role of prestige (jah).

Core Idea
A man is kuf' if he can pay mahr and provide one month's nafaqa, or earn it; prestige can compensate.

This lesson explores the wealth component of kafa'ah (suitability) in Hanafi marriage law. The core requirement is that the husband must be able to pay the mahr (dower) and provide nafaqa (maintenance). However, there is an internal Hanafi debate on the duration of nafaqa required, and exceptions exist for minor spouses and men of prestige. The passage also addresses a conceptual tension: kafa'ah is about equality, yet the wealth condition seems one-sided. The author resolves this by defining kafa'ah legally as the woman not being inferior or the man being equal or better.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wealth requirement for kafa'ah
The passage establishes that the husband must be capable of paying the mahr and providing nafaqa. Note that this is a condition on the husband's side, not mutual wealth equality.
The condition is about ability, not actual possession of wealth.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on nafaqa amount
Scholars differed on how much nafaqa must be affordable: six months or one month. The correction in al-Mujtaba (one month) is considered more apparent, and earning capacity suffices.
The mufta bihi is one month's nafaqa or the ability to earn it.
3
Examine exceptions: minor wife, minor husband, and jah
If the wife is a minor not requiring intercourse, the husband is kuf' even without nafaqa ability. A minor boy is kuf' for mahr if his father is rich, but not for nafaqa. A man with prestige (jah) like a sultan or scholar is kuf' even if only able to provide nafaqa.
These exceptions show that the requirement is flexible and context-dependent.
4
Understand the conceptual difficulty and its resolution
The passage notes that requiring wealth ability seems one-sided for equality-based kafa'ah. The author clarifies that legally, kafa'ah means the woman is not inferior or the man is equal or superior, resolving the apparent inconsistency.
This reflects the Hanafi juristic principle that kafa'ah is primarily a right of the guardian to avoid disparagement.

النفقة، فقيل يعتبر كتاب النكاح فصل في الكفاءة لأن هذا الرجل قادر على المهر فإنه يقضي أي الدينين شاء بذلك اهـ. واختلفوا في قدر نفقة ستة أشهر، وقيل نفقة شهر وصححه في التجنيس. وفي المجتبى : والصحيح أنه إذا كان قادراً على النفقة على طريق الكسب كان كفئاً اهـ. فقد اختلف التصحيح وتصحيح المجتبى أظهر كما لا يخفى. وفي الذخيرة : إذا كان يجد نفقتها ولا يجد نفقة نفسه يكون كفئاً، وإن لم يجد نفقتها لا يكون كفأ وإن كانت فقيرة ولو كانت الزوجة صغيرة لا تطيق الجماع فهو كفء وإن لم يقدر على النفقة لأنه لا نفقة لها. وفي المجتبى : والصبي كفء بغنى أبيه وهو الأصح .اهـ. يعني بالنسبة إلى المهر، وأما في النفقة فلا يعد غنياً بغنى أبيه لأن العادة أن الآباء يتحملون المهر عن الأبناء ولا يتحملون النفقة. كذا في الذخيرة والواقعات . وفي التبيين : وقيل إن كان ذا جاه كالسلطان والعالم يكون كفئاً وإن لم يملك إلا النفقة لأن الخلل ينجبر به ومن ثم قالوا : الفقيه العجمي يكون كفئاً للعربي الجاهل اهـ. وظاهر كلامهم أن القدرة على المهر والنفقة لا بد منه في كل زوج عربياً كان أو عجمياً لكل امرأة ولو كانت فقيرة بنت فقراء كما صرح به في الواقعات معللاً بأن المهر والنفقة عليه فيعتبر هذا الوصف في حقه اهـ. ففي إدخال القدرة عليهما في الكفاءة إشكال لأن الكفاءة المماثلة، وهذا شرط في حق الزوج فقط لكن قدمنا أنها شرعاً المماثلة أو كون المرأة أدنى.
The nafaqa (maintenance), so it is said: it is considered ... the chapter on marriage, section on suitability, because this man is capable of the mahr, for he can pay whichever of the two debts he wishes. Thus it ends. And they differed regarding the amount of maintenance: six months, and it was said: one month, and it was corrected in al-Tajnis. And in al-Mujtaba: The correct is that if he is capable of maintenance by means of earning, he is kuf'. Thus the corrections differed, and the correction of al-Mujtaba is more apparent as is not hidden. And in al-Dhakhirah: If he finds her maintenance but cannot find his own maintenance, he is kuf'. If he cannot find her maintenance, he is not kuf' even if she is poor. And if the wife is a minor who cannot bear intercourse, he is kuf' even if he cannot provide maintenance because there is no maintenance for her. And in al-Mujtaba: A minor child is kuf' due to his father's wealth, and this is the most correct. That is regarding the mahr. As for maintenance, he is not considered wealthy by his father's wealth because the custom is that fathers bear the mahr for sons but do not bear maintenance. Thus in al-Dhakhirah and al-Waqi'at. Thus including the ability for them in kafa'ah is problematic because kafa'ah is equality, and this is a condition only on the husband's side, but we have stated that legally it is equality or the woman being lower.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the wealth component in kafa'ah (suitability) for marriage. The author explains that the husband must be capable of paying the mahr (dower) and providing nafaqa (maintenance). There is disagreement on the amount of nafaqa required—whether six months or one month—with the correction in al-Mujtaba preferring one month. The ability to earn is sufficient. Exception: if the wife is a minor not requiring intercourse, the husband is kuf' even without maintenance ability. For a minor (boy), he is kuf' if his father is rich regarding mahr, but not for nafaqa. Prestige (jah) can compensate for lack of wealth, e.g., a scholar is kuf' for an ignorant Arab. The passage notes an inherent problem: kafa'ah is about equality, but requiring wealth for the husband seems one-sided; the author reconciles by stating that legally, kafa'ah means the woman is not inferior or the man is equal or better.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife, required in the marriage contract.
النفقة (al-nafaqa): Maintenance provided by the husband to the wife, including food, clothing, and shelter.
جاه (jah): Prestige, status, or influence that compensates for lack of wealth in kafa'ah.

Kafa'ah in Profession: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on profession in marital suitability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on considering profession in kafa'ah, explain the custom-based reasoning of each, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, suitability in profession for marriage is considered—a departure from Abu Hanifah's original reliance on Arab custom.

This lesson explores the sixth factor of kafa'ah: equality in profession (hirfah). The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifah initially did not require professional equality for Arabs who historically did not engage in base crafts, while Abu Yusuf argued it should be considered because lowly professions can cause shame. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) today is that profession matters, and this affects the guardian's right to object to a marriage.

Guided Path
1
Define the term
Understand what hirfah means: a trade, craft, or profession by which one earns a living. Note that the passage distinguishes it from sina'ah (industry) but ultimately treats them as similar.
Hirfah is broader than sina'ah, as it includes commerce.
2
Identify the dispute
Recognize that Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf differed on whether profession is a factor in kafa'ah. Abu Hanifah based his view on Arab custom (Arabs did not engage in base professions, so they were not shamed by them), while Abu Yusuf considered profession based on the custom of non-Arabs and the potential for shame.
The dispute is recorded in al-Bada'i' and Ghayat al-Bayan.
3
Examine the proofs
Analyze the reasoning behind each position: Abu Hanifah's dalil is custom ('urf) of the Arabs; Abu Yusuf's dalil is the general custom of people who take up professions and may be shamed by lowly ones, plus the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) that includes profession.
The passage notes that if Arabs themselves engage in professions, they too can be shamed.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Learn that the relied-upon position is that profession is considered. This is supported by the apparent narration from Abu Hanifah and his two companions, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan.
The Tarjih authority is Ghayat al-Bayan and the wider Hanafi tradition.
5
Apply the thamarah
See the practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifah's view, an Arab nobleman could marry a woman from a lowly profession without objection; under the mufta bihi, her guardian can object due to lack of professional equality.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows how the dispute affects real marriages.

As for the sixth, it is suitability in profession (al-hirfah) - with kasrah - and it is as in Diya' al-Hulum: with kasrah of the ha' and sukun of the ra', a noun from ihtiraf, earning by industry and trade. And he said in another place: industry is hirfah. And it is apparent that hirfah is more general than industry because it is the knowledge obtained from practice on work, and therefore the author expressed it as hirfah rather than industry, but in al-Qamus he said: Al-hirfah with kasrah is the food (subsistence) and the industry from which one earns, and everything that a person occupies himself with is called a craft and a profession because he inclines (yanharifu) to it. So it indicates that they are the same. And it has been verified in Ghayat al-Bayan that considering suitability in industries is the apparent narration from Abu Hanifah and his two companions, and it is: it was said: consider six months of maintenance. It was transmitted in al-Tatar Khaniyyah from al-Muntaqa from Muhammad, and in al-Khaniyyah and al-Tajnis from some: a year of maintenance. His statement: And the correction of al-Mujtaba is more apparent. He combined between the two sayings in al-Nahr and said: If it were said that if he is not a professional, then one month's maintenance, and if he is, then he should earn daily what he needs, it would be good. Then I saw it in al-Khaniyah, he transmitted what is in al-Mujtaba from the second, then said: And the better for professionals is his statement, and this points to what we said. His statement: (And it has been verified in Ghayat al-Bayan etc.). I say: And also in al-Bada'i': As for profession, al-Karkhi mentioned that suitability in it is considered according to Abu Yusuf, and that Abu Hanifah based the matter on the custom of the Arabs that their clients do these works, according to the custom of the people of the lands, and they take that as a profession, so they are shamed by lowly industries, so they are not between them. The implication of this is that if the Arabs themselves engage in professions, then suitability in profession is also considered. His statement: (But some works they do not intend as professions, so they are not shamed by them). And Abu Yusuf answered in reality. The end. I said.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage addresses the sixth factor in kafa'ah (suitability) for marriage: equality in profession (hirfah). The author defines hirfah as encompassing both industry and trade, noting that it is broader than 'industry' alone. There is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf holds that profession is considered, while Abu Hanifah's view is based on Arab custom—since Arabs did not engage in base professions, such equality was not required for them. However, if they do engage in a profession, it becomes relevant. The passage cites various sources and attempts to reconcile, noting that if a man is not a professional, a month's maintenance suffices, but if he is a professional, he must earn daily. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that profession is considered for kafa'ah.

Key Terms
الحرفة (al-hirfah): A trade, craft, or profession by which one earns a living, including both industry and commerce.
الصناعة (al-sina'ah): Industry or craft, a specific skill; sometimes used synonymously with hirfah.

B) Profession is considered

D) Only for Arabs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that equality in profession is required for kafa'ah, based on the apparent narration and the reasoning that a lowly profession can cause shame to the wife's family.

Ability to Pay Mahr and Maintenance as Kafa'ah Condition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ability to pay mahr and maintenance as condition of kafa'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ability to pay mahr and maintenance as a condition of kafa'ah and apply the rulings to different scenarios.

Core Idea
Ability to pay mahr and maintenance is a wajib condition for compatibility, but the amount and basis are disputed among Hanafi scholars.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of ability to pay mahr and maintenance as a condition for kafa'ah (compatibility) in marriage. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents multiple opinions from the school, discussing the required amount, scenarios where the condition is waived, and the role of social status. Understanding these nuances is crucial for a mufti or scholar determining compatibility in specific cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the passage discusses whether ability to pay mahr and maintenance is a condition for kafa'ah. The Hanafi school holds it is, but the extent is disputed.
2
Survey the differing opinions on the required amount
Note the views: some say six months' maintenance, some one year, some one month. The author notes that the correction of al-Mujtaba (ability to earn suffices) is more apparent.
3
Apply the scenario-based rulings
Examine how the ruling changes for different situations: if the husband can afford her maintenance but not his own, if the wife is a minor, if the groom is a minor, and if the husband has social status.
Pay attention to the distinction between mahr and maintenance for a minor groom.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The preferred view is that ability to earn maintenance suffices, and for a minor, father's wealth counts for mahr only. Social status can compensate for lack of wealth.

النفقة، فقيل يعتبر نفقة ستة أشهر) نقله في التتارخانية عن المنتقى عن محمد ونقل في الخانية والتجنيس عن بعضهم نفقة سنة. واختلفوا في قدر نفقة ستة أشهر، وقيل نفقة شهر وصححه في التجنيس. وفي المجتبى : والصحيح أنه إذا كان قادراً على النفقة على طريق الكسب كان كفئاً اهـ. فقد اختلف التصحيح وتصحيح المجتبى أظهر كما لا يخفى. وفي الذخيرة : إذا كان يجد نفقتها ولا يجد نفقة نفسه يكون كفئاً، وإن لم يجد نفقتها لا يكون كفأ وإن كانت فقيرة ولو كانت الزوجة صغيرة لا تطيق الجماع فهو كفء وإن لم يقدر على النفقة لأنه لا نفقة لها. وفي المجتبى : والصبي كفء بغنى أبيه وهو الأصح .اهـ. يعني بالنسبة إلى المهر، وأما في النفقة فلا يعد غنياً بغنى أبيه لأن العادة أن الآباء يتحملون المهر عن الأبناء ولا يتحملون النفقة. كذا في الذخيرة والواقعات . وفي التبيين : وقيل إن كان ذا جاه كالسلطان والعالم يكون كفئاً وإن لم يملك إلا النفقة لأن الخلل ينجبر به ومن ثم قالوا : الفقيه العجمي يكون كفئاً للعربي الجاهل اهـ. وظاهر كلامهم أن القدرة على المهر والنفقة لا بد منه في كل زوج عربياً كان أو عجمياً لكل امرأة ولو كانت فقيرة بنت فقراء كما صرح به في الواقعات معللاً بأن المهر والنفقة عليه فيعتبر هذا الوصف في حقه اهـ. ففي إدخال القدرة عليهما في الكفاءة إشكال لأن الكفاءة المماثلة، وهذا شرط في حق الزوج فقط لكن قدمنا أنها شرعاً المماثلة أو كون المرأة أدنى.
Regarding maintenance, it is said that maintenance of six months is considered. This is narrated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muntaqa from Muhammad, and in al-Khaniyyah and al-Tajnis it is narrated from some as maintenance of one year. They disagreed on the amount of six months' maintenance, and it is said one month's maintenance, and it was corrected in al-Tajnis. And in al-Mujtaba: The correct view is that if he is able to earn maintenance, he is compatible. So the correction differs, and the correction of al-Mujtaba is more apparent, as is not hidden. And in al-Dhakhirah: If he can afford her maintenance but not his own, he is compatible; if he cannot afford her maintenance, he is not compatible even if she is poor. If the wife is a minor who cannot bear intercourse, he is compatible even if he cannot afford maintenance because she has no maintenance. And in al-Mujtaba: A minor boy is compatible with the wealth of his father, and this is the most correct. This is regarding the mahr; as for maintenance, he is not considered wealthy by his father's wealth because customarily fathers bear the mahr for their sons but do not bear maintenance. So in al-Dhakhirah and al-Waqi'at. And in al-Tabyin: It is said that if he has status like a sultan or scholar, he is compatible even if he owns only enough for maintenance because the deficiency is compensated by it; hence they said: A non-Arab jurist is compatible for an ignorant Arab. The apparent meaning of their words is that ability for mahr and maintenance is necessary for every husband, Arab or non-Arab, for every woman even if she is poor, daughter of poor parents, as stated in al-Waqi'at, with the reasoning that mahr and maintenance are obligatory upon him, so this description is considered in his right. There is some issue in including ability for both in kafa'ah because kafa'ah means similarity, and this is a condition only for the husband, but we have stated that according to Sharia it is similarity or the woman being lower.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the condition of ability to pay mahr and maintenance in kafa'ah. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is commenting on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq which likely states that ability to pay is a condition. The commentary presents multiple opinions from the Hanafi school. The text begins by noting a difference: some say six months' maintenance, some say one year, some say one month. The author notes that the correction of al-Mujtaba takes precedence. Then it discusses scenarios: if he can afford her maintenance but not his own, he is compatible; if he cannot afford her maintenance, he is not, even if she is poor. For a minor wife who does not require maintenance, ability is not a condition. A minor boy is considered compatible through his father's wealth for mahr, but not for maintenance, as fathers customarily pay mahr but not maintenance. A person with social status like a sultan or scholar may be considered compatible even if he has only enough for maintenance, as his status compensates. The author concludes that the apparent view is that ability for both mahr and maintenance is required for every husband, regardless of the wife's status, though this seems problematic because kafa'ah is about similarity, but the condition is only on the husband.

Key Terms
الكفاءة (al-kafā'ah): Compatibility or suitability between spouses in specific qualities like lineage, religion, wealth, profession.
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, obligatory upon the husband for his wife.
المهر (al-mahr): The bridal gift (dower) given by the husband to the wife, obligatory in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He is not compatible under any condition
B) He is compatible because his status compensates for lack of wealth
C) He is compatible only if the wife is rich
D) He is compatible only if he can earn maintenance

Key Takeaway
Ability to pay mahr and maintenance is a wajib condition for kafa'ah, but the required amount is flexible; earning capacity and social status can satisfy the condition.

Compatibility in Profession (Hirfah)
Ruling with proof on profession compatibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compatibility in profession for marriage and apply the exception for close professions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi nikah, profession matters: base crafts disqualify, but close professions are compatible by custom.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author explains the sixth condition of kafa'ah (compatibility) in marriage: similarity in profession. He presents the Hanafi position that certain base professions (weaver, cupper, tanner, sweeper) are not compatible with higher ones, but under Abu Yusuf's view, professions that are close in status are considered compatible. This lesson will guide you through the proofs, the intra-madhhab dispute, and the practical application of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The sixth condition of kafa'ah is compatibility in profession. Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the husband's profession relative to the wife's family.
2
Locate the primary proof
A hadith (mursal) from Abu Hurairah is cited: 'People are compatible except a weaver, cupper, tanner, or sweeper.' This establishes that profession is a valid consideration.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The general rule is that people are compatible unless specified; profession is part of kafa'ah. The hadith exceptions indicate that base professions break compatibility with higher ones.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa based the ruling on Arab custom (disgrace of base crafts). Abu Yusuf later held that close professions (e.g., weaver with cupper) are compatible to avoid hardship.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, as stated by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, considering custom (urf) and istihsan. Local custom can even elevate a profession's status (e.g., weaver in Alexandria).

وأما السادس فالكفاءة في الحرفة - بالكسر - وهي كما في ضياء الحلوم بكسر الحاء وسكون الراء اسم من الاحتراف الاكتساب بالصناعة والتجارة. وقال في موضع آخر : الصناعة الحرفة اهـ. والظاهر أن الحرفة أعم من الصناعة لأنها العلم الحاصل من التمرن على العمل ولذا عبر المصنف بالحرفة دون الصناعة، لكن قال في القاموس : الحرفة بالكسر الطعمة والصناعة يرتزق منها وكل ما اشتغل الإنسان به وهي تسمى صنعة وحرفة لأنه ينحرف إليها .اهـ. فأفاد أنهما سواء. وقد حقق في غاية البيان أن اعتبار الكفاءة في الصنائع هو ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه. وقال أيضاً في البدائع : وأما الحرفة فقد ذكر الكرخي أن الكفاءة فيها معتبرة عند أبي يوسف، وذكر أن أبا حنيفة بنى الأمر فيها على عادة العرب أن مواليهم يعملون هذه ، على عادة أهل البلاد وأنهم يتخذون ذلك حرفة فيعيرون بالدنيء من الصنائع فلا يكون بينهم . ومقتضى هذا أن العرب إذا كانوا يحترفون بأنفسهم تعتبر فهم الكفاءة في الخرفة أيضاً. قلت . ولأن الناس يتفاخرون بشرف الحرف ويتعيرون بدناءتها وهي وإن أمكن تركها يبقى عارها كما في المجتبى. وفي الذخيرة معزياً إلى أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه : الناس بعضهم أكفاء لبعض إلا حائكاً أو حجاماً ـ وفي رواية ـ أو دباغاً. قال مشايخنا ورابعهم الكناس فواحد من هؤلاء الأربعة لا يكون كفئاً للصيرفي والجوهري وعليه الفتوى وبعد هذا المروي عن أبي يوسف أن الحرف متى تقاربت لا يعتبر التفاوت وتثبت الكفاءة، فالحائك يكون كفئاً للحجام، والدباغ يكون كفئاً للكناس، والصفار يكون كفئاً للحداد، والعطار يكون كفئاً للبزاز. قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : وعليه الفتوى .اهـ. فالمفتى به مخالفاً لما في المختصر لأن حقيقة الكفاءة في الصنائع لا تتحقق إلى بكونهما من صنعة واحدة إلا أن التقارب بمنزلة المماثلة فلا مخالفة. وفي فتح القدير : والحائك يكون كفئاً للعطار بالإسكندرية لما هناك من حسن اعتبارها و عدم عدها نقصاً ألبتة اللهم إلا أن يقترن بها خساسة غيرها .اهـ. وينبغي أن يكون صاحب الوظائف في الأوقاف كفئاً لبنت التاجر في إلا أن تكون وظيفة دنيئة عرفاً كسواق وفراس ووقاد وبواب وتكون الوظائف من الحرف لأنها صارت طريقاً للاكتساب في مصر كالصنائع اهـ. وينبغي أن من له وظيفة تدريس أو نظر يكون كفئاً لبنت الأمير بمصر. وفي القنية : الحائك لا يكون كفئاً لبنت الدهقان وإن كان معسراً، أو قيل هو . كفء اهـ. وفي المغرب: غلب اسم الدهقان على من له عقار كثيرة. وفي المجتبى: وهنا جنس أخس من الكل وهو الذي يخدم الظلمة يدعى شاكرياً وتابعاً وإن كان صاحب مروءة ومال فظلمه خساسة اهـ. وفي الظهيرية والشاكرية لا يكون كفئاً لأحد إلا لأمثالهم وهم الذين يتبعون هؤلاء المترفين. هكذا قاله شمس الأئمة الحلواني .اهـ. ولا يخفى أن الظاهر اعتبار هذه الكفاءة بين الزوج وأبيها وأن الظاهر اعتبارها وقت التزوج ، فلو كان دباغاً أولاً ثم صار تاجراً ثم تزوج بنت تاجر أصلي ينبغي أن يكون كفئاً لكن ما تقدم من أن الصنعة وإن أمكن تركها يبقى عارها يخالفه كما لا يخفى.
As for the sixth, it is compatibility in profession (al-hirfah, with kasr). It is, as in Diya' al-Hulum, with kasr of the ha and sukun of the ra, a noun from ihtiraf, earning by craft and trade. And he said in another place: al-sina'ah is al-hirfah. The apparent is that hirfah is more general than sina'ah because it is knowledge acquired by practice, so the author expressed it as hirfah rather than sina'ah. But al-Qamus said: al-hirfah is livelihood and craft by which one earns, and every occupation of man is called sin'ah and hirfah because he turns to it. So it indicates they are the same. And it has been verified in Ghayat al-Bayan that considering compatibility in crafts is the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa and his companions. And he also said in al-Bada'i: As for hirfah, al-Karkhi mentioned that compatibility in it is considered according to Abu Yusuf, and he mentioned that Abu Hanifa based the matter on the custom of the Arabs that their clients do these professions, according to the custom of the people of the land, and they take it as a profession, so they are disgraced by base crafts, so there is no compatibility between them. The implication of this is that if the Arabs themselves practice professions, then compatibility in profession is considered for them as well. I say: Because people boast about honorable professions and are disgraced by base ones, and even if they can leave it, its disgrace remains, as in al-Mujtaba. And in al-Dhakhirah, attributed to Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him): 'People are compatible with each other except a weaver or a cupper' and in one narration 'or a tanner.' Our scholars added a fourth: a sweeper. So one of these four is not compatible with a money-changer or a jeweler, and the fatwa is upon this. After this, it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that when professions are close, the difference is not considered and compatibility is established: a weaver is compatible with a cupper, a tanner with a sweeper, a brass-worker with a blacksmith, a perfumer with a clothier. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The fatwa is upon this. So the mufta bihi contradicts what is in al-Mukhtasar, because the reality of compatibility in crafts is not achieved unless they are of the same profession, but closeness is like similarity, so there is no contradiction. And in Fath al-Qadir: A weaver is compatible with a perfumer in Alexandria because of the good consideration of it there and it not being considered a deficiency at all, unless it is accompanied by baseness. It should be that holders of endowments (waqf) positions are compatible with a merchant's daughter, unless the position is base in custom, like water-carrier, groom, stoker, doorkeeper. And positions are considered professions because they have become a means of earning in Egypt like crafts. It should be that one who has a teaching or supervisory position is compatible with the daughter of an ameer in Egypt. And in al-Qunyah: A weaver is not compatible with a peasant's daughter even if he is poor, or it is said he is compatible. In al-Mughrib: The name 'dihqan' came to be applied to one who has much property. In al-Mujtaba: There is a base class lower than all, which is those who serve the oppressors, called shakiri and tabi', even if they have honor and wealth, their oppressing is baseness. In al-Zuhayriyyah: The shakiriyyah are not compatible with anyone except their likes, and they are those who follow these luxurious ones. This is what Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said. It is not hidden that the apparent is that this compatibility is considered between the husband and her father, and that it is considered at the time of marriage. So if he was a tanner first, then became a merchant, then married the daughter of an original merchant, it should be that he is compatible, but what was mentioned earlier that the profession even if it can be left, its disgrace remains, contradicts it, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the sixth condition of kafa'ah: compatibility in profession (al-hirfah). The commentator explains that hirfah and sina'ah are essentially the same. The authoritative narration (zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Hanifa and his companions considers profession in kafa'ah. Abu Yusuf explicitly states it, while Abu Hanifa's view is based on Arab custom where certain base professions cause disgrace. The text then presents a hadith from Abu Hurairah (RA) listing four base professions: weaver, cupper, tanner, and sweeper. These are not compatible with high professions like money-changer or jeweler. However, Abu Yusuf later said that close professions are compatible, e.g., a weaver with a cupper. The fatwa is on this more lenient view. The passage also considers regional customs: in Alexandria, a weaver is compatible with a perfumer because weaving is not seen as base there. Similarly, holders of waqf positions (teaching, supervision) are compatible with a merchant's daughter in Egypt, and teaching positions with an ameer's daughter. A special base class is those who serve oppressors (shakiri), they are only compatible with each other. The commentator notes that compatibility is considered at the time of marriage and with the wife's father. If a man had a base profession but later changed to a high one, there is a conflict: the disgrace of the former profession may persist. This shows the nuance in Hanafi fiqh regarding custom ('urf).

Key Terms
الحرفة (al-ḥirfah): Profession, craft, or occupation by which one earns a living, including trade and manufacturing.
الصناعة (al-ṣinā‘ah): Craft or trade, often synonymous with hirfah in this context.
الشاكرية (al-shākariyyah): A base class of people who serve oppressors, considered very low in compatibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following couples would likely be considered incompatible in terms of profession?
A) A weaver and a cupper's daughter
B) A tanner and a sweeper's daughter
C) A weaver and a money-changer's daughter
D) A brass-worker and a blacksmith's daughter

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, compatibility in profession is considered, but close professions are accepted, and local custom plays a decisive role.

Intellect in Kafa'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intellect as a condition of kafa'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the apparent Hanafi position on intellect in kafa'ah and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute that leads to a preferred fatwa considering intellect.

Core Idea
Though the six-list excludes intellect, later Hanafis consider it due to greater harm than poverty.

In this passage, the commentator of Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a subtle point: the author's list of six conditions for kafa'ah excludes intellect, implying a madman is compatible. However, a significant intra-Hanafi debate emerged, with many later scholars arguing that the harm caused by insanity outweighs poverty or base profession, and thus intellect should be considered. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the apparent position from the matn
The author of Kanz confined himself to six conditions; intellect is not among them, so the apparent ruling is that a madman is compatible.
This is the reading of the text at first glance.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi objection
Some scholars (e.g., author of al-Nahr) argue that intellect should be considered because insanity defeats the objectives of marriage and causes greater social stigma than poverty or a base profession.
The objection is based on harm (darar) and public interest (maslahah).
3
Analyze the dalil of the objectors
The objectors use a rational argument (dalil aqli) that the harm of insanity is more severe, so the omission of intellect from the list should be revisited.
Compare the strength of this argument to the literal text.
4
Compare with the view of al-Marghinani and other imams
Al-Marghinani in al-Binayah explicitly says a madman is not compatible. The other three imams consider insanity a defect that annuls the marriage, strengthening the case for considering intellect.
This cross-madhhab support influences the Hanafi tarjih.
5
Determine the preferred fatwa
The commentator recommends relying on the view that intellect is considered, and this is the mufta bihi among later Hanafis.
The authority_weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أشار المصنف باقتصاره على الأمور الستة إلى أنه لا غيرها فلا عبرة بالجمال كما في الخانية ولا يعتبر فيها العقل فالمجنون كفء للعاقلة وفيه اختلاف بين المشايخ قال في النهر : وقيل يعتبر لأنه يفوت مقاصد النكاح فكان أشد من الفقر ودناءة الحرفة وينبغي اعتماده لأن الناس يعيرون بتزويج المجنون أكثر من دنيء الحرفة الدنيئة. وفي البناية عن المرغيناني : لا يكون المجنون كفؤاً للعاقلة. وعند بقية الأئمة هو من العيو - التي ينفسخ بها النكاح .
And the author indicated by confining himself to the six matters that there is no other, so beauty is not considered as in al-Khaniyyah, and intellect is not considered in it, so a madman is compatible with a sane woman, but there is disagreement among the scholars. In al-Nahr it is said: It is considered because it defeats the objectives of marriage, so it is more severe than poverty and baseness of profession, and it should be relied upon because people are more disgraced by marrying a madman than by a low base profession. And in al-Binayah from al-Marghinani: A madman is not compatible with a sane woman. According to the other imams, it is among the defects that annul the marriage.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage addresses whether intellect ('aql) is a condition of kafa'ah. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq listed only six conditions (nasab, din, hurriyyah, yasar, hirfah, and presumably something else), implying that intellect is not considered. The commentator notes that beauty is also not considered. However, there is a dispute among Hanafi scholars. Some argue that intellect should be considered because a mad husband cannot fulfill the objectives of marriage, and the social stigma is greater than for a base profession. Al-Marghinani in al-Binayah explicitly states that a madman is not compatible with a sane woman. The passage also notes that according to the other three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), insanity is a defect that annuls the marriage itself. The commentator from al-Nahr recommends relying on the view that intellect is considered, given the harm.

Key Terms
المجنون (al-majnūn): A person who is insane, lacking sanity (aql).
العقل (al-‘aql): Intellect, mental capacity, sanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the view of the other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) regarding a madman's marriage?
A) They consider it a valid marriage
B) They consider insanity a defect that annuls the marriage
C) They agree with the Hanafi view that it is compatible
D) They consider it only if the wife is also mad

Key Takeaway
Though intellect is excluded from the six conditions of kafa'ah, the preferred Hanafi fatwa now considers it due to greater harm.

Compatibility in Occupation and the Six Matters
Explains the Hanafi criteria for compatibility in marriage, focusing on occupation and the six matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for compatibility (kafa'ah) in marriage regarding profession and identify which professions are considered incompatible.

Core Idea
Compatibility in profession is judged by customary honor; base crafts like weaving and cupping make a man incompatible with high-status professions.

In Hanafi nikah, compatibility (kafa'ah) is a right of the guardian, not a condition for validity. This lesson explores the detailed rulings on profession—one of the six matters—including which crafts are base, how approximate closeness can establish compatibility, and the disputed role of sanity. The source passage cites a hadith and the opinions of early Hanafi masters to guide the mufti in applying these criteria.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on profession
Determine that profession is one of the six matters of compatibility, and base professions (weaving, cupping, tanning, sweeping) render a man incompatible with high-status ones (money-changer, jeweler).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) excluding weaver, cupper, and tanner is the primary textual evidence.
Hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The exception in the hadith indicates that profession is a valid consideration for compatibility; the specific mention of base crafts shows they are not compatible with others.
The Hanafi scholars add a fourth: the sweeper.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and later Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani held that when crafts are close in honor (e.g., weaver and cupper), compatibility is established despite lack of identity.
This view is the relied-upon fatwa.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf's view of approximate closeness, overriding the stricter earlier view that only identical crafts are compatible.
The commentary also addresses changing professions and local custom (e.g., Alexandria, Egypt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن الناس يتفاخرون بشرف الحرف ويتعيرون بدناءتها وهي وإن أمكن تركها يبقى عارها كما في المجتبى. وفي الذخيرة معزياً إلى أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه : الناس بعضهم أكفاء لبعض إلا حائكاً أو حجاماً ـ وفي رواية ـ أو دباغاً. قال مشايخنا ورابعهم الكناس فواحد من هؤلاء الأربعة لا يكون كفئاً للصيرفي والجوهري وعليه الفتوى وبعد هذا المروي عن أبي يوسف أن الحرف متى تقاربت لا يعتبر التفاوت وتثبت الكفاءة، فالحائك يكون كفئاً للحجام، والدباغ يكون كفئاً للكناس، والصفار يكون كفئاً للحداد، والعطار يكون كفئاً للبزاز. قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : وعليه الفتوى .اهـ. فالمفتى به مخالفاً لما في المختصر لأن حقيقة الكفاءة في الصنائع لا تتحقق إلى بكونهما من صنعة واحدة إلا أن التقارب بمنزلة المماثلة فلا مخالفة. وفي فتح القدير : والحائك يكون كفئاً للعطار بالإسكندرية لما هناك من حسن اعتبارها و عدم عدها نقصاً ألبتة اللهم إلا أن يقترن بها خساسة غيرها .اهـ. وينبغي أن يكون صاحب الوظائف في الأوقاف كفئاً لبنت التاجر إلا أن تكون وظيفة دنيئة عرفاً كسواق وفراس ووقاد وبواب وتكون الوظائف من الحرف لأنها صارت طريقاً للاكتساب في مصر كالصنائع اهـ. وينبغي أن من له وظيفة تدريس أو نظر يكون كفئاً لبنت الأمير بمصر. وفي القنية : الحائك لا يكون كفئاً لبنت الدهقان وإن كان معسراً، أو قيل هو كفء اهـ. وفي المغرب: غلب اسم الدهقان على من له عقار كثيرة. وفي المجتبى: وهنا جنس أخس من الكل وهو الذي يخدم الظلمة يدعى شاكرياً وتابعاً وإن كان صاحب مروءة ومال فظلمه خساسة اهـ. وفي الظهيرية والشاكرية لا يكون كفئاً لأحد إلا لأمثالهم وهم الذين يتبعون هؤلاء المترفين. هكذا قاله شمس الأئمة الحلواني .اهـ. ولا يخفى أن الظاهر اعتبار هذه الكفاءة بين الزوج وأبيها وأن الظاهر اعتبارها وقت التزوج ، فلو كان دباغاً أولاً ثم صار تاجراً ثم تزوج بنت تاجر أصلي ينبغي أن يكون كفئاً لكن ما تقدم من أن الصنعة وإن أمكن تركها يبقى عارها يخالفه كما لا يخفى. وقد أشار المصنف باقتصاره على الأمور الستة إلى أنه لا غيرها فلا عبرة بالجمال كما في الخانية ولا يعتبر فيها العقل فالمجنون كفء للعاقلة وفيه اختلاف بين المشايخ قال في النهر : وقيل يعتبر لأنه يفوت مقاصد النكاح فكان أشد من الفقر ودناءة الحرفة وينبغي اعتماده لأن الناس يعيرون بتزويج المجنون أكثر من دنيء الحرفة الدنيئة. وفي البناية عن المرغيناني : لا يكون المجنون كفؤاً للعاقلة. وعند بقية الأئمة هو من العيوب التي يفسخ بها النكاح . وفي الذخيرة ولا عبرة بالبلد فالقروي كفء للمدني كما في فتح القدير. فعلى هذا التاجر في القرى يكون كفئاً لبنت التاجر في المصر للتقارب.
Because people boast about honorable crafts and are shamed by base ones, and even if one can leave it, its disgrace remains as in al-Mujtaba. In al-Dhakhira, attributed to Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him): 'People are compatible with each other except a weaver or a cupper' – in another narration – 'or a tanner.' Our scholars said: a fourth is a sweeper; so one of these four is not compatible with a money-changer or jeweler, and on this is the fatwa. After this, it is reported from Abu Yusuf that when crafts are close, disparity is not considered and compatibility is established: a weaver is compatible with a cupper, a tanner with a sweeper, a brass-smith with a blacksmith, a perfumer with a clothier. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: and on this is the fatwa. So the relied-upon view contradicts what is in al-Mukhtasar because the reality of compatibility in crafts is only achieved by being from the same craft, but closeness is like equality, so no contradiction. In Fath al-Qadir: a weaver is compatible with a perfumer in Alexandria because of the good estimation there and it being not considered a defect at all, unless it is accompanied by baseness of another kind. It is fitting that the holder of waqf positions should be compatible with the daughter of a merchant unless the job is base by custom like a water-carrier, overseer, stoker, or gatekeeper, and such jobs are considered crafts because they have become a means of earning in Egypt like crafts. It is fitting that one with a teaching or supervisory position is compatible with the daughter of a prince in Egypt. In al-Qunyah: a weaver is not compatible with the daughter of a landholder even if he is wealthy, or it is said he is compatible. In al-Maghrib: the name 'landholder' is dominant for one with many properties. In al-Mujtaba: here is a class baser than all, which is one who serves the oppressors, called 'shakiri' and 'tabi'' even if he is dignified and wealthy, for oppression is baseness. In al-Dhahiriyyah: the shakiri are not compatible with anyone except their likes, and they are those who follow these affluent ones. Thus said Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. It is not hidden that apparently this compatibility is between the husband and her father, and apparently it is considered at the time of marriage. So if one was a tanner first, then became a merchant, then married the daughter of an original merchant, it is fitting that he is compatible, but what preceded about the craft, even if possible to leave, its disgrace remains, contradicts this. The author indicated by limiting to six matters that there is nothing else, so beauty is not considered as in al-Khaniyya, nor is intelligence considered, so a mad person is compatible with a sane one, but there is a difference among the scholars. In al-Nahr: it is said it is considered because it defeats the purposes of marriage, so it is more severe than poverty and baseness of craft, and it should be relied upon because people are more disgraced by marrying a mad person than by a base craft. In al-Binaya from al-Marghinani: a mad person is not compatible with a sane one. According to the other imams, it is among the defects that invalidate marriage. In al-Dhakhira: there is no consideration of locality, so a villager is compatible with a city dweller as in Fath al-Qadir. According to this, a trader in a village is compatible with the daughter of a trader in the city due to closeness.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the criteria for compatibility (kafa'ah) in marriage according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by explaining that people take pride in honorable professions and are shamed by base ones, and even if a person abandons a lowly craft, its stigma remains. He then cites a hadith from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) stating that people are compatible except for weavers, cuppers, and tanners. The Hanafi scholars add a fourth: the sweeper (kannas). These four are not compatible with a money-changer or jeweler, and this is the fatwa. However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that when crafts are close in honor, disparity is not considered; for example, a weaver is compatible with a cupper, a tanner with a sweeper, etc. The later Hanafi master Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani confirms that the fatwa is on this view of approximate equivalence, not strict identity. The passage then discusses specific applications: in Alexandria, weavers are considered compatible with perfumers because the craft is not viewed as base; in Egypt, holders of waqf positions like teachers are compatible with princes' daughters, and those with lowly positions (e.g., doorkeeper) are not. The text also addresses the issue of a person changing professions: if a tanner becomes a merchant, he should be compatible with the daughter of an original merchant, but the lasting stigma of his former craft contradicts this. The author then mentions that the matn limited compatibility to six matters: lineage, freedom, religion, wealth, craft, and sanity? Actually, the text says the author (of Kanz) limited to six matters, but then it discusses that beauty is not considered, and there is disagreement about sanity. The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that sanity is not a criterion for compatibility, so a mad man is compatible with a sane woman, but some scholars like al-Marghinani consider it a defect. Finally, locality is not a factor: a villager is compatible with a city dweller, so a trader in a village is compatible with the daughter of a city trader due to closeness in status.

Key Terms
الكفاءة (al-kafā’a): Compatibility or suitability between spouses in certain attributes (lineage, religion, wealth, profession, etc.) giving the guardian a right to object.
الصنعة (al-ṣan‘a): Profession or craft; one of the six matters of compatibility. Lowly professions (weaving, cupping, tanning, sweeping) are considered incompatible with high ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, which of the following is true regarding compatibility in profession?
A) A weaver is never compatible with any other profession.
B) Only identical professions are considered compatible.
C) Approximate closeness in honor of the profession establishes compatibility.
D) The guardian cannot object based on profession.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi nikah, compatibility in profession is judged by customary honor; base crafts like weaving and cupping are incompatible with high-status professions, but approximate closeness in honor can establish compatibility.

Compatibility and Physical Defects
Ruling that physical defects do not affect compatibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that physical defects do not affect compatibility and distinguish this from the option of defects (khiyar al-'ayb).

Core Idea
A guardian cannot object to a marriage due to the husband's physical defect; compatibility and defects are separate issues.

The Hanafi school holds that compatibility (kafa'ah) is not considered in terms of freedom from physical defects such as leprosy or madness. This means a guardian cannot invalidate a marriage on the grounds that the husband has such a defect. However, the wife retains the right to annul the marriage under the option of defects, which will be discussed later. In this lesson, we examine the legal principle and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: compatibility is not considered regarding freedom from physical defects.
2
List the defects mentioned
The passage lists leprosy, madness, vitiligo, halitosis, and foul odor. Note that these are serious defects that would void a sale but do not affect compatibility.
3
Understand the scope
Compatibility (kafa'ah) is about the guardian's right to object; it is separate from the wife's right to annul for defects (khiyar al-'ayb).
4
Distinguish from khiyar al-'ayb
The wife can still annul the marriage if she discovers a defect, but the guardian cannot object on those grounds.
5
Note the authority
The ruling is from the Hanafi school; the phrase 'at our school' indicates it is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تعتبر الكفاءة عندنا في السلامة من العيوب التي يفسخ بها البيع كالجذام والجنون والبرص والبخر والدفر كما سيأتي، ولا تعتبر الكفاءة بين أهل الذمة، فلو زوجت نفسها فقال وليها ليس هذا كفئاً لم يفرق بل هم أكفاء بعضهم لبعض . قال في الأصل إلا أن يكون نسباً مشهوراً كبنت ملك من ملوكهم خدعها حائك أو سائس فإنه يفرق بينهم لا لعدم الكفاءة بل لتسكين الفتنة والقاضي مأمور بتسكينها بينهم كما بين المسلمين .
Compatibility is not considered in our school regarding freedom from defects that give the right of annulment in sale, such as leprosy, madness, vitiligo, halitosis, and foul odor, as will come. Nor is compatibility considered among the People of the Covenant (dhimmis). So if a woman marries herself and her guardian says, 'He is not compatible,' they are not separated; rather, they are compatible with each other. In al-Asl, unless it is a famous lineage, such as the daughter of a king among their kings who is deceived by a weaver or a groom, then they are separated between them, not for lack of compatibility, but to calm strife, and the judge is commanded to calm strife among them as among Muslims.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage clarifies two important points about compatibility (kafa'ah) in Hanafi fiqh. First, compatibility is not considered in the context of physical defects that would otherwise give the right of annulment in a sale contract. The defects listed—leprosy, madness, vitiligo, halitosis, and foul odor—are serious, yet they do not affect compatibility. This means a person with such a defect is still considered compatible with a healthy person in terms of the guardian's right to object; the right to annul the marriage on grounds of these defects is a separate matter (it will be discussed later in the book). Second, compatibility is not considered among non-Muslims (dhimmis). If a dhimmi woman marries herself, her guardian cannot object on grounds of incompatibility. However, there is an exception from the book al-Asl: if the woman is from a very famous noble lineage (e.g., the daughter of a king) and she is deceived into marrying a lowly weaver or groom, the judge may separate them—not because of incompatibility, but to prevent public strife and scandal. The judge is commanded to prevent fitna (social disorder) among them just as among Muslims.

Key Terms
كفاءة (kafa'ah): Compatibility in marriage, considered in terms of lineage, religion, profession, etc., but not in physical defects per Hanafi law.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to annul a marriage due to a defect discovered after the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true regarding compatibility (kafa'ah) in the Hanafi school?
A) It is considered in freedom from defects.
B) It is not considered in freedom from defects.
C) It is only considered among dhimmis.
D) It is always required.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi marriage law, physical defects do not affect compatibility; a guardian cannot object on that basis, but the wife may have an independent right to annul the marriage.

Compatibility Among Dhimmis and the Exception for Fitna
Ruling on compatibility among dhimmis and the exceptional case for famous lineage to prevent fitna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that dhimmis are compatible with each other, and identify the exceptional case where the judge may separate them to prevent fitna.

Core Idea
Dhimmis are compatible with each other; only a dangerously unequal match may be annulled to prevent public scandal.

The second part of the passage addresses compatibility among non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis). Generally, in Hanafi law, dhimmis are considered compatible with each other, so a guardian cannot object to a marriage on grounds of lineage or status. However, there is an important exception: if the woman is from a notably famous noble family (e.g., a king's daughter) and she marries a lowly weaver or groom, the judge may annul the marriage to prevent social disorder (fitna). This exception is not based on incompatibility but on the judge's duty to maintain public order.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Compatibility is not considered among dhimmis; they are compatible with each other.
2
Explain the effect
A guardian cannot object, and the marriage is valid even if the husband is of lower status.
3
Identify the exception
From al-Asl: if the wife is from a famous lineage (e.g., a king's daughter) and she is deceived by a lowly man (weaver/groom), the judge may separate them.
4
Understand the basis
The annulment is not for lack of compatibility but to prevent fitna (public disorder).
5
Note the judge's authority
The judge is commanded to calm fitna among dhimmis as among Muslims.

Guardian's Right to Annul for Inadequate Mahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardian's right to annul for low mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a guardian can annul a marriage or demand completion of the mahr when it is less than mahr al-mithl, and identify the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Guardians can annul a marriage or complete the mahr if it is below the proper amount—but only before consummation.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the guardian's authority when a woman marries for a mahr less than her proper mahr (mahr al-mithl). The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq gives Abu Hanifa's view that the guardian may separate the couple or complete the mahr. The Sahibayn disagree, arguing that any amount above the minimum (ten dirhams) is the woman's exclusive right. We will explore each side's evidence (qiyas) and the practical effects of their disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what right the guardian is claiming and under what condition (mahr less than mahr al-mithl).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its proof
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas: just as guardians have a right in compatibility (kafa'ah) because they are shamed by a mismatch, they have a right here because they are shamed by a low mahr.
The key analogy: kafa'ah → low mahr.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that any mahr above ten dirhams is the woman's property. If she waives her right, no one can object—similar to a creditor's remission after specification.
Analogy: ibra' (remission) after specification.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that disgrace (shame) is real for the guardian, unlike the impersonal remission of a debt. Hence the guardian's right is preserved.
Distinguishing factor: shame vs. mere financial right.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the guardian annuls before consummation, marriage ends with no mahr; after consummation, mahr is due. Under Sahibayn's view, no annulment possible.
Also, if one dies before annulment, guardian cannot demand completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو نقصت عن مهر مثلها للولي أن يفرق بينهم أو يتم المهر) يعني عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : ليس له ذلك لأن ما زاد عن العشرة حقها ومن أسقط حقه لا يعترض عليه كما في الإبراء بعد التسمية. ولأبي حنيفة أن الأولياء يفتخرون بغلاء المهر ويتعيرون بنقصانها فأشبه الكفاءة بخلاف الإبراء بعد التسمية لأنه لا يعير به، فحاصله أن في المهر حقوقاً ثلاثة : أحدها حق الشرع وهو أن لا يكون أقل من عشرة دراهم أو ما يساويها والثاني حق الأولياء أن لا يكون أقل من مهر المثل. والثالث حق المرأة وهو كونه ملكاً لها. ثم حق الشرع والأولياء مراعى وقت الثبوت فقط فلا حق لهما حالة البقاء. وأفاد بقوله «للولي أن يفرق» أن الولي لو فرق بينهما قبل الدخول فلا مهر لها وإن كان بعده فلها المسمى، وكذا إذا مات أحدهما قبل التفريق فليس لهم المطالبة بالتكميل لأن الثابت لهم ليس إلا أن يفسخ أو يكمل، هنا فإذا امتنع عن تكميل المهر لا يمكن الفسخ وإن طلقها الزوج قبل تفريق الولي قبل الدخول فلها نصف المسمى كما في الميحط . والمراد من الولي هنا العصبة وإن لم يكن محرماً على المختار كما قدمناه في الكفاءة فخرج القريب الذي ليس بعصبة، وخرج القاضي فلذا قال في الذخيرة من كتاب الحجر المحجور عليها : إذا تزوجت بأقل من مهر مثلها ليس للقاضي الاعتراض عليها لأن الحجر في المال لا في النفس اهـ.
His saying: 'And if it is less than her proper mahr (mahr al-mithl), the guardian may separate them or complete the mahr' means according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not have that because what is more than ten dirhams is her right, and the one who drops his right cannot be objected to, as in remission after specification. For Abu Hanifa, the guardians take pride in a high mahr and are shamed by its deficiency, so it resembles compatibility, unlike remission after specification because one is not disgraced by it. So the summary is that in mahr there are three rights: first the right of the Law, which is that it should not be less than ten dirhams or its equivalent; second, the right of the guardians, that it should not be less than the proper mahr; third, the right of the woman, that it becomes her property. Then the right of the Law and the guardians are considered only at the time of establishment, so they have no right at the time of continuation. His saying 'the guardian may separate' indicates that if the guardian separates them before consummation, there is no mahr for her, and if after consummation, she gets the specified mahr. Likewise, if one of them dies before separation, they cannot demand completion because what is established for them is only to annul or complete; here, if he refuses to complete the mahr, annulment is impossible; and if the husband divorces her before the guardian's separation before consummation, she gets half of the specified mahr as in al-Muhit. What is meant by 'guardian' here is the 'asaba (agnate) even if not a mahram according to the chosen view, as we mentioned in compatibility, so a relative who is not an 'asaba is excluded, and the judge is excluded; hence al-Dhakhira said in the chapter of interdiction: if a woman under interdiction marries for less than her proper mahr, the judge cannot object because interdiction is over wealth, not the person.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the guardian's right to annul a marriage or demand completion of the mahr when the woman marries for a mahr less than her proper mahr (mahr al-mithl). The text quotes the matn of Kanz: 'If it is less than her proper mahr, the guardian may separate them or complete the mahr.' The commentator explains that this is the position of Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that the guardian has no such right because any amount above the minimum (ten dirhams) is the woman's right, and if she waives her right, no one can object, analogous to a creditor remitting a debt after it is specified. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that guardians take pride in a high mahr and are shamed by a low one, so the issue resembles compatibility (kafa'ah) which gives the guardian a right to object. The passage then analyzes the mahr as having three rights: (1) the right of the Sharia that the mahr be at least ten dirhams, (2) the right of the guardians that it be at least the proper mahr, and (3) the right of the woman that it become her property. However, the rights of the Sharia and the guardians are only considered at the time of the contract; once the marriage is established, they do not persist. Thus, if the guardian separates before consummation, the woman gets no mahr; after consummation, she gets the specified mahr. If one dies before separation, the guardian cannot demand completion. If the husband divorces before consummation and before the guardian's separation, the woman gets half the specified mahr. The guardian referred to here is the 'asaba (agnate relative) according to the chosen view, not a non-'asaba relative or the judge. The judge cannot object because his interdiction over her wealth does not extend to her person.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr of a woman of similar status (family, beauty, etc.) in her locality.
العصبة (al-‘aṣaba): Agnate relatives (those related through males) who have the right of guardianship in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the basis for the guardian's right to annul the marriage if the mahr is less than the proper amount?
A) The woman's right to a fair mahr is being violated.
B) The guardian is responsible for the woman's financial welfare.
C) The guardians are shamed by a low mahr, similar to compatibility.
D) The Sharia requires a minimum mahr of ten dirhams.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa grants the guardian a right to annul or complete the mahr if it is less than mahr al-mithl, but this right is limited to the time of the contract and can be lost by certain events.

Marriage of a Minor: Father’s Authority vs. the Minor’s Interest
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a minor's marriage by a father or grandfather when there is incompatibility or gross fraud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of a minor's marriage by the father in cases of incompatibility or gross fraud, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, the father’s guardianship is unconditional; for the Sahibayn, it is limited by the child’s interest.

In Hanafi law, a father has broad authority to marry off his minor child. But what if he arranges a marriage that seems disadvantageous—such as marrying his daughter to a slave or accepting a grossly deficient mahr? The classical Hanafi masters disagreed. This lesson unpacks the debate between Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as recorded in the commentary of al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The contested case: a father marries his minor child to someone incompatible (e.g., a slave) or with a grossly unfair mahr. Does the marriage hold?
The same question applies to the grandfather, who shares the father's authority.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position
Abu Hanifa rules that the marriage is valid and binding, regardless of incompatibility or fraud. He views the father’s guardianship as absolute.
This is the view presented in the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq: 'صح' (it is valid).
3
State the Sahibayn’s counter-position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the marriage is not valid because guardianship is conditional on acting in the minor’s best interest; gross fraud or incompatibility violates that condition.
The commentary indicates their view is 'الأصح' (the more correct) in later Hanafi scholarship.
4
Analyze the underlying reasoning
Abu Hanifa relies on the father's presumed love and foresight; the Sahibayn insist on an objective standard of benefit, likening the guardian’s role to a trustee.
The dispute is essentially about the extent of paternal authority (wilaya).
5
Extract the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the marriage stands, and the minor cannot later object. Under the Sahibayn, the marriage is invalid, and the minor (upon majority) can seek annulment.
This affects whether the minor has a right to void the marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو زوج طفله غير كفء أو بغبن فاحش صح ولم يجز ذلك لغير الأب والجد) يعني لو زوج الأب الصاحي ولده الصغير أمة أو بنته الصغيرة عبداً أو زوجه وزاد على مهر المثل زيادة فاحشة أو زوجها ونقص عن مهر مثلها نقصاناً فاحشاً فهو صحيح من الأب والجد دون غيرهما عند أبي حنيفة ولم يصح العقد عندهما على الأصح لأن الولاية مقيدة بشرط قوله (يعني لو زوج الأب الصاحي) قال الرملي : لو زاد على هذا الذي لم يعرف بسوء الاختيار لكان أولى كما سيظهر مما يأتي قوله (ولم يصح العقد عندهما على الأصح لأن الولاية الخ) قال في النهر : هذا موافق لما قدمناه عن المحيط وغيره من اعتبار الكفاءة في جانبها مخالف لما مر عن الخبازية من عدم اعتبارها عند الكل. قال في الحواشي السعدية ولعلهما يعتبران الكفاءة بالحرية من جانبها
His saying: 'And if he marries his child to someone incompatible or with gross fraud, it is valid, but that is not permissible for other than the father and grandfather' means: if a sane father marries his young son to a slave woman or his young daughter to a slave, or marries his son and increases the mahr grossly, or marries his daughter and decreases from her proper mahr grossly, it is valid from the father and grandfather but not from others according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (the Sahibayn), the contract is not valid on the correct view because the guardianship is conditional. His saying (meaning if the sane father marries...) al-Ramli said: if he increases beyond what is known without bad choice, it would be better. His saying (and the contract is not valid according to them on the correct view because the guardianship is conditional) - al-Nahr said: this is in agreement with what we presented from al-Muhit and others regarding considering compatibility in her side, contrary to what passed from al-Khabbazi regarding not considering it at all. In al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya: perhaps they consider compatibility in freedom from her side.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the marriage of a minor (child) by a guardian other than the father or grandfather. The matn states: 'If he marries his child to someone incompatible or with gross fraud, it is valid, but that is not permissible for other than the father and grandfather.' The commentator explains that if the father (who is sane) marries his son to a slave woman or his daughter to a slave, or makes a grossly disproportionate mahr (overpaying for the son or underpaying for the daughter), the marriage is valid when performed by the father or grandfather. However, other guardians (e.g., a brother or uncle) cannot do so. According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage by a non-father guardian is still valid? Actually the matn says 'it is valid' from the father and grandfather, implying that from others it is not valid. The Sahibayn go further: they say even the father's contract would not be valid if it is grossly disadvantageous? Actually the text says 'لم يصح العقد عندهما على الأصح' meaning the contract is not valid according to them (Sahibayn) on the correct view. So the dispute is: Abu Hanifa says the father's contract is valid even with gross fraud, while the Sahibayn say it is not valid because the guardian's authority is conditional upon acting in the child's best interest. The passage references al-Ramli, al-Nahr, and al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya to clarify that the Sahibayn consider compatibility (especially freedom) from the side of the minor, but Abu Hanifa does not require that when the father acts. The commentary is cut off but indicates the difference stems from the extent of the guardian's authority.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): Gross fraud or disproportion in the mahr, where the difference between the specified mahr and the proper mahr is excessive.
الولاية (al-wilāya): Guardianship over a minor, which gives the guardian the right to contract marriage on the minor's behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Sahibayn's view on the marriage of a minor by the father if there is gross fraud in the mahr?
A) The marriage is valid but the minor can object upon majority.
B) The marriage is invalid because guardianship is conditional.
C) The marriage is valid only if the mahr is corrected.
D) The marriage is void ab initio only if the father was insane.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa upholds the father's absolute authority; the Sahibayn require the marriage to serve the minor's interest, making grossly disadvantageous contracts invalid.
