Wali's Right to Annul Due to Deficient Mahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wali's right regarding deficient mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the wali's right to annul marriage due to deficient mahr and identify the internal dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A deficient mahr gives the wali a right to annul or demand completion, per Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a key issue in Hanafi marriage law: what happens when the mahr specified is less than mahr al-mithl? The text presents the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and records the dissent of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Understanding this internal ikhtilaf is essential for grasping the full range of Hanafi positions on guardianship rights in marriage.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and identify the ikhtilaf
Read the passage to find the core ruling: the wali can annul or demand completion if mahr is less than mahr al-mithl. Note that this is attributed to Abu Hanifa, and there is a difference among the mashayikh.
The ruling is presented as the matn, but the commentator clarifies it is according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Explain Abu Hanifa's dalil
Identify the reasoning: guardians take pride in high mahr and are shamed by deficiency, analogous to kafa'ah. The text compares it to compatibility (kafa'ah) where guardians’ honor is considered.
The analogy is to kafa'ah, not to the woman's right.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's dalil
Find the opposing argument: the amount above ten dirhams is the woman's right; she can waive it, as in absolution after specification (ibra' after tashmiya). Therefore, the wali has no right to object.
The Sahibayn focus on the woman's ownership of the mahr above the minimum.
4
Identify the thamara al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the wali can annul before consummation; under the Sahibayn, he cannot. Also note the time limitation: the wali's right exists only at the time of contract, not after establishment.
The passage also mentions that if one party dies before separation, the wali cannot claim completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيهما كالآباء وديانة ومالاً وحرفة ولو نقصت من مهر مثلها فللولي أن يفرق بينهم أو يتم المهر وهذا اختلاف بين المشايخ كما في الذخيرة ولا عبرة بالبلد فالقروي كفء للمدني كما في فتح القدير. فعلى هذا التاجر في القرى يكون كفئاً لبنت التاجر في المصر للتقارب. ولا تعتبر الكفاءة عندنا في السلامة من العيوب التي يفسخ بها البيع كالجذام والجنون والبرص والبخر والدفر كما سيأتي، ولا تعتبر الكفاءة بين أهل الذمة، فلو زوجت نفسها فقال وليها ليس هذا كفئاً لم يفرق بل هم أكفاء بعضهم لبعض . قال في الأصل إلا أن يكون نسباً مشهوراً كبنت ملك من ملوكهم خدعها حائك أو سائس فإنه يفرق بينهم لا لعدم الكفاءة بل لتسكين الفتنة والقاضي مأمور بتسكينها بينهم كما بين المسلمين . وهوقوله : (ولو نقصت عن مهر مثلها للولي أن يفرق بينهم أو يتم المهر) يعني عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : ليس له ذلك لأن ما زاد عن العشرة حقها ومن أسقط حقه لا يعترض عليه كما في الإبراء بعد التسمية. ولأبي حنيفة أن الأولياء يفتخرون بغلاء المهر ويتعيرون بنقصانها فأشبه الكفاءة بخلاف الإبراء بعد التسمية لأنه لا يعير به، فحاصله أن في المهر حقوقاً ثلاثة : أحدها حق الشرع وهو أن لا يكون أقل من عشرة دراهم أو ما يساويها والثاني حق الأولياء أن لا يكون أقل من مهر المثل. والثالث حق المرأة وهو كونه ملكاً لها. ثم حق الشرع والأولياء مراعى وقت الثبوت فقط فلا حق لهما حالة .البقاء. وأفاد بقوله «للولي أن يفرق» أن الولي لو فرق بينهما قبل الدخول فلا مهر لها وإن كان بعده فلها المسمى، وكذا إذا مات أحدهما قبل التفريق فليس لهم المطالبة بالتكميل لأن الثابت لهم ليس إلا أن يفسخ أو يكمل، هنا فإذا امتنع عن تكميل المهر لا يمكن الفسخ وإن طلقها الزوج قبل تفريق الولي قبل الدخول فلها نصف المسمى كما في الميحط . والمراد من الولي هنا العصبة وإن لم يكن محرماً على المختار كما قدمناه في الكفاءة فخرج القريب الذي ليس بعصبة، وخرج القاضي فلذا قال في الذخيرة من كتاب الحجر المحجور عليها : إذا تزوجت بأقل من مهر مثلها ليس للقاضي الاعتراض عليها لأن الحجر في المال لا في النفس اهـ.
In both, like fathers, religion, wealth, and profession. And if it is less than her mahr al-mithl, then the guardian has the right to separate between them or complete the mahr. This is a difference among the mashayikh as in al-Dhakhira. And no consideration is given to the city, so a villager is compatible with a city dweller as in Fath al-Qadir. So on this, a merchant in the village is compatible with the daughter of a merchant in the city due to proximity. And compatibility is not considered with us in freedom from defects that nullify a sale, like leprosy, madness, leukoderma, halitosis, and fetid sweat, as will come. And compatibility is not considered among the People of the Dhimmah, so if she marries herself and her guardian says this is not compatible, they are not separated; rather they are compatible with each other. He said in al-Asl: unless it is a famous lineage, like the daughter of a king of their kings that a weaver or groom deceived, then they are separated, not due to lack of compatibility but to calm discord, and the judge is ordered to calm it among them as among Muslims. And his saying: (And if it is less than mahr al-mithl, the guardian has the right to separate or complete the mahr) meaning according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two companions) said: He does not have that because what exceeds ten is her right, and whoever drops his right is not objected to, as in absolution after specification. And for Abu Hanifa, the guardians take pride in high mahr and are shamed by its deficiency, so it resembles compatibility, unlike absolution after specification because he is not shamed by it. So the essence is that in mahr there are three rights: first, the right of the Shari'ah, which is that it should not be less than ten dirhams or its equivalent; second, the right of the guardians, that it should not be less than mahr al-mithl; third, the right of the woman, that it is her ownership. Then the right of the Shari'ah and the guardians is observed only at the time of establishment, so they have no right in the state of remaining. And his saying 'the guardian has the right to separate' indicates that if the guardian separates before consummation, then there is no mahr for her; and if after, then she has the specified mahr. Similarly, if one of them dies before separation, they do not have the right to demand completion, because what is established for them is only to annul or complete; so if he refuses to complete the mahr, annulment is not possible. And if the husband divorces her before separation by the guardian, before consummation, then she has half the specified mahr, as in al-Muhit. And by guardian here is meant the عصبة (agnatic relatives), even if not a mahram according to the preferred view, as we have mentioned in compatibility; so the relative who is not an asabah is excluded, and the judge is excluded. Hence it is said in al-Dhakhira from the book of interdiction: 'If a woman under interdiction marries for less than her mahr al-mithl, the judge has no objection against her because interdiction is in wealth, not in person.' End.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the wali's right regarding the mahr when it is less than mahr al-mithl. The author begins by stating generally that if the mahr is deficient, the wali may annul or demand completion. He notes that this is a point of ikhtilaf among later scholars. Then he clarifies that compatibility is not considered in defects that nullify a sale, and among dhimmis, except to prevent fitna. The core ruling is that according to Abu Hanifa, the wali (who is an agnate) has the right to separate the couple or demand completion of the mahr to mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree: they hold that the wali has no such right because the amount above ten dirhams is the woman's right, and she may waive it. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that guardians are concerned with the honor of the family; a low mahr brings shame, similar to the consideration of kafa'ah. The text then details the three rights in mahr: the right of the Shari'ah (minimum ten dirhams), the right of the guardians (mahr al-mithl), and the right of the woman (ownership). The timing of exercising these rights is explained: the wali's right exists only at the time of contract; once the marriage is established, he cannot later demand completion. The commentary also clarifies that if the wali annuls before consummation, no mahr is due; if after, the specified mahr is due. If one party dies before separation, the wali cannot claim completion. The term 'wali' here refers to the عصبة (agnatic relatives), not the judge or non-agnatic relatives. This indicates that the judge does not have the authority to object even if the woman is under interdiction, because the interdiction pertains to wealth, not personal freedom.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower appropriate for a woman of her status, considering family, beauty, etc.
كفاءة (kafa'ah): Compatibility in marriage, considering lineage, religion, wealth, and profession.
ولي (wali): Guardian for marriage; here specifically the عصبة (agnatic relatives).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what right does the wali have if the mahr is less than mahr al-mithl?
A) The wali can only demand completion of the mahr, not annul.
B) The wali can annul the marriage or demand completion of the mahr.
C) The wali has no right to interfere; the woman's consent suffices.
D) The wali can only annul the marriage, not demand completion.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa grants the wali the right to annul or demand completion of mahr to mahr al-mithl, a right the Sahibayn deny; the relied-upon view in the madhhab is Abu Hanifa's.

Nikah — Marriage

Father's Authority to Marry a Minor with Disparity
Explains a special rule with an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the father and grandfather may marry a minor with incompatibility or excessive dower, and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
The father's love compensates for financial loss in marriage, making the contract valid despite disparity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a special rule: a father or grandfather may marry his minor child to a non-compatible person or with an excessive dower, whereas other guardians cannot. This ruling is based on closeness of kinship and the higher objectives of marriage, but it is not absolute—the father must not be known for bad judgment. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, arguing that guardianship requires sound judgment and that its absence invalidates the contract regardless of kinship. We will unpack the reasoning, the dispute, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its scope
Identify the act: father/grandfather marrying a minor child. Note the ruling: valid even with incompatibility (non-kufu') or excessive dower (ghaban fahish). Contrast with other guardians, for whom it is invalid.
The text explicitly excludes other guardians.
2
Trace the evidence for the ruling
Abu Hanifa's proof: the father/grandfather has 'close kinship' which is evidence of sound judgment (nazar). Also, marriage has higher objectives (maqasid) that outweigh financial loss.
This is a 'talil' argument focused on the underlying rationale.
3
Identify the opposing position
The Sahibayn argue that guardianship is always conditioned by sound judgment. If that is absent (as with disparity), the contract is invalid for any guardian, including father and grandfather.
Their position is based on strict application of the condition.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the father and grandfather are presumed to have sound judgment due to their natural affection. This presumption can be rebutted only if the father is known for bad judgment (su' al-ikhtiyar). The passage later adds that this bad judgment must be manifested (e.g., marrying to a known evil person).
Thus the ruling is not absolute; it depends on the guardian's character.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa's view, the marriage is valid even with disparity, while under the Sahibayn it is invalid. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's, but with the added condition that the father not be known for bad judgment.
This lesson shows how Hanafi fiqh balances authority and welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو زوج طفله غير كفء أو بغبن فاحش صح ولم يجز ذلك لغير الأب والجد) يعني لو زوج الأب الصاحي ولده الصغير أمة أو بنته الصغيرة عبداً أو زوجه وزاد على مهر المثل زيادة فاحشة أو زوجها ونقص عن مهر مثلها الناس فيه أي ما يغبن فيه بعضهم بعضاً بأن يتحملوه ولا يعده كل أحد غبناً بخلاف الفاحش وهو ما لا يتغابن الناس فيه. قال في الجوهرة: والذي يتغابن فيه في النكاح ما دون نصف المهر . كذا قال شيخنا موفق الدين، وقيل ما دون العشر اهـ. فعلى الثاني نقصان المائة يسير، ونقصان عشرة منها فاحش وعلى الأول نقصان تسعة وأربعين من المائة و نقصان خمسين فاحش والأقرب القول الثاني كما لا يخفى .اهـ. تأمل قوله ( وقيده الشارحون His saying: (And if he marries his child to an incompatible person or with excessive dower, it is valid and that is not permissible for other than the father and grandfather) meaning if the judicious father marries his minor son to a slave woman or his minor daughter to a slave, or marries him and increases beyond mahr al-mithl excessively, or marries her and decreases from her mahr al-mithl excessively, then it is valid from the father and grandfather but not from others according to Abu Hanifa, and the contract is not valid according to them (the two companions) in the most correct view, because guardianship is conditioned by consideration; so when it is absent, the contract is invalid. And for him, the ruling is based on evidence of consideration, which is closeness of kinship, and in marriage there are objectives that outweigh the dower and compatibility. It is restricted by excessive dower because minor dower in mahr is forgiven by agreement. As in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is restricted to marriage because in financial transactions like sale, purchase, lease, hire, and settlement in a claim of wealth, the father and grandfather do not have the right to transact with excessive dower by consensus, because the objective is wealth and loss has occurred without compensation, so it is not permissible. In marriage, compensation is found, which is the objectives. And he (the author) left it unrestricted regarding the father and grandfather, but the commentators and others restricted it to them not being known for bad judgment, such that if they were known for that, recklessness and immorality, then the contract is invalid in the correct view. He said in Fath al-Qadir: And whoever marries his minor daughter, who is capable of acquiring good and evil, to someone he knows is evil and immoral, then that is a clear case of bad judgment, and because leaving consideration here is certain, so it is not opposed by appearance of an interest that would be missed due to the affection of fatherhood. End. So the apparent meaning of their words is that if the father is known for bad judgment, then his marriage with less than mahr al-mithl, or with more for a male minor with excessive dower, or to a non-compatible person, is valid in both? No, it is not valid. And the lack of compatibility may be due to immorality or not, such that if he marries his daughter to a poor person or a person with a lowly profession and he is not compatible, then the contract is invalid. Then the scholar Ibn al-Humam restricted their words to the corrupt case that is not the issue, because the slavery of the wife entails the slavery of her children. End. And this is indicated by their depiction as when he marries him to a slave woman, except that the apparent is that they consider compatibility in her side absolutely according to what passed. His saying (because minor dower in mahr is forgiven): minor dower is what people tolerate, i.e., what some overlook and not everyone considers a loss, as opposed to excessive dower which is not tolerated. He said in al-Jawhara: And what is tolerated in marriage is less than half the dower. Thus said our teacher Muwaffaq al-Din, and it was said less than a tenth. End. According to the second, a deficiency of one hundred is minor, and a deficiency of ten from one hundred is excessive; according to the first, a deficiency of forty-nine from one hundred is minor and a deficiency of fifty is excessive. The closest is the second view, as is not hidden. End. Consider his saying (and the commentators restricted it by that he not be known, etc.) He preceded in explaining his saying 'and not for a Muslim over a Muslim' with a restriction by disbelief, because immorality does not remove legal capacity according to us in the well-known view, and it is mentioned in al-Manzoomah. End. Thus said al-Ramli. I say: and it does not contradict what is here, as is apparent, because that is about the continuation of capacity with its condition, which is marrying from a compatible person with mahr al-mithl, and here is about negating permissibility when the mentioned condition is absent. Its implication is that if he is known for bad judgment and marries from a compatible person with mahr al-mithl, it is valid, since nothing opposing affection appears from him. His saying (until if he is known for that, recklessness and immorality): In al-Maghrib: al-majin is one who does not care what he does and what is said to him; its source is mujun and majana; the verb is from the door of talab. End. And in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn Malik: even if the father's bad judgment is known due to his foolishness or greed, his contract is not valid by agreement. His saying (and Ibn al-Humam restricted): he approved what the speech of the scholar implies, that his bad judgment appears.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage discusses the special authority of the father and grandfather (al-ab wa al-jadd) regarding marriage of minor children. The matn states that if the father marries his minor child to a non-compatible person or with excessive dower (ghaban fahish), the marriage is valid, but this is not permissible for any other guardian. The commentary explains this ruling according to Abu Hanifa, with a dispute from the Sahibayn. The key reasoning is that guardianship is based on sound judgment (nazar). The father and grandfather have close kinship and are presumed to act in the child's best interest, considering higher objectives (maqasid) of marriage beyond just financial aspects. Unlike financial transactions, marriage has non-monetary benefits that can compensate for the dower deficit. However, this presumption only holds if the father is not known for bad judgment (su' al-ikhtiyar). If the father is known to be reckless or immoral, the contract is invalid even for him. The passage then defines ghaban fahish (excessive dower) vs. ghaban yasir (minor dower). Minor dower is what people tolerate in business, and in marriage, it is defined as less than half the mahr according to one view, or less than one-tenth according to another. The preferred view is the latter. Further, the father's capacity (ahliyyah) for marriage is not removed by immorality alone; he retains the right to marry his child to a compatible person with mahr al-mithl. But if he shows bad judgment, the contract is void. This shows that the Hanafi madhhab balances the father's authority with the welfare of the child, requiring a minimum level of prudence.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): Excessive dower disparity that people do not normally tolerate; defined as more than half the mahr or more than one-tenth depending on the view.
غبن يسير (ghaban yasir): Minor dower disparity that people normally overlook and accept.
سوء الاختيار (su' al-ikhtiyar): Bad judgment; a condition of the guardian that invalidates the presumed benefit of the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab as presented in this passage, who can validly marry a minor to a non-kufu' or with excessive dower?
A) Any guardian, including the judge.
B) Only the father and grandfather.
C) Only the mother and grandmother.
D) Only the executor (wasi).

Key Takeaway
The father and grandfather have a special authority to marry a minor with disparity, but this authority is conditional on them not being known for bad judgment.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Mistaken Assumption and Annulment: The Father's Marriage to a Non-Compatiable Spouse
Explaining the ruling for a father's mistaken assumption of compatibility and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a father marries his minor daughter based on a mistaken belief of compatibility and distinguish between the positions that declare the marriage void versus annullable.

Core Idea
If a father mistakenly assumes compatibility, the marriage is liable to annulment; but if he knew the truth, it binds the daughter.

The previous lesson established that a father may validly marry his minor child to a non-compatible spouse unless he is known for bad choice. But what if the father was not known for bad choice but acted on a mistaken assumption about the groom? This lesson examines that scenario and the important intra-Hanafi dispute about whether such a marriage is void from the start or only annulled upon the daughter's refusal after maturity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of mistaken assumption
The passage discusses a case where a father marries his young daughter to a man who denies drinking alcohol, but later turns out to be an alcoholic. The father was unaware and assumed compatibility.
This is different from the father knowing the man is fasiq and marrying anyway.
2
Determine the ruling when father is unaware
If the father did not know the man's flaw and most of the man's family are righteous, the marriage is void by consensus because the father acted on a mistaken assumption of compatibility.
The text says 'bāṭil ittifāqan'.
3
Determine the ruling when father is aware
If the father knew the man was a drinker, the marriage is effective (nāfidh) even though it shows bad choice. However, this does not necessarily make him 'known for bad choice' in the community.
The distinction is between actual knowledge and public notoriety.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on legal effect
Most fatwas declare such a marriage void ab initio, but al-Zahiriyya and al-Dhakhira hold that it should be annulled (yubṭil) upon the daughter's refusal after maturity. The latter is considered the correct view (huwa al-ḥaqq).
This affects whether the marriage requires a judicial separation or is automatically void.
5
Apply the rule to other scenarios
The same principle applies if the father mistakenly assumes the man is freeborn but he is a freed slave, or any other condition of compatibility.
The key is that the father's decision was based on a false assumption.

Book of Marriage, Chapter on Compatibility
He completes the dowry even if he marries off his minor child to a non-compatible [spouse] or with excessive disparity, it is valid but not permissible for other than the father and grandfather. The guardianship: when it is lacking the contract becomes void, and because the ruling revolves around the evidence of guardianship which is closeness of kinship, and in marriage there are objectives that outweigh the dowry and compatibility. It is restricted by excessive disparity because slight disparity in the dowry is forgiven by agreement. Likewise in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is restricted to marriage because in financial transactions like sale, purchase, lease, hiring, and settlement in claims of property, the father and grandfather do not have the power [to transact] with excessive disparity by consensus, because the objective is property and deficiency has occurred without a compensator, so it is not permissible. In marriage, there is a compensator, which is the objectives. It is unrestricted regarding the father and grandfather, but the commentators and others restricted it by [the condition] that he not be known for bad choice, to the extent that if he is known for that—[i.e.,] foolishness and immorality—the contract is void according to the correct [view]. He said in Fath al-Qadir: "Whoever marries off his young daughter, who is capable of acquiring both good and bad [character], to someone he knows is evil and immoral, this is clearly his bad choice, and because leaving guardianship here is definitive, so it is not contradicted by the appearance of intending a benefit that overrides that, out of consideration for fatherly affection." End quote. So the apparent meaning of their words is that if the father is known for bad choice, whether he contracts [the marriage] for less than the dower of the like, or for more in the case of a minor with excessive disparity, or from a non-compatible [spouse], it is not valid in either case, regardless of whether the lack of compatibility is due to immorality or not, even if he marries his daughter to a poor man or someone of lowly profession and he is not compatible, the contract is void. And the authors of fatwas mention that if the father marries off his young daughter to someone who denies drinking alcohol but then he is found to be addicted to it, and she says after reaching maturity, 'I do not accept the marriage,' if the father did not know him as a drinker and most of his household are righteous, then the marriage is void by agreement because he only married [her] on the assumption that he was compatible. End quote. This indicates that if the father knew him as a drinker, then the marriage is effective, and there is no doubt that this is clearly bad choice on his part, but it does not necessarily follow from its realization that the father is known to people for it, for he may be characterized by it in reality but not be famous for it, so there is no contradiction between what they mentioned, as is not hidden. And there is a distinction between his knowledge and ignorance in al-Dhakhira: if he knows that he is not compatible, he knows that he has reflected thoroughly and recognized this contract as a benefit for her; but here he assumed him to be compatible, so apparently he does not reflect. End quote. And in most of the fatwas on this issue, [it is stated] that the marriage is void, so its apparent meaning is that it did not occur. And in al-Zahiriyya: they separate them, and he did not say it is void, and this is the correct [view]. For this reason, al-Dhakhira said regarding their statement 'the marriage is void' that is, it will be voided. Then know that there is no specificity for when he knows him to be immoral; rather, the intent is that if he marries [her] based on [the assumption] that he is compatible, but then he is not compatible, then it is void. For this reason, al-Qunyah said: "He married his young daughter to a man he assumed to be a freeborn but he was a freed slave, then it is void by agreement." And it is restricted to marrying off his minor child because if he marries off his adult daughter without her consent, the marriage is suspended on her approval according to some. His statement (the commentators and others restricted it by [the condition] that he not be, etc.) He presented earlier in the commentary on his statement 'and not to a Muslim from a disbeliever' that it is restricted by disbelief because immorality does not remove legal capacity in our [school] according to the well-known [view], and that is what is mentioned in the versified text, as al-Ramli said. I say: this does not contradict what is here, as is apparent, because that is about the continuation of legal capacity with its condition, which is his marrying her to a compatible [spouse] with the dower of the like, while what is here is about negating permissibility when the mentioned condition is absent, and its implication is that if he is known for bad choice and marries [her] to a compatible [spouse] with the dower of the like, it is valid since nothing opposing affection appears from him. His statement (even if he is known for that—foolishness and immorality) In al-Mughrib: al-majin is one who does not care what he does or what is said to him, its infinitive is al-majun and al-majanah is a noun from it, and the verb is from the category of talaba. End quote. And in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn Malik: even if the father is known for bad choice due to his foolishness or greed, his contract is not valid by agreement. His statement (the investigator Ibn al-Humam restricted, etc.) He approved what the investigator's words implied, that his bad choice becomes apparent. End quote. And there is a distinction between his knowledge and ignorance in al-Dhakhira: if he knows that he is not compatible, he knows that he has reflected thoroughly and recognized this contract as a benefit for her; but here he assumed him to be compatible, so apparently he does not reflect. End quote. And in most of the fatwas on this issue, [it is stated] that the marriage is void, so its apparent meaning is that it did not occur. And in al-Zahiriyya: they separate them, and he did not say it is void, and this is the correct [view]. For this reason, al-Dhakhira said regarding their statement 'the marriage is void' that is, it will be voided. And it is restricted to marrying off his minor child because if he marries off his adult daughter without her consent, the marriage is suspended on her approval according to some.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the father and grandfather's authority to marry off a minor child. The base ruling states that such a marriage, even to a non-compatible spouse or with excessive disparity in mahr, is valid (sahih) but is only permissible for the father and grandfather—not for relatives like the brother or uncle. The commentary explains that the underlying principle is guardianship (al-nazar), which is established by close kinship. Since marriage involves broad objectives (maqasid) beyond mere financial considerations, slight disparity in mahr is forgiven, whereas in financial transactions, even slight disparity is not allowed for anyone other than the father or grandfather. The commentators restrict this ruling by a crucial condition: the father or grandfather must not be known for bad choice (sawi' al-ikhtiyar). If he is known for foolishness or immorality, the marriage contract is void (batil) according to the correct view. The passage then discusses the case where the father marries his daughter to someone he mistakenly believes is compatible (e.g., assuming he does not drink when he does). If the father was unaware of the man's flaw, the marriage is void if the daughter refuses after maturity; if he knew, the marriage is binding. However, this does not necessarily make him 'known for bad choice' in the public eye. The fatwa collections differ: some say the marriage is void ab initio, while al-Zahiriyya holds that the couple should be separated (tafriq) without declaring the contract void. The relied-upon position is that it will be voided (yubtil) upon the daughter's rejection. Finally, the commentary clarifies that the ruling applies when the father marries based on a false assumption of compatibility; knowing the man is a fasiq is not the only scenario. If the father purposely marries to a non-compatible man, the contract is void if the father is known for bad choice, otherwise it is valid.

Key Terms
ظن (ẓann): Assumption or belief that may be mistaken. The father's action is based on ẓann, which can be correct or incorrect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view (huwa al-ḥaqq) regarding a father's marriage of his minor daughter based on a mistaken assumption of compatibility?
A) The marriage is void immediately.
B) The marriage is valid and binding.
C) The marriage is annullable upon the daughter's refusal after maturity.
D) The marriage is valid only if the mahr is fair.

Key Takeaway
When a father mistakenly assumes a groom is compatible, the marriage is not automatically void; the daughter can seek annulment after maturity, a view preferred by leading Hanafi authorities.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Father Marrying Minor Daughter to a Non-Suitable Groom: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on father marrying minor to non-kuf' based on knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a father's marriage of his minor daughter to a non-suitable groom is effective (nafiz) versus voidable (yubtil), and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether it is void ab initio.

Core Idea
If a father knowingly marries his minor daughter to a non-suitable groom, the marriage is effective; if he was ignorant, it is voidable upon her objection.

When a father acts as guardian for his minor daughter, his judgment about the groom's suitability is presumed. But what if he gets it wrong? The Hanafi school distinguishes between knowledge and ignorance. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks this distinction and resolves an apparent contradiction: a father may have bad judgment (su' al-ikhtiyar) yet the marriage stands if he knew the defect. We'll trace the ruling and the intra-school debate on whether such a marriage is void from the start or merely voidable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The father marries his minor daughter to a man who outwardly denies drinking but is later found to be an addict. The daughter objects after majority.
The key factor is the father's knowledge of the man's drinking habit.
2
Determine Father's Knowledge
If the father knew of the drinking, the marriage is effective (nafiz). If he did not know and assumed suitability, the marriage is voidable (yubtil) upon the daughter's rejection.
Knowledge implies the father reflected and deemed the marriage beneficial despite the defect.
3
Understand the Meaning of 'Batil'
The majority of fatwas say the marriage is 'batil', but the correct interpretation (according to al-Zahiriyya and al-Dhakhira) is that it will be annulled (yubtil) after the daughter's objection, not that it is void ab initio.
The author prefers the voidable view.
4
Resolve the Apparent Contradiction
The father's bad judgment (su' al-ikhtiyar) in marrying his daughter to a known drinker does not necessarily make him publicly known for bad judgment. The marriage remains effective because he acted with full awareness.
A father can have hidden bad judgment without losing his authority.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Some earlier scholars hold that the marriage is void from the start (batil haqiqatan), while later authorities (including the author) hold it is voidable (yubtil). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the latter.
This affects whether the marriage requires a formal annulment or is automatically void.

لغيرهما عدم الصحة وعليه ابتنى الفرع المعروف ولو زوج العم الصغيرة حرة الجد من معتق الجد فكبرت وأجازت لا يصح لأنه لم يكن العقد موقوفاً إذ لا مجيز له فإن العم ونحوه يصح منهم التزويج لغير الكفء، ولذا ذكر في الخانية وغيرها أن غير الأب والجد إذا زوج الصغيرة فالأحوط أن يزوجها مرتين مرة بمهر مسمى ومرة بغير التسمية لأنه لو كان في التسمية نقصان فاحش ولم يصح النكاح الأول يصح الثاني .اهـ. ولا فرق بين الصغير والصغيرة في هذا المعنى فالتخصيص بالصغيرة مما لا ينبغي وليس للتزويج من غير كفء حيلة كما لا يخفى وقيد بتزويج الأب أي بنفسه لأنه لا يجوز لوكيل الأب أن يزوج بنته الصغيرة بأقل من مهر مثلها كذا في القنية. وينبغي استثناء القليل الذي يتساهل فيه كما لا يخفى. وقيدنا الأب بكونه صاحياً لأن السكران إذا قصر في مهر ابنته بما لا يتغابن الناس فيه فإنه لا يجوز إجماعاً، والصاحي يجوز لأن الظاهر من حال السكران أنه لا يتأمل إذ ليس له رأي كامل فيبقي النقصان ضرراً محضاً، والظاهر من حال الصاحي أنه يتأمل. كذا في الذخيرة. وكذا السكران إذا زوج من غير الكفء كما في الخانية. وبه علم أن المراد بالأب من ليس بسكران ولا عرف بسوء الاختيار.
It is appropriate. The authors of fatwas mentioned that if the father marries his minor daughter to someone who denies that he drinks intoxicants, but then he is an addict, and she says after growing up: I do not consent to the marriage, if the father did not know him to be a drinker and the majority of his household were righteous, then the marriage is invalid (batil) by agreement because he only married on the presumption that he was suitable. This indicates that if the father knew him to be a drinker, the marriage is effective (nafiz). There is no doubt that this is from him bad judgment (su' al-ikhtiyar) with certainty, but his being so does not necessarily mean that the father is known to people as such; he may possess it inwardly and not be famous for it, so there is no contradiction in what they mentioned, as is not hidden. And in al-Dhakhira, a distinction is made between his knowledge and ignorance: if he knew that he was not suitable, he knew that he reflected thoroughly and recognized this contract as an interest for her. But here, he thought him suitable, so apparently he did not reflect. The occurrence in most fatwas in this issue is that the marriage is invalid (batil), so its apparent meaning is that it was not concluded. In al-Zahiriyya: they separate between them, and they did not say it is invalid, and that is correct. Therefore, al-Dhakhira said regarding their statement 'the marriage is invalid' meaning it will be annulled (yubtil). Then know that there is no specificity to when he knew him to be a sinner; rather, the intended meaning is that if he marries him based on suitability, and then he is not suitable, then it is invalid. Therefore, al-Qunyah said: He married his minor daughter to a man whom the guardian thought was a freeborn but he was a freedman, so it is invalid by agreement. And he restricted it with his marriage of a child, because if he marries his minor female child with a grossly deficient dower, then it is not permissible by agreement because it is wasting their wealth, since the dower belongs to them and there is no other hidden purpose to consider, as in Fath al-Qadir. And the intended meaning by 'not permissible' in his statement 'that is not permissible for other than them' is lack of validity. Upon this is built the well-known branch: if the uncle marries the minor free female to the freedman of the grandfather, and she grows up and ratifies, it is not valid because the contract was not suspended since there is no one to ratify it. For the uncle and the like, marriage to a non-suitable person is valid from them. Therefore, it is mentioned in al-Khaniyya and others that if someone other than the father and grandfather marries a minor girl, the precaution is to marry her twice: once with a named dower and once without naming, because if there is a gross deficiency in the naming and the first marriage is not valid, the second becomes valid. There is no difference between male and female child in this meaning, so specification by female is not appropriate. And there is no trick (hila) for marriage to a non-suitable person, as is not hidden. And he restricted it to the father marrying himself, because it is not permissible for the father's agent to marry his minor daughter for less than her proper dower, as in al-Qunyah. And it is appropriate to except the small amount in which people are lenient, as is not hidden. And we restricted the father to being sober, because if a drunkard is deficient in his daughter's dower to an extent that people would not disregard, it is not permissible by consensus. The sober person is permissible because the apparent state of the drunkard is that he does not reflect, since he does not have complete opinion, so the deficiency remains pure harm. The apparent state of the sober person is that he reflects. This is in al-Dhakhira. Likewise, the drunkard if he marries to a non-suitable person, as in al-Khaniyya. By this it is known that what is meant by 'father' is one who is not a drunkard nor known for bad judgment.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the ruling on a father marrying his minor daughter to a man who is not suitable (kuf') in terms of religious character. The author begins by quoting a fatwa from the jurists: if a father marries his minor daughter to a man who outwardly denies drinking alcohol but is actually an addict, and the daughter, after attaining majority, refuses the marriage, then if the father did not know of the drinking habit and the man's family were generally righteous, the marriage is void (batil) by consensus because the father acted on the presumption of suitability. However, if the father knew about the drinking, the marriage is effective (nafiz) despite being a clear case of bad judgment. The author then resolves an apparent contradiction: the father's bad judgment in marrying his daughter to a known drinker does not necessarily make him publicly known for bad judgment; he may do it secretly. The Dhakhira distinguishes between knowledge and ignorance: if the father knew of the defect, he is deemed to have fully considered the matter and found it beneficial; if he was ignorant, he did not reflect. Next, the author addresses the terminology: many fatwas say the marriage is 'batil', but the correct view (as in al-Zahiriyya) is that it is not void from the start but will be annulled after the daughter's rejection. The author then generalizes: there is no specificity to the case of drinking; whenever a guardian marries a minor based on a presumption of suitability that turns out false, the marriage is batil (meaning annulled). He supports this with a case from al-Qunyah where the father thought the groom was freeborn but he was a freedman. The passage then moves to the issue of a deficient dower (mahr): if a father marries his minor child with a dower far below the normal (ghabn fahish), it is invalid by consensus because it wastes the child's wealth. For a father, if he is sober, it is valid because he is presumed to have considered the matter; if he is drunk, it is not valid. This is according to al-Dhakhira. The father must not be known for bad judgment. The author also notes that for guardians other than father and grandfather (like an uncle), if they marry a minor to a non-suitable person with a deficient dower, the marriage is not valid from the start; the precaution is to perform two contracts. The passage concludes by stating that the father's agent cannot marry the minor for less than her proper dower unless the father specifically authorized it. This entire discussion is rooted in Hanafi principles of kafa'ah and guardianship.

Key Terms
كفء (kuf'): Suitability in marriage, primarily in religious character (din) and lineage.
باطل (batil): Void; in this context, it can mean either void from inception or voidable/annulled after rejection. The author clarifies that it means 'yubtil' (will be annulled).
سوء اختيار (su' al-ikhtiyar): Bad judgment or poor discernment in selecting a spouse for a ward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a father marries his minor daughter to a man he knew to be a drinker, what is the ruling on the marriage?
A) The marriage is void (batil) ab initio.
B) The marriage is effective (nafiz) despite the father's bad judgment.
C) The marriage is valid only if the daughter approves after majority.
D) The marriage is suspended until the daughter reaches puberty.

Key Takeaway
A father's marriage of his minor daughter to a non-suitable groom is effective if he knew the defect; otherwise it is voidable (not void ab initio) upon the daughter's objection.

Non-Father Guardians and Agent Authority in Minor Marriages
Ruling for non-father guardians and father's agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for non-father guardians marrying minors to non-suitable persons and explain why the father's agent cannot accept less than mahr al-mithl without authorization.

Core Idea
A non-father guardian's marriage of a minor to a non-suitable person is invalid; the father's agent cannot accept less than proper dower without express authorization.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two linked issues: the authority of guardians other than the father and grandfather, and the limitations of a father's agent. The author refutes a mistaken opinion that such marriages are valid subject to annulment, and stresses that the agent's power is narrow. Understanding these restrictions protects the minor's rights and prevents invalid contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Marrying a minor to a non-suitable (ghayr kuf') person by a guardian other than the father or grandfather. The relied-upon ruling is that such a marriage is invalid from the start (la yajuz).
The author uses the term 'tifl' (child) broadly, including both males and females.
2
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Sadr al-Shari'ah claimed the marriage is valid and the minor has a right to annul after puberty. Identify this claim and the refutation by Ibn al-Kamal and al-Taftazani, who say it has no basis in transmission.
The existence of an annulment option does not imply validity of the original contract.
3
Analyze the Agent's Case
The father's agent (wakil) cannot marry the minor for less than mahr al-mithl unless the father specifically authorizes it. If the father knows the groom and only authorizes the contract, it is valid per Abu Hanifa.
A small deficiency (qalil) commonly overlooked is excepted, per al-Ramz.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is that the marriage by a non-father guardian to a non-suitable person is invalid from the start, so no annulment is needed. The agent's contract with deficient dower is invalid unless authorized or the deficiency is negligible.
This is the view of the majority of later Hanafi scholars, as adopted by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Source Text

And he made absolute in 'non-suitable' so it includes if he marries her to his own slave; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as in al-Dhakhira. And he restricted with 'child' because if the father marries the adult woman to one who is not appropriate as a slave with her consent, it is permissible by agreement. And there is no specificity to the father; rather, every guardian is like that if she has no one closer than him before the contract. And 'child' (tifl) applies to male and female, and the group is said 'tifla' and 'atfal'. So it appears that for a non-suitable person, they have no objection. So either to specify this from it or to enter this into it. His statement (and the intended meaning by 'not permissible' etc.) contains a refutation of Sadr al-Shari'ah where he said in his commentary: And if other than them (father and grandfather) do it, then they (the minors) have the right to annul after puberty, for it implies validity, and it is a misconception as pointed out by Ibn al-Kamal and others. Likewise, al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani refuted it in al-Talwih in the discussion of impediments, and mentioned that it has no narration at all. His statement (because it is not permissible for the father's agent to marry his daughter, etc.) said in al-Ramz: It should be restricted to when the father does not know the husband, like when he appoints him to find a husband for his minor daughter. But if he knows him, especially after his proposal, and only appointed him for the mere contract, then it should be valid according to Abu Hanifa. And it appears that his intention is if the agent marries to a non-suitable person, not with less than the proper dower which is the subject of discussion. And regarding this, al-Nahr said: Its meaning should be what if he appoints him to marry his child; but if he specifies the amount that is a gross deficiency, then this statement of his is valid. (And it is appropriate to except the small amount, etc.) said in al-Ramz: This indicates their restriction with 'gross' so there is no need for the exception.

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, focusing on the rulings for guardians other than the father and grandfather. The author discusses that the ruling of 'non-suitable' (ghayr kuf') is general and includes marrying a minor to one's own slave; this is according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) as reported in al-Dhakhira. The restriction 'child' (tifl) is significant because if the father marries his adult daughter to a non-suitable person (e.g., a slave) with her consent, it is valid by consensus. The father has no special right over other guardians in this regard; any guardian (wali) can do so if there is no closer relative who is displeased before the contract. The term 'tifl' includes male and female children; the plural is 'atfal'. The author then addresses a potential objection: if someone marries a minor to a non-suitable person, the guardian has no objection? Actually, the text clarifies that the ruling applies. Then there is a critique of Sadr al-Shari'ah's view that if someone other than the father/grandfather does it, the minors have the right to annul after puberty, which would imply the marriage is valid. The refutation comes from Ibn al-Kamal and al-Taftazani, stating this opinion has no basis in transmission. Finally, the author discusses the ruling for a father's agent (wakil): it is not permissible for the agent to marry the minor daughter for less than her proper dower, unless the father specifically authorized it. If the father knows the groom and only authorized the contract, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa. The exception for a small amount (qalil) that people overlook is noted. This section reinforces the principle that the father (and grandfather) have broader authority in marring their minor children, while other guardians have more restrictions to protect the minor's interests.

Key Terms
وكيل الأب (wakil al-ab): The father's agent appointed to conduct the marriage contract for the father's minor child.
طفل (tifl): A child who has not reached puberty; includes both male and female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The marriage is valid but the minor can annul after puberty.
B) The marriage is invalid from the start, and no annulment is needed.
C) The marriage is suspended until the father approves.
D) The marriage is valid if the guardian is also a relative.

Key Takeaway
The marriage of a minor by a non-father guardian to a non-suitable person is invalid; the father's agent cannot accept deficient dower without express authorization.

Nikah — Marriage

Invalidity of Marriage of Minors by Non-Father Guardians: Ghabn Fahish and Non-Kafa'ah
Sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on kafa'ah and dower in minor marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a marriage of a minor by a guardian other than father/grandfather is absolutely invalid (batil) when there is ghabn fahish or non-kafa'ah, and identify the exceptions for the father's marriage when he is sober.

Core Idea
A minor's marriage by a non-father guardian with excessive dower deficiency or unsuitability is absolutely invalid—no ratification can rescue it.

In Hanafi nikah, the father (and grandfather) have full authority over their minor children's marriages, but other guardians (like uncles) have limited power. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains what happens when a non-father guardian marries a minor with a grossly deficient dower or to a non-suitable spouse. The ruling is stark: the marriage is invalid (batil) and cannot be ratified later, unlike in other schools where it might be suspended. We will analyze the conditions, exceptions, and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general ruling
The passage starts with a case: a guardian marries a minor slave girl (of his child) with a grossly deficient dower (ghabn fahish). The ruling is that it is invalid by consensus.
The term 'لا يجوز' here means invalid (batil), not just impermissible.
2
Distinguish between father/grandfather and other guardians
The key distinction is that the father (and grandfather) have special authority. For other guardians, such as a paternal uncle, the marriage is invalid even if the minor later ratifies it, because there is no one to ratify at the time of contract.
The contract is not suspended (mawquf); it is void from the start.
3
Understand the precautionary measure (ihtiyat) of double marriage
Some scholars recommend that a non-father guardian perform two marriage contracts: one with a named dower and one without naming, so that if the first is invalid due to deficiency, the second stands.
This is a practical hila to avoid invalidity, but the author notes there is no trick to marry a non-suitable spouse.
4
Note the exceptions: father's sobriety and slight deficiency
If the father himself marries the minor, his contract is valid even with some dower deficiency, provided he is sober (sahi) and the deficiency is not gross. A drunken father's contract is invalid. Also, a slight deficiency that people overlook is excepted.
The father's presumed deliberation (tamal) justifies his discretion.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: marrying to one's own slave
The passage mentions that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the prohibition includes marrying the minor to his own slave. This implies a difference from Abu Hanifa's view, though the detail is not elaborated here.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school there can be nuances on what constitutes non-kafa'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زوج أمة طقله بغبن فاحش فإنه لا يجوز اتفاقاً لأنه إضاعة ما لهما لأن المهر ملكهما ولا مقصود آخر باطن يصرف النظر إليه كما في فتح القدير. والمراد بعدم الجواز في قوله «لم يجز ذلك لغيرهما عدم الصحة وعليه ابتنى الفرع المعروف ولو زوج العم الصغيرة حرة الجد من معتق الجد فكبرت وأجازت لا يصح لأنه لم يكن العقد موقوفاً إذ لا مجيز له فإن العم ونحوه يصح منهم التزويج لغير الكفء، ولذا ذكر في الخانية وغيرها أن غير الأب والجد إذا زوج الصغيرة فالأحوط أن يزوجها مرتين مرة بمهر مسمى ومرة بغير التسمية لأنه لو كان في التسمية نقصان فاحش ولم يصح النكاح الأول يصح الثاني .اهـ. ولا فرق بين الصغير والصغيرة في هذا المعنى فالتخصيص بالصغيرة مما لا ينبغي وليس للتزويج من غير كفء حيلة كما لا يخفى وقيد بتزويج الأب أي بنفسه لأنه لا يجوز لوكيل الأب أن يزوج بنته الصغيرة بأقل من مهر مثلها كذا في القنية. وينبغي استثناء القليل الذي يتساهل فيه كما لا يخفى. وقيدنا الأب بكونه صاحياً لأن السكران إذا قصر في مهر ابنته بما لا يتغابن الناس فيه فإنه لا يجوز إجماعاً، والصاحي يجوز لأن الظاهر من حال السكران أنه لا يتأمل إذ ليس له رأي كامل فيبقي النقصان ضرراً محضاً، والظاهر من حال الصاحي أنه يتأمل. كذا في الذخيرة. وكذا السكران إذا زوج من غير الكفء كما في الخانية. وبه علم أن المراد بالأب من ليس بسكران ولا عرف بسوء الاختيار. وأطلق في غير الكفء فشمل ما إذا زوجها من مملوك نفسه فعندهما كما في الذخيرة. وقيد بالطفل لأن الأب لو زوج الكبيرة من مملوكه برضاها فهو جائز اتفاقاً، ولا خصوصية للأب بل كل ولي كذلك إن لم يكن لها غيره أقرب منه لم يرض به قبل العقد والطفل الصبي ويقع على الذكر والأنثى والجماعة يقال طفلة وأطفال اهـ.
If he marries a slave woman of his child with excessive deception, it is not permissible by agreement, because it is wasting the property of both, since the dower is owned by them, and there is no other hidden purpose to consider, as in Fath al-Qadeer. What is meant by non-permissibility in his statement 'that is not permissible for others' is invalidity, and upon this is built the well-known branch: if the paternal uncle marries the minor free woman to the freed slave of the grandfather, and she reaches puberty and ratifies, it is not valid, because the contract was not suspended, as there is no one to ratify. Indeed, the paternal uncle and the like can validly marry (the minor) to a non-suitable spouse. Therefore, it is mentioned in al-Khaniyah and others that if someone other than the father and grandfather marries a minor girl, the precaution is to marry her twice: once with a named dower and once without naming, because if there is a great deficiency in the naming and the first marriage is not valid, the second becomes valid. There is no difference between a minor boy and girl in this meaning, so specification by minor girl is not appropriate. There is no trick for marrying a non-suitable spouse. It is restricted by the marriage by the father himself, because it is not permissible for the father's agent to marry his minor daughter for less than her proper dower, as in al-Qunyah. A slight amount that is overlooked should be excepted, as is obvious. We restricted the father to being sober because if a drunken father reduces his daughter's dower to an amount not ordinarily overlooked, it is not permissible by consensus; but the sober is permissible because the apparent condition of the drunken is that he does not deliberate, having no complete opinion, so the deficiency remains pure harm, whereas the apparent condition of the sober is that he deliberates. So in al-Dhakhirah. Likewise the drunken if he marries (the minor) to a non-suitable spouse, as in al-Khaniyah. From this it is known that what is meant by father is one who is not drunken nor known for bad choice. The expression 'non-suitable spouse' is general, including if he marries her to his own slave; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as in al-Dhakhirah. It is restricted to a child because if the father marries an adult woman to his slave with her consent, it is permissible by agreement. The father has no exclusivity, rather every guardian is like that if there is no other closer guardian who did not consent before the contract. The child is a boy and applies to male, female, and group; one says 'tiflah' and 'atfal' etc.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding marriage of minors by guardians other than the father or grandfather. The author begins by stating a case: if a guardian marries a minor slave girl (of his child) with a grossly deficient dower (ghabn fahish), it is unanimously invalid because it wastes the property of the two parties (the minor and the guardian's child) since the dower belongs to them and there is no other hidden benefit. He then clarifies that 'non-permissibility' here means invalidity (adam al-sihhah), not just impermissibility, citing a known branch: if a paternal uncle marries his minor niece to the freed slave of the grandfather, and she later reaches puberty and ratifies, it is still invalid because the contract was not suspended (mawquf) — there is no one to ratify it since the uncle's authority is limited. The author notes that guardians other than father and grandfather (like uncle) are valid to marry minors to non-suitable spouses (but with the risk of invalidity), so the precautionary measure (ihtiyat) is to perform two marriage contracts: one with a named dower and one without, so that if the first fails due to deficiency, the second stands. The ruling applies equally to minor boys and girls. There is no legal trick (hila) to marry a non-suitable spouse. The text then restricts to the father marrying personally: an agent of the father cannot marry his minor daughter for less than mahr al-mithl. A slight deficiency that is customarily overlooked is excepted. The father must be sober; if drunk, his reduction of dower (even if not excessive) is impermissible by consensus because a drunk does not deliberate properly. The same applies if a drunk marries to a non-suitable spouse. Therefore, 'father' here means one who is not drunk and not known for bad judgment. The general expression 'non-suitable spouse' includes even marrying her to his own slave (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, as in al-Dhakhirah). The restriction to a 'child' (tifl) is because if the father marries an adult daughter to his slave with her consent, it is valid by agreement. This ruling applies to all guardians, not just fathers, if there is no closer guardian who did not consent before the contract. The term 'tifl' includes both genders and groups.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): A gross deficiency in the dower that is not customarily overlooked (لا يتغابن الناس فيه).
كفاءة (kafa'ah): Suitability in marriage between spouses in lineage, wealth, profession, etc.
صاحي (sahi): Sober, sane, with full rational capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a paternal uncle marries his minor niece to a man with a dower that is grossly deficient (ghabn fahish), and the niece later reaches puberty and ratifies the marriage, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage becomes valid upon ratification.
B) The marriage is invalid and cannot be ratified.
C) The marriage is valid only if the niece knew about the deficiency at the time of ratification.
D) The marriage is suspended and she can choose to accept or reject.

Key Takeaway
A minor's marriage by a non-father guardian with ghabn fahish or to a non-kuf’ is absolutely invalid (batil) and cannot be cured by later ratification—only a new valid contract suffices.

Self-Marriage in Nikah: Cousin and Agent
Ruling with proof on self-marriage by a cousin and an agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two cases where self-marriage is valid in Hanafi nikah and identify the conditions that make each valid or invalid.

Core Idea
A paternal cousin can marry his minor cousin, and a specifically authorized agent can marry his principal – both rely on the agent being a mere intermediary.

This lesson addresses two special scenarios in Hanafi marriage law: a paternal cousin marrying his minor cousin, and an agent marrying the woman who appointed him. The key distinction is that in marriage, the agent is merely an intermediary (safir/mu'abbar) – not a full representative – which allows these self-marriages under specific conditions. We will examine the textual proof, the conditions, and the difference from agency in sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage to identify the two scenarios: (1) a paternal cousin marrying his minor cousin, and (2) an agent marrying his principal (the woman who appointed him). Note the ruling: both are valid.
The cousin case applies only to a minor cousin; the agent case requires specific authorization.
2
Distinguish marriage agency from sale agency
The author explains that in marriage the agent is an expresser (mu'abbar) and intermediary (safir), not a direct representative with rights like in sale. In sale, the agent cannot self-deal because rights revert to him; in marriage, rights do not revert, so self-marriage is possible.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage cites two hadith: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf marrying Umm Hakim with her authorization using one expression, and the Prophet acting as intermediary between a man and a woman. Both support the permissibility of self-marriage by an authorized person.
The hadith from Uqbah ibn Amir is narrated by Abu Dawud.
4
Analyze conditions for the agent to self-marry
The agent must be specifically authorized to marry her to himself. If she says 'marry me to a man' (indefinite), he cannot marry her to himself because he is definite. Similarly, 'marry me to whomever you wish' does not allow self-marriage due to ignorance of the husband.
The passage contrasts with bequests where ignorance does not invalidate.
5
Understand the cousin case – minor vs adult
The cousin case applies only to a minor cousin. For an adult cousin, if she appoints him he is an agent (second case), otherwise he is a fuduli (unauthorized) whose marriage is invalid.
This distinction prevents misunderstanding of the scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
للابن العم أن يزوج بنت عمه من نفسه وللوكيل أن يزوج موكلته من نفسه
حاصله بعض مسائل الوكيل والفضولي وتأخيرهما عن الولي ظاهر لأن ولايته أصلية قوله : (لابن العم أن يزوج بنت عمه من نفسه وللوكيل أن يزوج موكلته من نفسه) لأن الوكيل في النكاح معبر وسفير والتمانع في الحقوق دون التعبير ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه بخلاف البيع لأنه مباشر حتى رجعت الحقوق إليه، وروى البخاري أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف قال لأم حكيم بنت فارض أتجعلين أمرك إلي؟ قالت نعم قال : تزوجتك. فعقده بلفظ واحد. وعن عقبة بن عامر أنه عليه السلام قال لرجل أترضى أن أزوجك فلانة؟ قال : نعم. وقال للمرأة : أترضين أن أزوجك فلاناً؟ قالت : نعم. فزوج أحدهما صاحبه وكان ممن شهد الحديبية. رواه أبو داود فما في الغاية من أن قولهم إنه سفير ومعبر لم يسلم من النقض فإن الوكيل لو زوج موكلته على عبد نفسه يطالب بتسلميه سهو فإنه لم يلزمه بمجرد العقد وإنما لزمه بالتزامه حيث جعله مهراً وأضاف العقد إليه والمراد ببنت العم الصغيرة فيكون ابن العم أصيلاً من جانب وولياً من جانب، ولا يراد بها الكبيرة هنا لأنها لو وكلته فهو وكيل داخل في المسألة الثانية وإلا فهو فضولي سيأتي بطلانه إن لم يقبل عنها أحد ولو أجازته بعده. والمراد بالوكيل الوكيل في أن يزوجها من نفسه لما في المحيط : لو وكلته بتزويجها من رجل فزوجها من نفسه لم يجز لأنها أمرته بالتزويج من رجل نكرة وهو معرفة بالخطاب والمعرفة لا تدخل تحت النكرة. وفي الولوالجية : لو قالت المرأة زوج نفسي ممن شئت لا يملك أن يزوجها من نفسه فرق بين هذا وبين ما إذا أوصى بثلث ماله فقال للموصى له ضع ثلث ما ي حيث شئت كان للموصى له أن يضع عند نفسه، والفرق أن الزوج مجهول وجهالة الزوج تمنع صحة الشرط وصار كالمسكوت عنه بخلاف الوصية لأن الجهالة لا تمنع صحة الوصية فيعتبر التفويض مطلقاً .اهـ. فلو وكلته أن يتصرف في أمورها لا يصح من غيره
قوله (وجهالة الزوج تمنع صحة الشرط الخ) قال في الرمز : هذا يقتضي أن لا أيضاً اهـ. قلت: لكن تقدم في باب الولي خلافه حيث قال عند قول المتن «وإن استأذنها الولي الخ» : أما إذا قالت وأنا راضية بما تفعله أنت بعد قوله إن أقواماً يخطبونك أو زوجني ممن تختاره ونحوه فهو استئذان صحيح كما في الظهيرية .
Section: The paternal cousin may marry his cousin to himself, and the agent may marry his principal to himself. Its summary is some issues of the agent and the unauthorized (fuduli), and their precedence over the guardian is apparent because his authority is original. His statement: (The paternal cousin may marry his cousin to himself and the agent may marry his principal to himself) because the agent in marriage is an expresser and intermediary, and mutual avoidance is in rights not expression, and rights do not revert to him, unlike sale because he is direct until rights revert to him. Al-Bukhari narrated that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said to Umm Hakim bint Qariz: 'Do you entrust your affair to me?' She said, 'Yes.' He said, 'I marry you.' So he contracted with one expression. And from Uqbah ibn Amir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to a man: 'Are you pleased that I marry you to so-and-so?' He said, 'Yes.' And he said to the woman: 'Are you pleased that I marry you to so-and-so?' She said, 'Yes.' So he married one to the other. It was narrated by Abu Dawud. So what is in al-Ghayah that their saying 'he is an intermediary and expresser' is not safe from objection, for if the agent marries his principal to his own slave, he is demanded to hand him over — a mistake, because he is not obliged by mere contract, but rather by his commitment where he made him the dower and added the contract to himself. What is meant by 'cousin' is the minor cousin, so the paternal cousin is an original party on one side and a guardian on the other. The adult cousin is not meant here because if she appoints him, he is an agent included in the second issue; otherwise he is a fuduli whose invalidity will come if no one accepts for her even if she subsequently ratifies. What is meant by 'agent' is the agent to marry her to himself, as in al-Muhit: If she appoints him to marry her to a man, and he marries her to himself, it is not permissible because she ordered him to marry her to an indefinite man (nakirah), and he is definite by address, and the definite does not fall under the indefinite. In al-Walwaljiyah: If the woman says, 'Marry me to whomever you wish,' he does not have the right to marry her to himself. The difference between this and when one bequeaths a third of his wealth and says to the legatee, 'Place a third of my wealth wherever you wish,' the legatee may place it with himself. The difference is that the husband is unknown, and ignorance of the husband prevents the validity of the condition, and it becomes as if unstated. Unlike the bequest because ignorance does not prevent the validity of the bequest, so the delegation is considered absolute. Then if she appoints him to manage her affairs, it is not valid otherwise. His statement (And ignorance of the husband prevents the validity of the condition, etc.) said in al-Ramz: This necessitates that it is not valid either. I say: But earlier in the chapter of the guardian, the opposite was stated where he said at the text 'And if the guardian seeks her permission, etc.': If she says 'And I am pleased with what you do' after his saying 'Some people are proposing to you' or 'Marry me to whomever you choose' and the like, it is a valid request for permission as in al-Zahiriyyah.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This section (fasl) addresses two specific cases: (1) a paternal cousin marrying his minor cousin to himself, and (2) an agent marrying his principal (the woman who appointed him) to himself. The author explains that these are distinct from normal agency because in marriage, the agent is merely an intermediary (safir) and expresser (mu'abbar), not a direct representative whose rights revert to him, unlike in sale where the agent is a direct participant. He provides hadith evidence: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf married Umm Hakim by her authorization using a single expression, and the Prophet himself acted as intermediary between a man and a woman. The text addresses an objection: if an agent marries his principal to his own slave, he is not liable to deliver the slave by the mere contract, but only if he commits to it as dower. The cousin case applies only to a minor cousin; for an adult cousin, if she appoints him, he is an agent (second case), otherwise he is a fuduli whose marriage is invalid unless someone else accepts. The agent case has a condition: she must authorize him specifically to marry her to himself; if she tells him to marry her to a man without specifying, he cannot marry her to himself because 'a man' is indefinite while he is definite. Similarly, if she says 'marry me to whomever you wish,' he cannot marry her to himself due to ignorance of the husband, which invalidates the condition. The author contrasts this with a bequest where the legatee may assign to himself because ignorance does not invalidate bequests. Finally, there is a cross-reference to a previous discussion where a woman's general delegation (e.g., 'I am pleased with what you do') may be valid as permission for the guardian to choose.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): A person appointed by the woman to arrange her marriage; in marriage, the agent is a mere intermediary (safir/mu'abbar) unlike in sale.
فضولي (fuduli): A person who acts without authority to contract a marriage for someone else; such a contract is invalid (batil) unless subsequently ratified by a guardian.
معبر (mu'abbar): An expresser; one who conveys the consent but does not become a party with rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is valid because he is her agent.
B) It is invalid because she specified 'a man' (indefinite) and he is definite.
C) It is valid only if she explicitly intended him.
D) It is invalid because agents cannot marry themselves to principals under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
A paternal cousin can marry his minor cousin; an agent can marry his principal only if specifically authorized – both rely on the intermediary concept.

Nikah — Marriage

Marriage of a Guardian or Agent to Himself
Ruling with proofs and intra-Hanafi dispute on witness identification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wali or wakil marrying himself to the woman under his authority, identify the hadith proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on witness identification.

Core Idea
A wali or wakil can marry himself to his ward or client, but must properly identify her to witnesses to avoid invalidation.

This lesson examines the ruling that a paternal cousin (ibn al-amm) may marry his minor paternal cousin to himself, and an agent (wakil) may marry his female client to himself. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides the rationale, hadith evidence, and addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the agent must identify the bride to the witnesses. Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of guardianship and agency in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What exactly is being ruled? The act is a wali or wakil marrying himself to the woman under his authority. The ruling is that it is permissible (sahih) under specific conditions.
The act is not a direct marriage like a regular guardian marrying his ward to another.
2
Locate the Dalil
The text cites two hadith: (1) Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf marrying Umm Hakim with her consent in one utterance, and (2) the Prophet (s) acting as intermediary for a man and woman. These prove that a third party can conclude the marriage with the consent of both.
The hadith are ahad but their meaning (dalala) is definitive for the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
In the first hadith, Abd al-Rahman asked for her consent and then said 'I marry you', showing a single utterance suffices. In the second, the Prophet asked both parties and then married them. This demonstrates that an intermediary (whether wali or wakil) can conclude the contract.
The key is that the intermediary is acting as a mere transmitter, not acquiring rights.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Al-Khassaf holds that the agent need not identify the wife to witnesses; the preferred view (al-Walwaji, mufta bihi) requires identification by name and lineage if she is absent, or by pointing if present. The text discusses the practical implications.
This ikhtilaf affects the validity of the marriage if the witnesses do not know the bride.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq favors the view requiring identification, following al-Walwaji and noting that caution is to combine both methods (unveiling and naming). This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the need for certainty in testimony and practical caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كتاب النكاح فصل في الكفاءة
لابن العم أن يزوج بنت عمه من نفسه وللوكيل أن يزوج موكلته من نفسه
حاصله بعض مسائل الوكيل والفضولي وتأخيرهما عن الولي ظاهر لأن ولايته أصلية قوله : (لابن العم أن يزوج بنت عمه من نفسه وللوكيل أن يزوج موكلته من نفسه) لأن الوكيل في النكاح معبر وسفير والتمانع في الحقوق دون التعبير ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه بخلاف البيع لأنه مباشر حتى رجعت الحقوق إليه، وروى البخاري أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف قال لأم حكيم بنت فارض أتجعلين أمرك إلي؟ قالت نعم قال : تزوجتك. فعقده بلفظ واحد. وعن عقبة بن عامر أنه عليه السلام قال لرجل أترضى أن أزوجك فلانة؟ قال : نعم. وقال للمرأة : أترضين أن أزوجك فلاناً؟ قالت : نعم. فزوج أحدهما صاحبه وكان ممن شهد الحديبية. رواه أبو داود فما في الغاية من أن قولهم إنه سفير ومعبر» لم يسلم من النقض فإن الوكيل لو زوج موكلته على عبد نفسه يطالب بتسليمه سهو فإنه لم يلزمه بمجرد العقد وإنما لزمه بالتزامه حيث جعله مهراً وأضاف العقد إليه والمراد ببنت العم الصغيرة فيكون ابن العم أصيلاً من جانب وولياً من جانب، ولا يراد بها الكبيرة هنا لأنها لو وكلته فهو وكيل داخل في المسألة الثانية وإلا فهو فضولي سيأتي بطلانه إن لم يقبل عنها أحد ولو أجازته بعده. والمراد بالوكيل الوكيل في أن يزوجها من نفسه لما في المحيط : لو وكلته بتزويجها من رجل فزوجها من نفسه لم يجز لأنها أمرته بالتزويج من رجل نكرة وهو معرفة بالخطاب والمعرفة لا تدخل تحت النكرة. وفي الولوالجية : لو قالت المرأة زوج نفسي ممن شئت لا يملك أن يزوجها من نفسه فرق بين هذا وبين ما إذا أوصى بثلث ماله فقال للموصى له ضع ثلث ما حيث شئت كان للموصى له أن يضع عند نفسه، والفرق أن الزوج مجهول وجهالة الزوج تمنع صحة الشرط وصار كالمسكوت عنه بخلاف الوصية لأن الجهالة لا تمنع صحة الوصية فيعتبر التفويض مطلقاً .اهـ. فلو وكلته أن يتصرف في أمورها لا يصح من غيره
