من
وأطلق في الوكالة به فأفاد أنه لا يشترط الإشهاد عندها للصحة وإنما لخوف الإنكار، ولم يبين كيف يزوجها الوكيل من نفسه وأنه هل يشترط أن يعرفها الشهود للاختلاف، فذكر الخصاف أنه لا يشترط معرفتها ولا ذكر اسمها ونسبها للشهود حتى لو قال تزوجت المرأة التي جعلت أمرها إلي على صداق كذا عندهم صح والمختار في المذهب خلافه وإن كان الخصاف كبيراً في العلم يقتدى به قال الولوالجي في فتاواه : امرأة وكلت رجلاً أن يزوجها نفسه فذهب الوكيل وقال اشهدوا أني قد تزوجت فلانة ولم تعرف الشهود فلانة لا يجوز النكاح ما لم يذكر اسمها واسم أبيها وجدها لأنها غائبة والغائبة لا تعرف إلا بالنسبة، ألا ترى أنه لو قال تزوجت امرأة وكلتني بالنكاح لا يجوز . وإن كانت حاضرة متنقبة ولا يعرفها الشهود فقال اشهدوا أني تزوجت هذه المرأة فقالت المرأة زوجت نفسي منه جاز وهو المختار لأنها حاضرة والحاضرة تعرف بالإشارة فإذا أرادوا الاحتياط يكشف وجهها حتى يعرفها الشهود أو يذكر اسمها واسم أبيها واسم جدها حتى يكون متفقاً عليه فيقع الأمن أن من يرفع إلى قاض يرى قول من لا يجوز وهو نصير بن يحيى فيبطل النكاح. هذا كله إذا كان الشهود لا يعرفون المرأة، أما إذا كانوا يعرفونها وهي غائبة فذكر اسمها لا غير جاز النكاح إذا عرف الشهود أنه أراد به المرأة التي عرفوها لأن المقصود من النسبة التعريف وقد حصل باسمها اهـ. وقد وقع في كثير من الفتاوى والاحتياط كشف وجهها أو ذكر اسمها بكلمة أو والصواب بالواو كما في عمدة الفتاوى للصدر الشهيد لأن الاحتياط الجمع بينهما لا أحدهما. وفي الخانية : رجل أرسل رجلاً ليخطب له امرأة يعينها فذهب الرسول وزوجها إياه جاز لأنه أمره بالخطبة وتمام الخطبة بالعقد .اهـ. ويشترط للزوم عقد الوكيل موافقته في المهر المسمى فلذا قال في الخانية : لو وكله في أن يزوجه فلانة بألف درهم فزوجها إياه بألفين، إن أجاز الزوج جاز، وإن رد بطل النكاح ، وإن لم يعلم الزوج بذلك حتى دخل بها فالخيار باقِ
شمس
قوله (والمختار في المذهب خلافه الخ) قال المقدسي فيما نقل عنه : إن أراد أن كلام الولوالجي يشهد له فممنوع لأن ذاك في صحة نكاح المنتقبة أي فهو المختار بالنسبة إلى قول نصير بن يحيى، ومما يؤيد ذلك أن الأئمة الحلواني مع . جلالة قدره نقل كلام الخصاف بجميل الأوصاف . أنه كبير يقتدى به ولو كان المختار خلافه لنبه عليه ا.هـ. وذكر قريباً من هذا في الرمز وفيه : إن اقتصار الولوالجي على خلاف كلام الخصاف يشعر باختياره ونقل الحلواني له لا يفيد أنه المختار في البحر الرائق/ ج٣/ ١٦٥
المذهب
Chapter: The Book of Marriage, Section on Suitability. The paternal cousin may marry his paternal uncle's daughter to himself, and the agent may marry his female client to himself. The summary is some issues of the agent and the unauthorized person, and their delay from the guardian is apparent because his guardianship is original. His statement: (The paternal cousin may marry his paternal uncle's daughter to himself, and the agent may marry his female client to himself) because the agent in marriage is an intermediary and transmitter, and prevention is in rights, not in transmission, and rights do not revert to him unlike sale because he is direct so rights revert to him. Bukhari narrated that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said to Umm Hakim bint Qariz: 'Do you place your matter in my hands?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'I marry you.' So he concluded it with one utterance. And from Uqba ibn Amir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to a man: 'Are you pleased that I marry you to so-and-so?' He said: 'Yes.' And he said to the woman: 'Are you pleased that I marry you to so-and-so?' She said: 'Yes.' So he married one to the other, and he was among those who witnessed the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah. Abu Dawud narrated it. So what is in al-Ghayah that their statement that he is an intermediary and transmitter is not free from criticism, for if the agent marries his client to his own slave, he is demanded to hand him over inadvertently; he is not obliged by mere contract, but rather by his commitment where he made him a dowry and added the contract to himself. What is meant by 'paternal uncle's daughter' is the minor, so the paternal cousin is a principal on one side and a guardian on the other. The major is not meant here because if she appoints him as agent, he is an agent included in the second issue; otherwise he is an unauthorized person whose invalidness will come if no one accepts for her even if she ratifies later. What is meant by 'agent' is the agent in marrying her to himself, because in al-Muhit: If she appointed him to marry her to a man and he married her to himself, it is not permissible because she ordered him to marry her to an indefinite man (nakira) and he is definite by address, and the definite does not fall under the indefinite. In al-Walwajiyyah: If a woman said 'marry me to whomever you wish', he does not have the right to marry her to himself. There is a difference between this and when one bequeaths a third of his property and says to the legatee 'place the third wherever you wish' – the legatee may place it with himself. The difference is that the husband is unknown, and ignorance of the husband prevents the validity of the condition, and it becomes like what is left unmentioned, unlike the bequest because ignorance does not prevent the validity of the bequest, so the delegation is considered absolute. End. So if she appointed him to act in her affairs, it is not valid from someone else. His statement (And ignorance of the husband prevents the validity of the condition etc.) said in al-Ramz: This necessitates that not also. End. I say: But it preceded in the chapter of the guardian contrary to this, where he said at the statement of the matn 'And if the guardian seeks her permission etc.': As for when she says 'I am pleased with what you do' after his saying 'some men are proposing to you' or 'marry me to whomever you choose' and the like, it is a valid seeking of permission as in al-Zahiriyyah. [PAGE_241] The Book of Marriage, Section on Suitability, and the marriage of a slave and slave girl without the master's permission is suspended like the marriage of an unauthorized person, and part of the contract does not depend on... silence. He has the right to marry her to himself all the more, as in al-Khaniyyah. Agency is established by explicit statement as well as by silence. Therefore, it is said in al-Zahiriyyah: If the adult paternal cousin said 'I want to marry you to myself', it is permissible. End. He did not restrict it to a virgin, and it was restricted to a virgin in Ghayat al-Bayan and others. The apparent is that it is specific to the guardian as previously explained. And he spoke in absolute terms about agency, so it indicates that witnessing is not required for validity, but only for fear of denial. He did not explain how the agent marries her to himself and whether it is necessary that the witnesses know her due to difference. Al-Khassaf mentioned that it is not necessary to know her nor mention her name and lineage to the witnesses, so that if he said 'I married the woman who placed her matter in my hands for such a dowry' in their presence, it is valid. The preferred view in the school is contrary to this, even though al-Khassaf is great in knowledge to be followed. Al-Walwaji said in his Fatawa: A woman appointed a man to marry her to himself. The agent went and said 'Bear witness that I have married so-and-so', but the witnesses did not know so-and-so. The marriage is not valid unless he mentions her name, her father's name, and her grandfather's name, because she is absent and the absent is only known by relation. Do you not see that if he said 'I married a woman who appointed me for marriage', it is not valid. If she is present veiled and the witnesses do not know her, and he said 'Bear witness that I married this woman', and the woman said 'I married myself to him', it is valid, and that is the preferred view because she is present and the present is known by indication. If they want precaution, they may uncover her face so the witnesses know her, or mention her name, her father's name, and her grandfather's name so that there is agreement and security arises that if the case is taken to a judge who holds the view of one who does not permit – i.e., Nasir ibn Yahya – he would invalidate the marriage. This is all if the witnesses do not know the woman. But if they know her and she is absent, mentioning only her name is sufficient; the marriage is valid if the witnesses understand that he meant the woman they know, because the purpose of relation is identification, and it has been achieved by her name. End. It has occurred in many fatwas that precaution is to uncover her face or mention her name with 'or', and the correct is with 'and' as in 'Umdat al-Fatawa by al-Sadr al-Shahid, because precaution is to combine both, not one of them. In al-Khaniyyah: A man sent a man to propose to a specific woman for him; the messenger went and married her to him – it is valid because he ordered him to propose, and the completion of the proposal is the contract. End. For the agent's contract to be binding, his agreement on the named dowry is required. Hence, in al-Khaniyyah: If he appointed him to marry him to so-and-so for one thousand dirhams, and he married her to him for two thousand, if the husband approves, it is valid; if he rejects, the marriage is void; and if the husband does not know until he has consummated, the option remains. Shams. His statement (And the preferred view in the school is contrary to this etc.) al-Maqdisi said in what is transmitted from him: If he intends that the statement of al-Walwaji supports him, it is prevented, because that is in the validity of the marriage of a veiled woman, i.e., it is the preferred view relative to the statement of Nasir ibn Yahya. What supports this is that the imams, al-Halwani despite his great status, transmitted the statement of al-Khassaf with beautiful descriptions that he is great to be followed; if the preferred view were contrary, he would have pointed it out. End. Something similar is mentioned in al-Ramz, and in it: Al-Walwaji's confinement to contradicting al-Khassaf's statement indicates his choice, and al-Halwani's transmission of it does not imply that it is the preferred view in the school. In al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 3 p. 165.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the ruling that a paternal cousin (ibn amm) may marry his paternal uncle's daughter to himself, and similarly an agent (wakil) may marry his female client to himself. The commentator begins by explaining the reasoning: the agent in marriage is merely an intermediary and transmitter, not a party who acquires rights, unlike in a sale where the agent becomes directly liable. He then provides two hadith proofs: one from Sahih al-Bukhari where Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf married Umm Hakim with her consent in a single utterance, and another from Sunan Abi Dawud where the Prophet (peace be upon him) acted as intermediary in a marriage. The commentator addresses a potential objection from al-Ghayah that the agent is merely an intermediary, noting that if the agent marries his client to his own slave, he becomes obligated to hand over the slave as dowry—not by the contract itself but by his commitment. He clarifies that the ruling about the cousin applies to a minor cousin, where the cousin acts as both principal and guardian; for an adult cousin, she may appoint him as agent or he would be a fuduli (unauthorized person). He then cites al-Muhit and al-Walwajiyyah regarding the conditions for an agent marrying himself: if the woman tells him to marry her to any man, he cannot marry himself because the husband is indefinite and he is definite; an analogy with bequest is distinguished. The commentary also discusses that silence can establish agency, and that witnessing is not required for validity but only for evidence. A significant intra-madhhab dispute is presented: al-Khassaf holds that the agent need not identify the wife to witnesses, while al-Walwaji and the preferred view require identification by name and lineage if she is absent, or by pointing if present. The commentator notes that the preferred view aligns with caution, and that combining both methods (unveiling and naming) is best. Finally, the passage addresses a case where a messenger sent to propose actually marries the woman: it is valid because the proposal implies authorization for the contract. Throughout, the commentator uses Hanafi sources like al-Muhit, al-Walwajiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, and al-Zahiriyyah, demonstrating the school's internal deliberation.

Key Terms
ابن العم (ibn al-amm): Paternal cousin (son of paternal uncle); in this context, he is a guardian (wali) for his minor paternal cousin.
وكيل (wakīl): Agent appointed by a woman to arrange her marriage; in this case, he may marry her to himself under specific conditions.
شهود (shuhūd): Witnesses required for marriage contract; their knowledge of the bride is subject to ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, what must the agent do when marrying his client to himself if she is absent and the witnesses do not know her?
A) He need only say 'I married the woman who appointed me' without naming her.
B) He must mention her name, father's name, and grandfather's name.
C) He must bring her to the witnesses in person.
D) The marriage is invalid in all cases.

Key Takeaway
A wali or wakil can marry himself to his ward/client, but the preferred Hanafi view requires that he identify her to the witnesses by name and lineage if absent, or by indication if present, to avoid invalidation.

Nikah — Marriage

Witness Identification in an Agent's Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness identification in agent marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid testimony in an agent's marriage and distinguish al-Khasaf's view from the chosen (mufta bihi) view.

Core Idea
Witnesses must know the woman; a mere claim 'the woman who authorized me' is insufficient.

This passage addresses a nuanced fiqh issue: when a woman appoints an agent to marry her to himself, must the witnesses explicitly know who she is? Al-Khasaf argued that a general reference suffices, but the majority of Hanafi scholars require specific identification. Understanding this dispute is crucial for ensuring the validity of such marriages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its requirement
The act is a woman appointing an agent to marry her to himself. The requirement is that witnesses must be present, but are they required to know her identity?
2
State al-Khasaf's position
Al-Khasaf held that it is sufficient for the agent to say 'I marry the woman who placed her affair in my hand' without naming her.
He argued that the authorization itself is enough identification.
3
State the chosen (mufta bihi) position
The chosen view requires that if the woman is absent, the agent must mention her name, father's name, and grandfather's name; if present, pointing suffices.
This is to avoid future disputes and align with the opinion of later authorities.
4
Understand the rationale
The purpose of lineage is identification; for an absent person, only naming achieves this. For a present person, pointing works.
The cautious approach combines both name and visual identification.
5
Identify the practical difference
If the agent fails to properly identify, a judge who follows Nasir ibn Yahya (who invalidates such marriages) could nullify it.
Thus, caution is to satisfy all views.

Then he said: A woman appointed a man to marry her for four hundred dirhams, and the agent married her to the husband for one year, then the husband claimed that the agent married her for a dinar, and the agent affirmed that. If the husband admits that the woman did not authorize a dinar, the woman has the option: if she wishes, she may ratify the marriage for a dinar and has nothing else; if she wishes, she may reject the marriage and she is entitled to her proper dowry (mahr al-mithl) whatever it may be, unlike the preceding [case] because there the woman was satisfied with the specified, so when the marriage is void and the dower (uqr) is due by entry, it does not exceed what she was satisfied with. Here, the woman was not satisfied with the specified in the contract, so she gets her proper dowry whatever it may be, and she does not have the waiting period maintenance. If the husband claims authorization for a dinar and she denies, the saying is hers with an oath. This is a matter that needs caution; it is recommended to have witnesses to her affair and she should ratify after the contract if it violates her order. Similarly, the guardian, if she is an adult, does what the agent does. End.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rules governing a woman who appoints a man as her agent to marry her to himself. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute because the author contrasts the view of al-Khasaf (who does not require naming the woman for witnesses) with the chosen view of the madhhab (which requires identification). The passage also covers the consequences if the agent exceeds his mandate regarding the dowry. The author begins by stating that agency can be established by silence, as when a guardian says to a paternal cousin 'I want to marry you' and she remains silent, that is permission. Then the discussion moves to the requirements for witnesses: if the woman is absent, the agent must mention her name, father's name, and grandfather's name; if present, a gesture suffices. The cautious approach is to both uncover her face and mention her name. The passage then addresses what happens when the agent marries her for a different amount than authorized: the husband may ratify or reject, and if he enters without knowing, the option remains. A concrete case is given: a woman authorizes marriage for 400 dirhams, but the agent marries her for a year (i.e., a deferred payment?) or the husband claims a different price. The ruling is that if the husband admits the woman did not authorize the lower amount, she may choose to accept or reject, and if she rejects, she gets mahr al-mithl, not limited to the authorized amount. This differs from a previous case where she had agreed to a specified mahr. The passage concludes with practical advice: the woman should ratify after the contract if the agent violated her instructions, and the guardian acts similarly.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the woman to contract her marriage, possibly to himself.
فضولي (fuḍūlī): A person who acts without authority or guardianship; mentioned here for comparison (the slave's marriage without permission is like that of a fuduli).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what must the agent do when marrying an absent woman to himself?
A) Simply state that he married the woman who appointed him.
B) Mention her name, father's name, and grandfather's name.
C) Uncover her face for the witnesses.
D) Both B and C, as caution combines both.

Key Takeaway
In an agent marriage, witnesses must be able to identify the woman; the cautious view requires both name and sight.

Consequences of the Agent Exceeding Authority on Mahr
Ruling on agent exceeding mahr authority and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when an agent exceeds his authorized mahr and state the options for the husband and woman.

Core Idea
If the agent marries for a different mahr than authorized, the marriage is suspended on the husband's ratification.

This passage deals with a common scenario: the agent contracts the marriage with a different mahr than the woman authorized. The ruling hinges on the husband's acceptance. We explore the consequences of ratification, rejection, and the role of entry, as well as the woman's entitlement to mahr al-mithl when she did not approve the specified amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The woman authorizes the agent to marry her for a specific mahr; the agent marries her for a different amount.
2
State the ruling
The marriage is valid but suspended; it becomes binding if the husband (the agent) ratifies the increase, and void if he rejects.
If the husband enters without knowledge, he retains the option.
3
Explain the woman's options
If the husband rejects, the marriage is void and the woman gets mahr al-mithl (proper dowry), not limited to the authorized amount.
This differs from a case where she had agreed to a specific mahr.
4
Understand the difference
If the woman had agreed to the specified mahr, she cannot claim more than that even after void; here she did not agree, so she gets mahr al-mithl.
This is based on the principle that she did not consent to the term.
5
Practical recommendation
The woman should ratify the contract after the fact if she approves, to avoid disputes.
The same applies to the guardian if she is an adult.

بلغ، وليس لها نفقة العدة، وإن كان الزوج يدعي التوكيل بدينار وهي تنكر كان القول قولها مع اليمين وهذا أمر يحتاط فيه وينبغي أن يشهد على أمرها وتجيزه بعد العقد إذا خالف أمرها، وكذا الولي إذا كانت بالغة يفعل ما يفعله الوكيل اهـ .
Section on compatibility and the marriage of a slave and slave woman without the master's permission is suspended like the marriage of the unauthorized agent (fuduli). And half of the contract is not dependent on her silence. He [the agent] has the right to marry her to himself primarily, as in al-Khaniyya. Agency is established by explicit statement and also by silence, as stated in al-Zahiriyya: If the paternal cousin said 'I want to marry you to myself,' it is permissible. He did not restrict it to a virgin, but it was restricted to a virgin in Ghayat al-Bayan and others. The apparent is that it is specific to the guardian as previously explained. And he [the author] spoke generally about agency, so it indicates that witnessing is not required for validity but only for fear of denial. He did not explain how the agent marries her to himself and whether it is required that the witnesses know her, due to disagreement. Al-Khasaf mentioned that it is not required that they know her or mention her name and lineage to the witnesses, so that even if he said 'I have married the woman who placed her affair in my hand for such a dowry in their presence,' it is valid. But the chosen view in the madhhab is contrary to this, even though al-Khasaf was great in knowledge and followed. Al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa: A woman appointed a man to marry her to himself, so the agent went and said 'Bear witness that I have married so-and-so' while the witnesses did not know so-and-so; the marriage is not valid until he mentions her name, her father's name, and her grandfather's name, because she is absent, and the absent one is only known by relation. Do you not see that if he said 'I married a woman who appointed me for marriage,' it is not valid. If she is present and veiled and the witnesses do not know her, and he said 'Bear witness that I married this woman,' and the woman said 'I married myself to him,' it is valid, and this is the chosen view because she is present, and the present one is known by pointing. If they want caution, they uncover her face so the witnesses know her, or he mentions her name, her father's name, and her grandfather's name so that it is agreed upon, and there is security that anyone who raises it to a judge who holds the opinion of those who do not permit, namely Nasir ibn Yahya, would invalidate the marriage. All this is when the witnesses do not know the woman. If they know her and she is absent, mentioning her name alone is sufficient if the witnesses know that he meant the woman they know, because the purpose of lineage is identification, and it has been achieved by her name. And it appears in many fatawa that caution is to uncover her face or mention her name with the word 'or', but the correct view is with 'and' as in 'Umdat al-Fatawa by al-Sadr al-Shahid, because caution is to combine both, not one of them. In al-Khaniyya: A man sent a man to propose to a specific woman, and the messenger went and married her to him; it is valid because he ordered him to propose, and the entirety of the proposal is the contract. It is a condition for the bindingness of the agent's contract that he agrees with the specified dowry, so in al-Khaniyya: If he authorized him to marry him to so-and-so for a thousand dirhams, and he married her to him for two thousand, then if the husband ratifies, it is valid; if he rejects, the marriage is void. If the husband did not know of that until he entered upon her, the option remains. [Gloss: 'and the chosen in the madhhab is contrary to this' etc. Al-Maqdisi said: If he intended that al-Walwaliji's statement supports him, it is prevented because that concerns the validity of the marriage of a veiled woman; it is the chosen view relative to Nasir ibn Yahya's statement. Supporting this is that the imams, including al-Halwani with his great rank, transmitted al-Khasaf's statement with beautiful description, that he is great and followed; if the chosen were contrary, he would have alerted to it. Similar is mentioned in al-Ramz: that al-Walwaliji's restriction to contrary of al-Khasaf's statement suggests his choice, and al-Halwani's transmission does not indicate that it is the chosen in the madhhab.] And [she] established the marriage... section on compatibility: If he ratifies, then the specified dowry is due and nothing else. If he rejects, the marriage is void, and the proper dowry (mahr al-mithl) is required if it is less than the specified; otherwise the specified is required. If the husband does not accept the increase and the agent says 'I will pay the increase and bind you to the marriage,' he does not have that. Then he said: A woman appointed a man to marry her for four hundred dirhams, and the agent married her to the husband for one year, then the husband claimed that the agent married her for a dinar, and the agent affirmed that. If the husband admits that the woman did not authorize a dinar, the woman has the option: if she wishes, she may ratify the marriage for a dinar and has nothing else; if she wishes, she may reject the marriage and she is entitled to her proper dowry (mahr al-mithl) whatever it may be, unlike the preceding [case] because there the woman was satisfied with the specified, so when the marriage is void and the dower (uqr) is due by entry, it does not exceed what she was satisfied with. Here, the woman was not satisfied with the specified in the contract, so she gets her proper dowry whatever it may be, and she does not have the waiting period maintenance. If the husband claims authorization for a dinar and she denies, the saying is hers with an oath. This is a matter that needs caution; it is recommended to have witnesses to her affair and she should ratify after the contract if it violates her order. Similarly, the guardian, if she is an adult, does what the agent does. End.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rules governing a woman who appoints a man as her agent to marry her to himself. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute because the author contrasts the view of al-Khasaf (who does not require naming the woman for witnesses) with the chosen view of the madhhab (which requires identification). The passage also covers the consequences if the agent exceeds his mandate regarding the dowry. The author begins by stating that agency can be established by silence, as when a guardian says to a paternal cousin 'I want to marry you' and she remains silent, that is permission. Then the discussion moves to the requirements for witnesses: if the woman is absent, the agent must mention her name, father's name, and grandfather's name; if present, a gesture suffices. The cautious approach is to both uncover her face and mention her name. The passage then addresses what happens when the agent marries her for a different amount than authorized: the husband may ratify or reject, and if he enters without knowing, the option remains. A concrete case is given: a woman authorizes marriage for 400 dirhams, but the agent marries her for a year (i.e., a deferred payment?) or the husband claims a different price. The ruling is that if the husband admits the woman did not authorize the lower amount, she may choose to accept or reject, and if she rejects, she gets mahr al-mithl, not limited to the authorized amount. This differs from a previous case where she had agreed to a specified mahr. The passage concludes with practical advice: the woman should ratify after the contract if the agent violated her instructions, and the guardian acts similarly.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the woman to contract her marriage, possibly to himself.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dowry equivalent to what women of similar status in her family would receive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent authorized for a mahr of 400 dirhams marries the woman for a dinar (which is less). The husband claims the agent was authorized for a dinar. Who has the burden of proof?
A) The husband must prove authorization for a dinar.
B) The woman must deny the authorization.
C) The woman's statement is taken with an oath.
D) The agent must prove his claim.

Key Takeaway
When an agent marries with a different mahr than authorized, the marriage is suspended on the husband's acceptance; rejection voids it.

Definition and Ruling of Fuduli (Unauthorized Agent) in Marriage
Defines fuduli, states ruling, rebuts Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the fuduli's marriage contract and explain why it is suspended rather than void, contrasting with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A fuduli's marriage contract is valid but pending — not void, because the ruling can be delayed.

This passage defines the fuduli (unauthorized agent) and presents the Hanafi position that his contract is suspended (mawquf), not void. It contrasts with the Shafi'i view that such contracts are batil. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of contractual validity in Hanafi fiqh and the concept of delayed legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fuduli and the Hanafi ruling
The fuduli is one who acts without authority. His contract is sahih ghayr nafidh (suspended).
The passage analogizes a slave's marriage to a fuduli's.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i holds that all fuduli contracts are void because the contract cannot produce its immediate effect.
For Shafi'i, void means batil, not salvageable.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The contract is placed for its effect; the fuduli cannot establish it, so it is futile (laghw).
This is a purely aqli (rational) argument.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The pillar (rukn) is sound because it issues from a competent person; the ruling can be delayed, as seen in a minor's contract.
Delayed ruling is not a conceptual impossibility.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi: the contract becomes operative if ratified later; Shafi'i: it never becomes operative and must be re-contracted.
This practical difference affects whether a marriage can be saved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ونكاح العبد والأمة بغير إذن السيد موقوف كنكاح الفضولي) شروع في بيان الفضولي وبعض أحكامه، وهو من يتصرف لغيره بغير ولاية ولا وكالة أو لنفسه وليس أهلاً له. وإنما زدناه ليدخل نكاح العبد بغير إذن إن قلنا إنه فضولي وإلا فهو ملحق به في أحكامه. والفضولي جمع فضل غلب في الاشتغال بما لا يعنيه وما لا ولاية له فيه، فقول بعض الجهلة لمن يأمر بالمعروف أنت فضولي يخشى عليه الكفر، وصفته أنه عقد صحيح غير نافذ، والأصل أن كل عقد صدر من الفضولي وله مجيز انعقد موقوفاً على الإجازة. وقال الشافعي : تصرفات الفضولي كلها باطلة لأن العقد وضع لحكمه والفضولي لا يقدر على إثبات الحكم فيلغو ولنا أن ركن التصرف صدر من أهله مضافاً إلى محله ولا ضرر في انعقاده فينعقد موقوفاً حتى إذا رأى المصلحة فيه ينفذه، وقد يتراخى حكم العقد عن العقد. وفسر المجيز في النهاية بقابل يقبل الإيجاب، سواء كان فضولياً أو وكيلاً أو أصيلاً، فإن كان له مجيز حالة العقد توقف وإلا بطل بيانه الصبي إذا باع ما له أو اشترى أو تزوج أو زوج أمته أو كاتب عبده أو نحوه يتوقف على إجازة الولي في حالة الصغر
His saying: (And the marriage of a slave and slave woman without the master's permission is suspended like the marriage of the unauthorized agent) is a beginning in explaining the unauthorized agent (fuduli) and some of his rules. He is one who acts for another without guardianship or agency, or for himself while not being qualified for it. We only added this to include the marriage of a slave without permission if we say he is a fuduli, otherwise he is attached to it in his rules. The word fuduli is a plural of fadl (superfluous); it applies to one who busies himself with what does not concern him and what he has no authority over. So the statement of some ignorant people to one who enjoins good, 'You are a fuduli,' risks disbelief. His description is that his contract is valid but not executed (ghayr nafidh). The principle is that every contract issued by a fuduli, if there exists a ratifier (mujiz), is concluded as suspended (mawquf) upon ratification. Al-Shafi'i said: All transactions of the fuduli are void because the contract is placed for its effect, and the fuduli cannot establish the effect, so it is futile. Our proof is that the pillar (rukn) of the transaction issued from a qualified person, attached to its place, and there is no harm in its conclusion, so it is concluded as suspended, so that when he sees benefit in it, he enforces it. And the ruling of the contract may be delayed from the contract. And the ratifier (mujiz) is explained in al-Nihaya as one who accepts the offer (qabil yaqbal al-ijab), whether he is a fuduli, an agent, or a principal. If there is a ratifier at the time of the contract, it is suspended; otherwise it is void. Its statement is the minor if he sells his property, or buys, or marries, or marries off his slave woman, or makes a kitaba contract for his slave, or similar, it is suspended upon the guardian's ratification during minority.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the fuduli (unauthorized agent), specifically in the context of marriage. It begins by explaining that the marriage of a slave without the master's permission is analogous to that of a fuduli: both are suspended (mawquf) pending ratification. The author defines the fuduli as one who acts without legal authority (wilaya) or agency (wakala), either for someone else or for himself when he is not qualified (e.g., a slave marrying without permission). The term 'fuduli' literally means 'busybody' and is used for someone interfering in what is not his concern. The author notes that using this term for someone enjoining good is blameworthy. The legal description of a fuduli's contract is that it is 'sahih ghayr nafidh'—valid in its fundamental elements but not operative until ratified. The principle is that if there exists a potential ratifier (mujiz), the contract is concluded as suspended. The author then presents the Shafi'i objection: all fuduli transactions are void because the contract is intended to produce its legal effect immediately, and the fuduli cannot do so. The Hanafi response is that the essential pillar (rukn) of the transaction (e.g., offer and acceptance) proceeds from someone qualified (the fuduli himself is qualified to utter the words) and is attached to its proper subject; there is no harm in allowing it to be suspended, as the ruling can be delayed. The ratifier is defined as anyone who can accept the offer, whether he is a fuduli, an agent, or the principal himself. The existence of a ratifier at the time of contract causes suspension; otherwise the contract is void. The example of a minor's transactions is given: they are suspended on the guardian's ratification during minority.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuḍūlī): A person who acts without authority (wilaya or wakala) for another, or acts for himself when not legally qualified (e.g., a slave marrying without permission).
مجيز (mujīz): The person who has the authority to ratify (ijaza) a suspended contract; defined as 'one who accepts the offer' (qabil yaqbal al-ijab).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man (without being a guardian or agent) marries a woman to someone else, the contract is:
A) Void (batil) and cannot be ratified.
B) Valid and immediately binding.
C) Suspended (mawquf) pending ratification by the woman's guardian.
D) Valid only if the woman herself ratifies immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognises the fuduli's contract as valid but suspended, allowing ratification to complete its effect.

Woman's Option When Wakil Marries for Less than Named Dower
Ruling on woman's khiyar when wakil violates dower instruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to a woman when her wakil marries her for less than the specified dower, and distinguish the ruling based on whether the woman had consented to the named dower.

Core Idea
A woman may ratify a marriage contracted with a lesser dower or reject it and claim the proper dower.

When a woman appoints an agent (wakil) to conduct her marriage contract, the agent must adhere to her instructions. If the wakil violates her instructions by setting a lower dower than specified, the marriage is not automatically binding on the woman. She has a choice: accept the marriage with the lower dower, or reject it and demand her proper dower (mahr al-mithl). This lesson explores the nuances of this ruling, including the evidentiary burden when there is a dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The woman appoints a wakil to marry her for a specific dower. The wakil marries her for a lesser amount without her knowledge.
2
Determine the woman's options
She may ratify the marriage with the lower dower, or reject it, thereby voiding the marriage.
The marriage is valid upon conclusion but subject to the woman's right to rescind.
3
Analyze the dower consequences
If she ratifies, the lower dower is due. If she rejects and the marriage was consummated, the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is due, which may be more or less than the originally specified amount.
If the proper dower is less than the named dower, the named dower is due.
4
Compare with the consent scenario
In a previous case (mentioned in the text), the woman had consented to the named dower before the contract, so she could not claim more. Here she did not consent, so she is entitled to the proper dower.
This distinction is crucial for determining the amount owed.

وإذا أقامت
كتاب النكاح فصل في الكفاءة
إن أجاز كان عليه المسمى لا غير، وإن رد بطل النكاح فيجب مهر المثل ان كان أقل من المسمى وإلا يجب المسمى، وإن لم يرض الزوج بالزيادة فقال الوكيل أنا أغرم الزيادة وألزمكما النكاح لم يكن له ذلك . ثم قال امرأة وكلت رجلاً ليزوجها بأربعمائة درهم فزوجها الوكيل مع الزوج سنة ثم زعم الزوج أن الوكيل زوجها منه بدينار وصدقة الوكيل في ذلك، فلو كان الزوج مقراً أن المرأة لم توكله بدينار كانت المرأة بالخيار إن شاءت أجازت النكاح بدينار وليس لها غير ذلك، وإن شاءت ردت النكاح ولها عليه مهر مثلها بالغاً ما بلغ بخلاف تقدم لأن ثمة المرأة رضيت بالمسمى، فإذا بطل النكاح ووجب العقر بالدخول لا يزاد على ما رضيت، أما هنا المرأة ما رضيت بالمسمى في العقد فكان لها مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ، وليس لها نفقة العدة، وإن كان الزوج يدعي التوكيل بدينار وهي تنكر كان القول قولها مع اليمين وهذا أمر يحتاط فيه وينبغي أن يشهد على أمرها وتجيزه بعد العقد إذا خالف أمرها، وكذا الولي إذا كانت بالغة يفعل ما يفعله الوكيل اهـ .
And if she appoints [a wakil]... Chapter on Marriage, Section on Compatibility. If he ratifies, then the named dower is due, nothing else. If he rejects, the marriage becomes void and the proper dower is due if it is less than the named dower; otherwise the named dower is due. If the husband does not accept the increase and the wakil says, 'I will pay the increase and bind you both to the marriage,' he does not have that right. Then he said: A woman appointed a man to marry her for four hundred dirhams, but the wakil married her to the husband for a dinar. Then the husband claims that the wakil married her to him for a dinar, and the wakil confirms this. If the husband admits that the woman did not authorize him for a dinar, then the woman has the choice: if she wishes, she may ratify the marriage for a dinar and nothing else; if she wishes, she may reject the marriage and she has the right to her proper dower, whatever it may be, unlike the previous case, because in that case the woman had consented to the named dower. So when the marriage becomes void and the dower is obligatory due to consummation, it is not increased beyond what she consented to. Here, the woman did not consent to the named dower in the contract, so she has the right to her proper dower, whatever it may be. She has no right to maintenance during the waiting period. If the husband claims that she authorized [the wakil] for a dinar and she denies, then her word is taken with her oath. This matter requires caution, and it is proper that her affair be witnessed and that she ratify it after the contract if it contradicts her instruction. Likewise, the guardian, if she is an adult, does what the wakil does. End.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a scenario where a woman appoints a wakil (agent) to marry her for a specific dower (400 dirhams), but the wakil marries her for a lower amount (a dinar). The author explains the options. If the husband ratifies, the dower is the lower amount as agreed. If the husband rejects, the marriage is void and the woman gets the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) if less than the named, otherwise the named. But if the woman rejects, she gets full proper dower. The key distinction is that in the previous case (referred to as 'bikhilaf taqaddum'), the woman had consented to the named dower before the contract, so she cannot claim more; here she did not. She also does not get 'iddah maintenance. If the husband claims she authorized for a dinar and she denies, her word with oath is accepted. The passage advises caution and suggests having witnesses.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the woman to conduct her marriage contract.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower of a woman of similar status, used when the named dower is invalid or no dower is mentioned.
عقر (ʿuqar): The dower due for consummation of a void marriage (nikah fasid).
نفقة العدة (nafaqat al-ʿiddah): Maintenance during the waiting period after divorce or annulment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman appointed a wakil to marry her for 400 dirhams, but the wakil married her for 100 dirhams without her knowledge. The husband admits the wakil exceeded his authority. What are the woman's options?
A) She must accept the marriage for 100 dirhams.
B) She may ratify the marriage for 100 dirhams or reject it and claim the proper dower.
C) The marriage is void automatically and she gets 400 dirhams.
D) Her guardian must decide.

Key Takeaway
When a wakil violates the woman's dower instruction, she has the option to ratify or reject; if she rejects, she is entitled to a proper dower, and in disputes, her word with oath is taken.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Definition and Ruling of Fudooli in Marriage
Definition of fudooli and Hanafi ruling on his marriage contracts with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of fudooli, state that his marriage contract is mawqoof (suspended), and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position that it is void.

Core Idea
A contract by an unauthorized person is valid but suspended — ratification can give it effect.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the fudooli (unauthorized agent) and presents the Hanafi ruling that his marriage contract is mawqoof — valid in its formation but not effective until ratified by the rightful party. The text then contrasts the Shafi'i view that such contracts are absolutely void, providing the proof for each position. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly applying the rules of marriage contracts and appreciating the Hanafi approach to contractual validity.

Guided Path
1
Define fudooli
Identify the Hanafi definition: one who acts on behalf of another without guardianship or agency, or for himself without capacity. Note the inclusion of a slave marrying without permission.
Fudooli literally means 'one who busies himself with what does not concern him.'
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The marriage contract of a fudooli is mawqoof (suspended) — valid (sahih) but not effective (ghayr nafidh) until ratified by the person with the right to consent.
Mawqoof is a distinct Hanafi category between valid and void.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The pillar (rukn) of the contract came from a qualified person and is attached to its proper place; there is no harm in delaying the effect. The rule of a contract can be deferred.
This is a rational (aqli) argument based on the nature of contracts.
4
Understand the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that contracts are designed to produce effects immediately; since the fudooli cannot produce the effect, the contract is void (laghw).
For Shafi'i, no subsequent ratification can cure the defect.
5
Identify the practical difference
Under Hanafi, a woman married by a fudooli may ratify the marriage, making it valid from the beginning. Under Shafi'i, the marriage is void and a new contract is required.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf — the real consequence of the legal difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ونكاح العبد والأمة بغير إذن السيد موقوف كنكاح الفضولي) شروع في بيان الفضولي وبعض أحكامه، وهو من يتصرف لغيره بغير ولاية ولا وكالة أو لنفسه وليس أهلاً له. وإنما زدناه ليدخل نكاح العبد بغير إذن إن قلنا إنه فضولي وإلا فهو ملحق به في أحكامه. والفضولي جمع فضل غلب في الاشتغال بما لا يعنيه وما لا ولاية له فيه، فقول بعض الجهلة لمن يأمر بالمعروف أنت فضولي يخشى عليه الكفر، وصفته أنه عقد صحيح غير نافذ، والأصل أن كل عقد صدر من الفضولي وله مجيز انعقد موقوفاً على الإجازة. وقال الشافعي : تصرفات الفضولي كلها باطلة لأن العقد وضع لحكمه والفضولي لا يقدر على إثبات الحكم فيلغو ولنا أن ركن التصرف صدر من أهله مضافاً إلى محله ولا ضرر في انعقاده فينعقد موقوفاً حتى إذا رأى المصلحة فيه ينفذه، وقد يتراخى حكم العقد عن العقد. وفسر المجيز في النهاية بقابل يقبل الإيجاب، سواء كان فضولياً أو وكيلاً أو أصيلاً، فإن كان له مجيز حالة العقد توقف وإلا بطل بيانه الصبي إذا باع ما له أو اشترى أو تزوج أو زوج أمته أو كاتب عبده أو نحوه يتوقف على إجازة الولي في حالة الصغر ، فلو بلغ قبل أن يجيزه الولي فأجازه بنفسه نفذ لأنها كانت متوقفة ولا ينفذ بمجرد بلوغه ولو طلق الصبي امرأته أو خلعها أو أعتق عبده على مال أو دونه أو وهب أو تصدق أو زوج عبده أو باع ما له بمحاباة فاحشة أو اشترى بأكثر من القيمة بما لا يتغابن فيه أو غير ذلك مما لو فعله وليه لا ينفذ كانت هذه الصور باطلة غير متوقفة ولو أجازها بعد البلوغ لعدم المجيز وقت العقد إلا إذا كانت لفظ الإجازة يصلح لابتداء العقد فيصح على وجه الإنشاء كأن يقول بعد البلوغ أوقعت ذلك الطلاق والعتاق اهـ. قال في فتح القدير : وهذا أن يفسر المجيز هنا بمن يقدر على يوجب إمضاء العقد لا بالقابل مطلقاً ولا بالولي إذ لا توقف في هذه الصور وإن قبل فضولي آخر أو ولي لعدم قدرة الولي على إمضائها .اهـ. ومن الباطل لكونه لا مجيز له تزويجه أمة وتحته حرة أو أخت امرأته أو خامسة أو صغيرة في دار الحرب إذا لم يكن سلطان ولا قاض، وأما كفالة المكاتب وتوكيله بعتق عبده ووصيته بعين من ماله فصحيح إذا أجاز بعد عتقه إلا في الأول فبغير إجازة لما عرف في التبيين. ودخل تحت تعريف الفضولي ما لو علق طلاق زوجة غيره بشرط فهو موقوف، فإن أجاز الزوج تعلق فتطلق بوجود الشرط، ولو وجد قبلها لم تطلق عندها إلا إذا وجد ثانياً بعدها كما في فتح القدير. ولذا قلنا «من يتصرف» ولم نقل «من يعقد عقداً ولذا فسر في فتح القدير المجيز بمن يقدر على الإمضاء لا بالقابل إذ ليس في اليمين قابل . وفي التجنيس : حر تزوج عشر نسوة بغير إذنهن فبلغهن الخبر فأجزن جميعاً جاز نكاح التاسعة والعاشرة لأنه لما تزوج الخامسة كان رد النكاح الأربع ، فلما تزوج التاسعة كان رد النكاح الأربع الأخر فبقي نكاح التاسعة والعاشرة موقوفاً على إجازتهما اهـ. وفي الخانية : عبد تزوج امرأة بغير إذن المولى ثم امرأة ثم امرأة فبلغ المولى فأجاز الكل، فإن لم يكن دخل بهن جاز نكاح الثالثة لأن الإقدام على نكاح الثالثة فسخ لنكاح الأولى والثانية فيتوقف نكاح الثالثة فينفذ بإجازة المولى، وإن كان دخل بهن لا يصح نكاحهن لأن الإقدام على نكاح الثالثة عدة الأولى والثانية لم يصح فلم يكن فسخاً لما قبلها فلا تصح إجازة المولى كما لو تزوجهن في عدة واحدة .اهـ. وهذا يوجب تقييد ما في التجنيس أيضاً. وقوله «موقوف» أي على الإجازة فلو تزوج بغير إذن السيد ثم أذن السيد لا ينفذ لأن الإذن ليس بإجازة فلا بد من إجازة العبد في فقد يخطب الشخص لينظر ما يجاب به وما يشترط عليه وما يطلب منه قوله (لما عرف في التبيين) حيث قال لأن كفالته جائزة في حق نفسه نافذة عليه لأنها التزام المال في الذمة وذمته مملوكة له قابلة للإلزام وإنما لا يظهر في الحال لحق المولى، فإذا زال المانع بالعتق ظهر موجبه، وأما التوكيل والوصية فالإجازة فيهما إنشاء لأنهما ينعقدان بلفظ الإجازة والإنشاء لا يستدعى عقداً سابقاً قوله (ولو وجد قبلها) أي لو وجد الشرط قبل الإجازة لم تطلق عندها أي عند الإجازة إلا إذا وجد الشرط ثانياً بعد الإجازة قوله (لأن الأقدام على نكاح الثالثة فسخ الخ) قال المقدسي فيما نقل عنه : ينبغي تقييده بما إذا كان عالماً بالحكم وإلا ففي هذا الزمان الذي غلب فيه الجهل ربما لا يقصد بالثالثة إبطال الأولين وكذا ما قبله اهـ ومثله في الرمز قال ولا سيما أن مالكاً يجيز الأربع للعبد وقد عذرت الأمة بالجهل لاشتغالها بالخدمة .
His saying: (The marriage of a slave and a slave woman without the master's permission is suspended, like the marriage of a fudooli.) This is a beginning of explaining the fudooli and some of its rulings. He is one who acts on behalf of another without guardianship or agency, or acts for himself but is not qualified. We added this to include the slave's marriage without permission if we say he is a fudooli; otherwise he is annexed to him in his rulings. Fudooli is the intensive form of fadl, prevailing in busying oneself with what does not concern him and in which he has no authority. So the saying of some ignorant people to one who enjoins good, 'You are a fudooli,' one fears disbelief for him. Its description is that it is a valid contract that is not effective. The principle is that every contract issued by a fudooli, if it has a ratifier, is concluded as suspended pending ratification. Al-Shafi'i said: All actions of a fudooli are void because the contract was placed for its effect and the fudooli cannot establish the effect, so it is null. We argue: The pillar of the action issued from one qualified to do so, attached to its proper place, and there is no harm in its conclusion, so it is concluded as suspended, so that if he sees benefit in it, he can give effect to it; and the rule of a contract may be deferred from the contract itself. And 'mujiz' (ratifier) is interpreted in al-Nihayah as one who accepts the offer, whether he is a fudooli, agent, or principal. If there is a ratifier at the time of the contract, it is suspended; otherwise it is void. Its explanation: A minor who sells his property or buys, or marries, or marries off his slave woman, or makes a kitabah contract with his slave, or similar, is suspended pending the guardian's ratification during minority. If he attains puberty before the guardian ratifies, and he ratifies it himself, it becomes effective because it was suspended; it does not become effective by mere puberty. If the minor divorces his wife, or makes khul', or frees his slave for a consideration or without, or gifts, or gives charity, or marries off his slave, or sells his property with extravagant favor, or buys at more than value in a way not normally overlooked, or other such things that if his guardian did would not be effective — these forms are void and not suspended, even if he ratifies after puberty, due to the absence of a ratifier at the time of contract, unless the expression of ratification can serve as an initiation of the contract, so it becomes valid as a new inception, like saying after puberty, 'I effect that divorce and that emancipation.' End. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This is that 'mujiz' here is interpreted as one who can cause the contract to be effective, not the acceptor absolutely, nor the guardian, since there is no suspension in these forms even if another fudooli or guardian accepts, due to the inability of the guardian to give effect to them. End. Among the void cases due to having no ratifier is marrying a slave woman while having a free wife, or a sister of his wife, or a fifth wife, or a minor in dar al-harb when there is no sultan or qadi. As for the kafalah of a mukatab, his appointment of an agent to free his slave, and his will of a specific item from his property — these are valid if he ratifies after his emancipation, except the first: without ratification, as known in al-Tabyin. Included under the definition of fudooli is if he suspends the divorce of another's wife on a condition: it is suspended. If the husband ratifies, it becomes attached and she is divorced upon occurrence of the condition. If the condition occurred before ratification, she is not divorced at that time (i.e., at ratification) unless it occurs a second time after ratification, as in Fath al-Qadir. Hence we said, 'Who acts' and did not say, 'Who makes a contract.' Hence 'mujiz' in Fath al-Qadir is interpreted as one who can cause effectiveness, not the acceptor, since there is no acceptable acceptor in the oath. And in al-Tajnis: A free man married ten women without their permission; they heard the news and all ratified. The marriage of the ninth and tenth is valid because when he married the fifth, it revoked the first four; when he married the ninth, it revoked the other four, so the marriages of the ninth and tenth remained suspended pending their ratification. End. And in al-Khaniyah: A slave married a woman without the master's permission, then a woman, then a woman; the master was informed and ratified all. If he had not consummated with them, the marriage of the third is valid because proceeding to the third marriage revokes the first and second, so the third marriage is suspended and takes effect by the master's ratification. If he had consummated with them, their marriages are not valid because proceeding to the third marriage while the 'iddah of the first and second was still ongoing is invalid, so it did not revoke the previous ones; thus the master's ratification is not valid, as if he married them in the same 'iddah. End. This requires restricting what is in al-Tajnis as well. And his saying 'suspended' means pending ratification. If he marries without the master's permission and then the master gives permission, it does not take effect because permission is not ratification; so the slave's ratification is necessary. For he may propose to see what response will be given, what conditions are imposed, and what is demanded from him. His saying (as known in al-Tabyin) where he said: Because his kafalah is valid in his own right and binding upon him, as it is an obligation of wealth in the liability, and his liability is owned by him, capable of being obligated; it is only not manifested at present due to the master's right. When the impediment is removed by emancipation, its requirement becomes manifest. As for agency and will, ratification in them is an inception because they are concluded with the word of ratification, and inception does not require a prior contract. His saying (if it occurred before it) — i.e., if the condition occurred before ratification, she is not divorced at that time (at ratification) unless the condition occurs a second time after ratification. His saying (because proceeding to the third marriage is a revocation, etc.) — al-Maqdisi said in what is transmitted from him: It should be restricted to the case where he knows the ruling; otherwise, in this time when ignorance prevails, perhaps he does not intend by the third to revoke the first two, and likewise what preceded. End. Similar is in al-Ramz: He said, especially since Malik permits four for the slave, and the slave woman is excused due to ignorance because of her occupation with service.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the legal status of a contract made by a fudooli (unauthorized agent). The Hanafi school defines a fudooli as one who acts on behalf of another without authority (guardianship or agency) or acts for himself without legal capacity. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that such a contract is 'mawqoof' (suspended) — meaning it is valid in its formation but not effective until ratified by the person who has the right to authorize it. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, holding that all transactions of a fudooli are absolutely void (batil) because the contract is intended to produce effects, and the fudooli cannot bring about those effects. The Hanafi response is that the essential elements (rukn) of the contract are present: a qualified person (the fudooli is capable of utterance and understanding), an object appropriate for the contract, and there is no harm in suspending the effect until a ratifier (mujiz) appears. The text then explains the concept of 'mujiz' — the one who can approve the contract. According to al-Nihayah, the mujiz is the party accepting the offer, but later in Fath al-Qadir, the mujiz is defined as one who can enforce the contract (i.e., the owner of the right). The passage then distinguishes between cases where the contract is batil without being mawqoof: actions of a minor that are inherently harmful (like excessive gifts) are void even if later ratified, because at the time of contract there was no one capable of ratification. Other examples include marriages that are prohibited by law (e.g., marrying a fifth wife or a sister of one's wife) — these are void ab initio with no chance of ratification. The discussion includes rulings on slaves marrying without permission, conditional divorce of another's wife, and multiple marriages by a free man without permission. The passage emphasizes the importance of intention: for the rule that a third marriage revokes previous ones, al-Maqdisi restricts it to those who know the ruling, as in later times ignorance may prevail.

Key Terms
فضولي (fudūlī): One who enters into a contract on behalf of another without legal authority (guardianship or agency), or for himself without capacity.
موقوف (mawqūf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but not effective until ratified by the person who has the right to do so.
مجيز (mujīz): The one who ratifies a suspended contract, making it effective. In this text, interpreted as the person who can enforce the contract.
إجازة (ijāzah): Ratification; the act of approving a suspended contract after it has been concluded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of a marriage contract conducted by a fudooli (unauthorized agent)?
A) It is void (batil) and cannot be ratified.
B) It is valid (sahih) and immediately effective.
C) It is suspended (mawqoof) pending ratification by the person who has the right.
D) It is void if the fudooli is a stranger, but valid if he is a relative.

Key Takeaway
A fudooli's contract is valid but not effective until ratified; this distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i who regard it as void.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Al-Fuduli and Void Marriages Without a Potential Ratifier
Defining fuduli and listing void marriages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-fuduli and state which marriage contracts are void because they lack a potential ratifier.

Core Idea
A fuduli's marriage contract is suspended if a ratifier exists; otherwise it is void.

The concept of the fuduli is central to Hanafi contract law. In marriage, a fuduli acts without ownership or agency. His action is not automatically void—it can be ratified if there is someone with the authority to do so. But not all cases have such a potential ratifier. This passage lists those marriage scenarios that are void from the outset because no one can ratify them. Understanding these is essential for correctly distinguishing suspendable contracts from void ones.

Guided Path
1
Define the fuduli
The passage defines fuduli as 'one who transacts' (من يتصرف) rather than 'one who contracts'. Note that the definition excludes oaths and other acts where no passive party exists.
The text emphasizes the act of transacting, not just contracting.
2
Identify the condition for suspension
A fuduli's contract is suspended (mawquf) only if there exists a potential ratifier (mjiz) at the time of the contract. If no such ratifier exists, the contract is batil from the start.
The ratifier is defined as the one who can execute the contract, not merely the passive party or guardian.
3
List the void marriage scenarios
From the passage: marrying a slave woman while having a free wife, marrying the sister of one's wife, marrying a fifth wife, or marrying a young girl in dar al-harb without a sultan or judge. These have no potential ratifier.
These are examples of marriages that cannot be cured by later ratification.
4
Understand the exception for new inception
If the wording of ratification can also initiate a new contract (e.g., 'I execute that divorce' after puberty), it may be valid as a new inception, not as ratification.
This applies to divorce and emancipation as well.
5
Apply to non-marriage cases
The passage also mentions the kafala of a mukatab and his agency for freeing his slave—these are valid only upon ratification after emancipation, except the first which is valid without ratification.
Shows broader application of the fuduli concept.

كتاب النكاح فصل في الكفاءة ٢٤٣ الصور باطلة غير متوقفة ولو أجازها بعد البلوغ لعدم المجيز وقت العقد إلا إذا كانت لفظ الإجازة يصلح لابتداء العقد فيصح على وجه الإنشاء كأن يقول بعد البلوغ أوقعت ذلك الطلاق والعتاق اهـ. قال في فتح القدير : وهذا أن يفسر المجيز هنا بمن يقدر على يوجب إمضاء العقد لا بالقابل مطلقاً ولا بالولي إذ لا توقف في هذه الصور وإن قبل فضولي آخر أو ولي لعدم قدرة الولي على إمضائها .اهـ. ومن الباطل لكونه لا مجيز له تزويجه أمة وتحته حرة أو أخت امرأته أو خامسة أو صغيرة في دار الحرب إذا لم يكن سلطان ولا قاض، وأما كفالة المكاتب وتوكيله بعتق عبده ووصيته بعين من ماله فصحيح إذا أجاز بعد عتقه إلا في الأول فبغير إجازة لما عرف في التبيين. ودخل تحت تعريف الفضولي ما لو علق طلاق زوجة غيره بشرط فهو موقوف، فإن أجاز الزوج تعلق فتطلق بوجود الشرط، ولو وجد قبلها لم تطلق عندها إلا إذا وجد ثانياً بعدها كما في فتح القدير. ولذا قلنا «من يتصرف» ولم نقل «من يعقد عقداً ولذا فسر في فتح القدير المجيز بمن يقدر على الإمضاء لا بالقابل إذ ليس في اليمين قابل .
Book of Nikah, Section on Compatibility. The invalid scenarios are those that are not suspendable, even if she ratifies after puberty, because there was no one with the capacity to ratify at the time of the contract, except if the word of ratification is suitable to initiate a contract, so it is valid as an inception, like if she says after puberty: 'I execute that divorce and emancipation.' This ends. Al-Marghinani said in Fath al-Qadir: This means that mjiz here is interpreted as the one who has the power to necessitate the execution of the contract, not the passive party absolutely, nor the guardian, because there is no suspension in these scenarios, even if another fuduli or guardian accepts, due to the guardian's inability to execute them. And among the void scenarios due to there being no ratifier: marrying a slave woman while he has a free woman, or marrying the sister of his wife, or a fifth wife, or a young girl in dar al-harb when there is no sultan or judge. As for the kafala of a mukatab, his appointment of an agent to free his slave, and his will of a specific item of his property, these are valid if he ratifies after emancipation, except the first, which is valid without ratification, as is known in al-Tabyin. Included under the definition of al-fuduli is: if he suspends the divorce of another's wife on a condition, it is suspended; if the husband ratifies, it becomes contingent, and divorce occurs upon the condition's existence. If the condition existed before ratification, it does not occur upon ratification, unless it occurs again after ratification, as in Fath al-Qadir. Therefore we said: 'one who transacts' and not 'one who contracts', and therefore it is explained in Fath al-Qadir that the ratifier is the one who has the power to execute, not the passive party, since in an oath there is no passive party.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage opens the section on compatibility (kafa'a) but actually delves into the rules of the fuduli (unauthorized agent) in marriage. The author first clarifies that certain marriage scenarios are absolutely void (bātil) because they lack any potential ratifier at the time of contract. For example, a marriage to a fifth wife or to a slave woman when the husband already has a free wife. These cannot be saved by later ratification. However, if the word used for ratification can also initiate a new contract, it may be valid as a new inception. The author then cites Fath al-Qadir to define the 'ratifier' (mjiz) as the one who can enforce the contract, not the passive party. The passage also includes the ruling on the kafala of a mukatab and the fuduli's role in suspending divorce. The key takeaway: a fuduli's act is suspendable only if there is a potential ratifier; otherwise, it is void.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): A person who transacts in a contract without being the owner or an agent.
مجيز (mjiz): The one who has the authority to ratify the contract.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended contract awaiting ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A fuduli's marriage is void if no potential ratifier exists at the time of contract; only when a ratifier exists is the contract suspendable.

Multiple Marriages by a Fuduli: Ratification, Rescission, and Consummation
Cases of multiple fuduli marriages and ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine which of a sequence of fuduli marriages are validated by ratification, applying the Hanafi rule of implied rescission and the condition of non-consummation.

Core Idea
Proceeding to a marriage beyond the permitted number implicitly rescinds earlier ones, but consummation blocks that rescission.

This lesson delves into two intricate cases from al-Tajnis and al-Khaniyya that illustrate how a fuduli's multiple marriages are affected by ratification. Understanding the interplay between the order of contracts and the fact of consummation is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi nikah rulings in such scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
First, a free man marries ten women without their permission, and they later ratify. Second, a slave marries three women without his master's permission, and the master ratifies.
2
Understand the rule of implied rescission
In Hanafi law, when a free man marries a fifth woman, it implicitly rescinds the first four. Similarly, marrying a ninth rescinds the fifth through eighth. This logic determines which marriages can be ratified.
Each new marriage after a block of four is considered a rescission of the previous block.
3
Note the condition of consummation
In the slave case, if the slave consummated any of the marriages, the rescission effect is blocked, and ratification cannot validate any marriage.
Consummation means the marriages were valid at the time, so proceeding to a third does not rescind the first two.
4
Apply the rules to the slave case
Without consummation, the third marriage can be ratified because the act of marrying the third rescinds the first two. With consummation, no marriage can be ratified.
5
Incorporate the knowledge requirement
Al-Maqdisi adds that the rescission effect assumes the person was aware of the ruling; in times of widespread ignorance, the intent to rescind may not be present.
This is a practical consideration for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التجنيس : حر تزوج عشر نسوة بغير إذنهن فبلغهن الخبر فأجزن جميعاً جاز نكاح التاسعة والعاشرة لأنه لما تزوج الخامسة كان رد النكاح الأربع ، فلما تزوج التاسعة كان رد النكاح الأربع الأخر فبقي نكاح التاسعة والعاشرة موقوفاً على إجازتهما اهـ. وفي الخانية : عبد تزوج امرأة بغير إذن المولى ثم امرأة ثم امرأة فبلغ المولى فأجاز الكل، فإن لم يكن دخل بهن جاز نكاح الثالثة لأن الإقدام على نكاح الثالثة فسخ لنكاح الأولى والثانية فيتوقف نكاح الثالثة فينفذ بإجازة المولى، وإن كان دخل بهن لا يصح نكاحهن لأن الإقدام على نكاح الثالثة عدة الأولى والثانية لم يصح فلم يكن فسخاً لما قبلها فلا تصح إجازة المولى كما لو تزوجهن في عدة واحدة .اهـ. وهذا يوجب تقييد ما في التجنيس أيضاً. وقوله «موقوف» أي على الإجازة فلو تزوج بغير إذن السيد ثم أذن السيد لا ينفذ لأن الإذن ليس بإجازة فلا بد من إجازة العبد في فقد يخطب الشخص لينظر ما يجاب به وما يشترط عليه وما يطلب منه قوله (لما عرف في التبيين) حيث قال لأن كفالته جائزة في حق نفسه نافذة عليه لأنها التزام المال في الذمة وذمته مملوكة له قابلة للإلزام وإنما لا يظهر في الحال لحق المولى، فإذا زال المانع بالعتق ظهر موجبه، وأما التوكيل والوصية فالإجازة فيهما إنشاء لأنهما ينعقدان بلفظ الإجازة والإنشاء لا يستدعى عقداً سابقاً قوله (ولو وجد قبلها) أي لو وجد الشرط قبل الإجازة لم تطلق عندها أي عند الإجازة إلا إذا وجد الشرط ثانياً بعد الإجازة قوله (لأن الأقدام على نكاح الثالثة فسخ الخ) قال المقدسي فيما نقل عنه : ينبغي تقييده بما إذا كان عالماً بالحكم وإلا ففي هذا الزمان الذي غلب فيه الجهل ربما لا يقصد بالثالثة إبطال الأولين وكذا ما قبله اهـ ومثله في الرمز قال ولا سيما أن مالكاً يجيز الأربع للعبد وقد عذرت الأمة بالجهل لاشتغالها بالخدمة .
In al-Tajnis: A free man married ten women without their permission, then the news reached them and they all ratified; the marriage of the ninth and tenth is valid because when he married the fifth, it constituted a revocation of the first four, and when he married the ninth, it was a revocation of the other four, so the marriages of the ninth and tenth remain suspended on their ratification. And in al-Khaniyya: A slave married a woman without the master's permission, then another woman, then another woman; the master was informed and ratified all. If he had not consummated with them, the marriage of the third is valid because proceeding to the third marriage is a rescission of the first and second, so the third marriage is suspended and executed by the master's ratification. If he had consummated with them, their marriages are not valid because proceeding to the third marriage while the first and second are valid is not a rescission, so the master's ratification is not valid, as if he had married them within a single waiting period. This necessitates a restriction on what is in al-Tajnis as well. And his statement 'suspended (mawquf)' means suspended on ratification. So if he marries without the master's permission and then the master simply gives permission (idhn), it is not executed because permission is not ratification; the slave's ratification is required. For the phrase 'as known in al-Tabyin' where he said: because his kafala is valid in his own right and binding on him, as it is a financial obligation on his liability, and his liability is owned by him and capable of being obligated; it only does not appear immediately due to the master's right, so when the impediment is removed by emancipation, its effect appears. As for agency and will, ratification in them is an inception because they are concluded by the word of ratification and inception does not require a prior contract. His statement 'if it occurred before it' means if the condition occurred before ratification, she is not divorced upon ratification unless the condition occurs again after ratification. His statement 'because proceeding to the third marriage is a rescission...' – al-Maqdisi said: it should be restricted to when the person is aware of the ruling; otherwise in this time when ignorance prevails, perhaps by the third marriage he does not intend to invalidate the first two. Similarly in al-Ramz: he said especially since Malik permits four for a slave, and the slave woman is excused due to ignorance because of her preoccupation with service.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents two intricate cases from al-Tajnis and al-Khaniyya illustrating how a fuduli's multiple marriages are affected by ratification. In the first case, a free man marries ten women sequentially; upon ratification by the women, only the ninth and tenth survive because each successive marriage after four constitutes a revocation of the previous four. In the second case, a slave marries three women without his master's permission; if the master ratifies all, the third is valid only if no consummation preceded, because the act of marrying the third shows intent to rescind the earlier ones. But consummation invalidates that reasoning. The commentary then discusses the need for actual ratification (ijaza) as opposed to mere permission (idhn), and includes a note from al-Maqdisi adding a condition of knowledge of the ruling, especially in times of widespread ignorance.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; here meaning that each subsequent marriage implicitly rescinds the earlier ones.
عدة (idda): Waiting period; used here in the context of consummation affecting the validity of subsequent marriages.
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification; the act of giving consent to a contract made by a fuduli.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the slave consummated all marriages.
B) If the slave did not consummate any marriage.
C) If the slave consummated only the first.
D) If the master gave verbal permission.

Key Takeaway
The validity of multiple fuduli marriages upon ratification depends on the order of contracts and the presence of consummation, requiring careful application of the implied rescission rule.

Ratification and Revocation in Fuduli Marriage Contracts
Detailing ratification methods and revocation rights of fuduli vs agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a fuduli and an agent in marriage regarding the power to revoke the contract and apply the rule that ratification can occur by words or actions.

Core Idea
A fuduli in marriage cannot revoke because he bears no liability; an agent can revoke to fulfill the principal's intent.

In Hanafi fiqh, a contract made by a fuduli (unauthorized agent) is suspended pending ratification. This lesson explores how ratification occurs and the critical distinction between a fuduli and a proper agent (wakil) when it comes to revocation. The core principle is that absence of personal liability (uhda) in marriage prevents the fuduli from revoking, whereas the agent can revoke to achieve the principal's goal.

Guided Path
1
Identify ratification methods
From the passage, list the words and actions that constitute ratification of a fuduli marriage. Words include 'I ratify', 'well done', etc.; actions include accepting the dowry.
Note the exception: saying 'divorce her' is ratification but only when not said by a master to his slave.
2
Understand the general rule for fuduli
The fuduli in marriage cannot retract his contract before ratification. This is because, unlike in sale, there is no personal liability (uhda) to escape from.
This rule is derived from al-Zahiriyya and is the relied-upon mufta bihi position.
3
Contrast with the agent's power
An agent in a suspended marriage can revoke by word or deed. The agent's revocation is valid to realize the principal's intention, even though he also has no liability.
The agent can revoke by marrying the principal to another woman (deed) or by verbal rescission.
4
Analyze the exception for fuduli becoming agent
If a fuduli later becomes an agent, he gains the power to revoke by deed (e.g., marrying the principal to a sister), but not by word. This is due to the necessity of fulfilling the new agency.
This nuance is illustrated by the two scenarios given in the passage.
5
Apply to overlapping contracts
The principle is applied to cases where multiple marriages are contracted. The passage gives an example: a fuduli marrying a man to five women allows the man to choose four, but if the man himself married five, the fifth implicitly revokes the previous four.
This distinction hinges on whether the contractor has the power to revoke explicitly or implicitly.

العاقد وإن صدر العقد منه كما في التجنيس. وتثبت الإجازة لنكاح الفضولي بالقول والفعل؛ فمن الأول «أجزت ونحوه، وكذا نعم ما صنعت وبارك الله لنا» و«أحسنت» و«أصبت» و«طلقها» إلا إذا قال المولى لعبده كما سيأتي الظهيرية : والفضولي في باب النكاح لا يملك الرجوع قبل الإجازة والوكيل في النكاح الموقوف يملك الرجوع قولاً أو فعلاً بيانه رجل وكل رجلاً بأن يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأة بالغة بغير إذنها أوزوجها أبوها فلم يبلغها حتى نقض الوكيل النكاح قولاً أو فعلاً بأن يزوجه أختها صح ولو كان فضولياً، والمسألة بحالها لا يملك . وروي عن أبي يوسف في قوله الأول أن الفضولي يملك الرجوع أيضاً، والفضولي في باب البيع يملك الرجوع بالإجماع لأن الرجوع فرار عن العهدة في باب البيع بخلاف النكاح، وفي وجه الوكيل يملك الفسخ قولاً لا فعلاً بأن وكله بأن يزوجه امرأة بعينها فزوجها بغير رضاها ملك الوكيل نقضه قولاً لأنه وكيل فيه، ولا يملك نقضه فعلاً حتى لو زوجه أختها لا ينقض نكاح الأولى لأنه فضولي في نكاح الثانية، وفي وجه يملك الفسخ فعلاً لا قولاً نحو أن يوكل رجلاً بأن يزوجه فأجاز الوكيل نكاحاً باشره قبل ذلك صح استحساناً، ولا يملك نقض هذا النكاح قولاً لأنه كان فضولياً حين عقده، ويملك نقضه فعلاً بأن يزوجه أختها من غير رضاها لأنه وكيل في العقد الثاني اهـ. فحاصله أن كل عقد صدر من الفضولي في النكاح فإنه لا يملك نقضه قولاً ولا فعلاً لأنه لا عهدة عليه ليتخلص منها إلا إذا صار وكيلاً بعده فله نقضه فعلاً لضرورة امتثال ما وكل فيه، وإنما ملك الوكيل في الموقوف الفسخ مع أنه لا عهدة عليه أيضاً لتنجيز مراد الموكل فإنه لم يحصل مقصوده بالموقوف، فللوكيل الانتقال عنه إلى غيره وإنما لم يجز له الفسخ فعلاً في المسألة الثانية لأن الموكل بتزوجها معينة فحيث زوجها له انتهت وكالته فلم يملك تزويجاً آخر، ولذا كان فضولياً في الثاني. وتفرع على الأصل المذكور ما لو زوج فضولي رجل خمس نسوة في عقد متفرقة فللزوج أن يختار أربعاً منهن ويفارق الأخرى بخلاف ما لو تزوج الرجل خمس نسوة في عقد متفرقة بغير رضاهن لأن إقدامه على نكاح الخامسة يتضمن نقض نكاح
